Quiz Attempt #119757

Total Questions: 44
Question 1
Summarising and interpreting primary studies related to the identified research question or objective in a qualitative manner is called: (UGC NET 05 Jan Evening 2022)
  • A.Qualitative review
  • B.Realistic review
  • C.Narrative review
  • D.Meta review
Correct Answer: Narrative review

The process of summarizing and interpreting primary studies related to the identified research question or objective in a qualitative manner is called a "Narrative review." In a narrative review, the researcher synthesizes and presents the findings from various primary studies in a narrative format without using statistical techniques or formal meta-analysis. This type of review is particularly common in qualitative research, where the focus is on exploring and understanding the themes, patterns, and insights from the included studies in a descriptive and comprehensive way.

Question 2
Sets of principles that describe and predict events are known as: (UGC NET 13 Mar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Hypotheses
  • B.Concepts
  • C.Analyses
  • D.Theories
Correct Answer: Theories

Theories are systematic and organized sets of principles or statements that explain, describe, and predict phenomena or events in a particular field of study. They are used to understand and provide explanations for observed patterns, relationships, and behaviors in various disciplines, including the sciences, social sciences, and humanities. Theories serve as frameworks for guiding research, making predictions, and advancing knowledge.

Question 3
Arrange the following research components in correct sequence: (UGC NET 21 Mar 2023 Evening)A. Preparing a research planB. Collecting DataC. Drawing conclusionD. Formulating a research question/objectiveE. Analyzing dataChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, D, B, E, C
  • B.D, A, B, E, C
  • C.B, D, A, C, E
  • D.A, B, D, C, E
Correct Answer: D, A, B, E, C

1. Formulating a research question/objective: The research process typically begins with defining the research question or objective, which sets the direction for the study.

2. Preparing a research plan: Once you have a clear research question, you can create a research plan outlining how you will conduct the study, including the methodology, data collection techniques, and analysis methods.

3. Collecting Data: With the research plan in place, you can proceed to collect data according to your chosen methodology.

4. Analyzing data: After collecting the data, you analyze it to draw meaningful insights and conclusions from the information you've gathered.

5. Drawing conclusions: Finally, based on the data analysis, you draw conclusions and discuss the findings in the context of your research question or objective.

Question 4
Which of the following are the steps in systematic review of literature? (UGC NET 21 Mar 2023 Morning)A. Search for archival recordsB. Define the purposeC. Assess the relevance of selected studiesD. Identify the quality of each studyE. Interview the authors of each study selectedChoose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B and C only
  • B.B, C and D only
  • C.C, D and E only
  • D.A, B and E only
Correct Answer: B, C and D only

The steps in a systematic review of literature typically include:

1. Define the purpose: Clearly define the research question or objective of the systematic review.

2. Assess the relevance of selected studies: Evaluate the relevance of identified studies to the research question, often through a screening process.

3. Identify the quality of each study: Assess the quality of each included study, usually through a systematic appraisal of study design, methodology, and potential biases.

Question 5
The process of deduction in research has the following steps. Which are they? (UGC NET 06 Mar 2023 Evening)A. Photo-copying the research materialB. TheoryC. Hypothesis and data collectionD. Data analysis, findings, confirmation, or rejection of hypothesisE. Preparing the indexChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B and C only
  • B.B, C and D only
  • C.C, D and E only
  • D.B, D and E only
Correct Answer: B, C and D only

The correct steps in the process of deduction in research are typically:

a. Theory: Developing a theoretical framework that guides the research.

b. Hypothesis and data collection: Formulating hypotheses based on the theory and collecting data to test these hypotheses.

c. Data analysis, findings, confirmation, or rejection of the hypothesis: Analyzing the collected data, drawing conclusions, and confirming or rejecting the hypotheses.

Question 6
Identify the correct order of following steps in a research process: (UGC NET 04 Mar 2023 Evening)A. Review of LiteratureB. Formulation of HypothesisC. Defining the Research ProblemD. Collection of dataE. Preparing the research designChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B, C, D, E
  • B.B, C, A, E, D
  • C.C, A, B, E, D
  • D.B, C, A, D, E
Correct Answer: C, A, B, E, D

1. Defining the Research Problem: The research process typically begins with identifying and defining a specific research problem or question. This step involves clarifying what you want to investigate and why it's important.

2. Review of Literature: After defining the research problem, researchers conduct a thorough review of the existing literature related to the topic. This involves studying previous research, theories, and studies relevant to the problem to understand the current state of knowledge.

3. Formulation of Hypothesis: Based on the insights gained from the literature review, researchers formulate hypotheses or research questions. These hypotheses represent educated guesses or predictions about the expected outcomes of the research.

4. Preparing the Research Design: Once the research problem is defined, and hypotheses are formulated, researchers plan the research design. This step involves deciding on the research methods, data collection techniques, and overall strategy for conducting the study.

5. Collection of Data: With the research design in place, researchers collect data by implementing the chosen research methods. Data collection involves gathering information from participants or sources, which will be used to test the hypotheses or answer the research questions.

Question 7
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 05 Jan Morning 2022)Statement I:A Systematic review can be described as a ‘replicable and scientific’ process.Statement II:A transparent review may help us in minimizing personal and other biases.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Statement I: "A Systematic review can be described as a ‘replicable and scientific’ process." This statement is true. A systematic review is a research method used to collect, evaluate, and synthesize all available evidence on a specific research question in a rigorous, transparent, and systematic manner. It follows a predefined and replicable protocol, ensuring that the review process can be replicated by others to verify the findings.

 

Statement II: "A transparent review may help us in minimizing personal and other biases." This statement is also true. Transparency in the review process means that all steps, methods, and decisions taken during the review are clearly reported and made publicly available. This openness helps identify potential biases that may influence the review's findings and allows others to assess the reliability and validity of the review's conclusions. By being transparent, researchers can reduce the risk of personal biases influencing the review process.

Question 8
The objective of exploring the existing literature should be to identify which of the following issues? (UGC NET 01 Dec Evening 2021)a. What is already known about this area?b. What concepts and theories are relevant to this area?c. How to get funding for the research?d. What are the significant controversies in this area?e. Are there any inconsistencies in the findings of this area?Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, c and d only
  • B.b, c, d and e only
  • C.a, b, d and e only
  • D.a, b, c and e only
Correct Answer: a, b, d and e only

(a) "What is already known about this area?" - Exploring the existing literature helps researchers understand the current state of knowledge on a particular topic or research area. This knowledge provides a foundation for building upon previous findings and identifying gaps in the literature.

 

(b) "What concepts and theories are relevant to this area?" - The existing literature contains various concepts and theoretical frameworks related to the research area. Identifying these concepts and theories helps researchers develop a theoretical framework for their study and understand the broader context of their research.

 

(c) "What are the significant controversies in this area?" - By reviewing the existing literature, researchers can identify areas of disagreement or controversies in the field. Understanding these controversies helps guide the direction of the research and may lead to new research questions or hypotheses.

 

(d) "Are there any inconsistencies in the findings of this area?" - Exploring the existing literature allows researchers to assess the consistency of findings across different studies. Identifying inconsistencies can highlight potential limitations in previous research and areas that need further investigation.ifferent studies. Identifying inconsistencies can highlight potential limitations in previous research and areas that need further investigation.

Question 9
A systematic review of literature adopts: (UGC NET 29 Oct 2022 Evening)
  • A.Explicit procedure
  • B.Implicit procedures
  • C.Personal-choice
  • D.Peer-suggested procedures
Correct Answer: Explicit procedure

A systematic review of literature adopts an explicit procedure. This means that it follows a structured and well-defined methodology to identify, select, appraise, and synthesize all relevant studies on a specific research question or topic. The process is systematic and transparent, aiming to minimize bias and subjectivity.

 

In a systematic review, the researchers outline the inclusion and exclusion criteria, search strategies, data extraction methods, and methods for assessing the quality of included studies. This explicit procedure allows others to replicate the review and ensures the review is rigorous and reliable.

Question 10
The purpose of review of literature includes: (UGC NET 19 Dec 2018 Evening)(a) To understand the subject background(b) To formulate research questions(c) To find out relevant methodology(d) To debate the ethical aspects of research(e) To carry out meta-analysis of bibliography(f) To identify the data sources
  • A.(b), (c), (d) and (e)
  • B.(a), (b), (c) and (f)
  • C.(c), (d), (e) and (f)
  • D.(a), (b), (c) and (e)
Correct Answer: (a), (b), (c) and (f)

The review of literature aims to gain a comprehensive understanding of existing research and discussions relevant to a specific topic or area of study. By conducting a literature review, researchers can enhance their knowledge in their field of study. It allows them to learn about essential concepts, research methods, and experimental techniques applied in their field. Additionally, researchers gain insights into how these concepts are practically applied to real-world problems.

Question 11
Which of the following phrases is not relevant to describe the meaning of research as a process? (UGC NET Dec 2010)
  • A.Systematic Activity
  • B.Objective Observation
  • C.Trial and Error
  • D.Problem Solving
Correct Answer: Objective Observation

The research process involves systematic activity, which refers to a step-by-step progression of work where each step depends on the previous one. It requires identifying, locating, assessing, and analyzing the information needed to support the research question. Additionally, the research process involves trial and error to refine and improve the approach as well as problem-solving to address any challenges or obstacles encountered during the research.

 

However, the phrase "Objective Observation" does not directly describe the process of research. While observation can be a part of the research process, the term "objective" implies an unbiased and neutral perspective, which may not always be the case in research. Research involves not only objective observations but also subjective interpretations and analyses, depending on the nature of the study and the researcher's approach.

Question 12
Given below are stages of research process. Arrange these in the correct sequence of carrying them out: (UGC NET 24 Dec Evening 2021)a. Sampling casesb. Research questionc. Literature reviewd. Data collectione. Data analysisChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.c, b, a, d, e
  • B.a, c, b, d, e
  • C.c, a, d, b, e
  • D.b, d, e, a, c
Correct Answer: c, b, a, d, e

The correct sequence of carrying out the stages of the research process is as follows:

1. Literature review: This is the initial stage where you review existing literature and research on the topic to understand what has already been studied and what gaps exist in the current knowledge.

 

2. Research question: After conducting the literature review, you can formulate your research question or hypothesis based on the gaps identified and the specific area you want to study.

 

3. Sampling cases: Once you have formulated your research question, you can proceed to select the appropriate sampling cases or participants for your study. This step involves defining your target population and selecting a representative sample from it.

 

4. Data collection: With the sample selected, you can now collect the data for your study. This step involves gathering information and data from the selected sample through various methods such as surveys, interviews, observations, etc.

 

5. Data analysis: After collecting the data, you need to analyze it to draw meaningful conclusions and answer your research question. Data analysis involves applying appropriate statistical or qualitative techniques to make sense of the data and test any hypotheses you may have.

Question 13
14.)According to Kerlinger (1973), good research problem should be: (UGC NET 27 Nov Morning 2021)a. Describing the relationship between two or more variables.b. Articulated intelligently.c. Philosophically oriented.d. In the form of a question.e. Amenable to empirical testing.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b and e only
  • B.a, d and e only
  • C.b, c and e only
  • D.b, d and e only
Correct Answer: a, d and e only

According to Kerlinger (1973), a good research problem should have the following characteristics:

a. Describing the relationship between two or more variables: The research problem should involve investigating the connection or association between two or more variables. This suggests that the study should have a clear focus on understanding how variables interact with each other.

 

b. In the form of a question: A well-defined research problem should be stated in the form of a question. This helps to articulate what the study aims to investigate and what specific information the researcher is seeking.

 

c. Amenable to empirical testing: The research problem should be something that can be tested and investigated using empirical evidence. This means that the problem should be capable of being observed, measured, or analyzed in a systematic and scientific manner.

Question 14
When a reviewer reviews a research article without knowing the author’s name, it is referred to as: (UGC NET 20 Dec 2018 Morning)
  • A.Anonymous review
  • B.Behind-the-curtain review
  • C.Uncategorized review
  • D.Blind review
Correct Answer: Blind review

When a reviewer reviews a research article without knowing the author's name, it is referred to as blind review. In blind review, the identity of the author is kept confidential from the reviewers to ensure unbiased evaluation of the research article.

 

There are various types of peer review processes, including single blind review and double blind review. In single blind review, the author does not know the reviewers' identities, while in double blind review, both the reviewers and the authors are unaware of each other's identities. This practice is common among science journals.

 

Other types of peer review processes include open peer review, where the identity of the author and reviewers is known to all participants, and transparent peer review, which openly publishes the entire peer review process for transparency and recognition of the reviewers' work.

 

Additionally, there are collaborative review approaches where a team of reviewers work together to assess a paper, and post-publication review, where appraisal and revision of a published paper continue or occur after its publication, often through comments or discussions alongside the paper.

Question 15
A good review of research literature aims at: (UGC NET 20 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Subjective analysis of the content.
  • B.Provides information about the authors and their affiliations.
  • C.Generates research questions and validating those questions.
  • D.Conducts multiple task-based screening.
Correct Answer: Generates research questions and validating those questions.

A good review of research literature aims to achieve the following:

  • 1. Conduct a comprehensive survey of the relevant literature in a specific field of research.
  • 2. Synthesize the information found in the literature into a concise and informative summary.
  • 3. Critically analyze the gathered information by identifying gaps in the current knowledge, highlighting limitations of existing theories and viewpoints, and formulating research questions to address these gaps.
  • 4. Present the reviewed literature in a well-organized manner, facilitating a clear understanding of the subject.

 

In essence, a literature review not only illuminates the evolution of knowledge within the field but also showcases what has been accomplished, what is widely accepted, what is emerging, and the current state of thinking on the topic. Additionally, in research-based texts like a Doctoral thesis, a literature review plays a vital role in identifying areas that remain unexplored or under-researched, known as research gaps, and explaining how the proposed research project aims to contribute to filling these gaps. By achieving these objectives, a well-executed literature review lays the foundation for sound research, generating relevant research questions and providing validation for those questions.

Question 16
Which of the following are VALID reasons for 'Literature Review' in research? (UGC NET 20 Oct2022Morning)a. It shows the present status of knowledge in the field of research so that the significance of the proposed research question is clear.b. It gives a correct context to the scope of the work proposed in the thesis.c. It demonstrates the scholarliness of the thesis writer.d. It fills the minimum page requirement for a thesis.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a and b only
  • B.c and d only
  • C.a and c only
  • D.b and d only
Correct Answer: a and b only

Valid reasons for conducting a literature review in research include:

a. It shows the present status of knowledge in the field of research so that the significance of the proposed research question is clear: A literature review helps researchers understand what has already been studied and what gaps exist in the current knowledge. By reviewing the existing literature, the significance of the research question or problem being addressed in the study becomes apparent.

 

b. It gives a correct context to the scope of the work proposed in the thesis: A literature review provides the context for the research and helps to define the scope and boundaries of the study. It helps the readers understand the background and rationale for the research, making the study more meaningful and relevant.

Question 17
A research problem is feasible only when: (UGC NET Jun 2007)
  • A.it has utility and relevance
  • B.it is researchable
  • C.it is new and adds something to knowledge
  • D.all the above
Correct Answer: it is researchable

A research problem is considered feasible when it is researchable. Feasibility in this context means that the research problem can be effectively studied and investigated using appropriate research methods and approaches.

 

The feasibility of a research problem is determined by its suitability for empirical investigation. Researchers need to assess whether they have access to the necessary resources, data, and expertise to address the research problem successfully.

Question 18
The originality of a research topic will depend upon factors of: (UGC NET 21 Dec 2018 Morning)(a) Uniqueness of the topic(b) Utilitarian dimensions(c) Support system(d) Non-requirement of supervision(e) Feasibility of the study
  • A.(a), (b), (c) and (d)
  • B.(a), (b), (d) and (e)
  • C.(b), (c), (d) and (e)
  • D.(a), (b), (c) and (e)
Correct Answer: (a), (b), (c) and (e)

The originality of a research topic is determined by several crucial factors:

(i) Uniqueness of the topic: An original research topic should address a specific research gap or explore a novel area of study, contributing new insights to the existing body of knowledge.

 

(ii) Utilitarian dimensions: The research topic should have practical relevance and potential implications in real-world contexts, making it useful and beneficial to society, industry, or academia.

 

(iii) Support system: A research topic's originality can be influenced by the availability of adequate resources, funding, access to data, and necessary facilities to conduct the study effectively.

 

(iv) Feasibility of the study: The research topic should be feasible and manageable within the available time, resources, and expertise, ensuring that the research can be conducted successfully.

Question 19
The identification of a research problem involves: (UGC NET 21 Dec 2018 Morning)(a) Selection of the academic area(b) Demarcation of the study area(c) Rejection of personal and collective choices(d) Specific topics within the area(e) Management of financial sourcesOptions:
  • A.(a), (b) and (c)
  • B.(a), (b) and (d)
  • C.(b), (c) and (d)
  • D.(c), (d) and (e)
Correct Answer: (a), (b) and (d)

The identification of a research problem involves the following steps:

(i) Identify the Broad Study Area: This step involves selecting the field in which the researcher intends to work, exploring areas of concern or interest.

 

(ii) Dissect the Broad Study Area into Subareas: The researcher breaks down the broad study area into more specific and manageable subareas for focused investigation.

 

(iii) Mark-up Your Interest: From the subareas, the researcher identifies and highlights their specific area of interest or passion.

 

(iv) Study Research Questions: The researcher formulates clear and specific research questions that need to be addressed within their area of interest.

 

(v) Set Out Objectives: The researcher sets clear objectives, both primary and sub-objectives, that outline the purpose and goals of the research.

 

(vi) Assess Your Objectives: This step involves evaluating the feasibility and achievability of the identified research objectives.

 

(vii) Check Back: Before proceeding with the actual research work, the researcher reviews all the steps taken in formulating the research problem, ensuring they are on the right track.

Question 20
Formulation of a research problem depends upon: (UGC NET 22 Dec 2018 Morning)(a) What is the object behind the researcher’s choice?(b) What are the specific questions?(c) What is the conceptual model?(d) What negative factors to research upon?(e) Reasons for unlimiting the study.(f) Construction of hypotheses.Options:
  • A.(c), (d), (e) and (f)
  • B.(a), (b), (c) and (f)
  • C.(b), (c), (d) and (e)
  • D.(a), (c), (e) and (f)
Correct Answer: (a), (b), (c) and (f)

The process of formulating a research problem involves considering various aspects:

(a) The researcher needs to define the objective or purpose behind choosing a particular research problem, which helps in identifying the underlying motivation or intention.

 

(b) Specific questions related to the research problem need to be articulated. These questions guide the research and help in narrowing down the scope of the study.

 

(c) A conceptual model provides a theoretical framework that helps in organizing ideas, concepts, and variables related to the research problem.

 

(d) Constructing hypotheses involves proposing specific statements or predictions that can be tested during the research process. Hypotheses provide a direction for the study and serve as a basis for data analysis and interpretation

Question 21
Which stage in research creates a working thesis for the research paper by specifying and organizing the category of information? (UGC NET 21 Jun 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Research design
  • B.Developing a hypothesis
  • C.Review of literature
  • D.Analysis of data
Correct Answer: Review of literature

The stage in research that involves creating a working thesis for the research paper by specifying and organizing the category of information is known as the "Review of literature." During this stage, a literature review is conducted to identify, evaluate, and synthesize relevant literature within a specific research field. The literature review sheds light on the evolution of knowledge in the field, showcasing what has been previously explored, what is widely accepted, what is currently emerging, and the current state of thinking on the topic.

 

Moreover, the literature review serves the purpose of identifying any research gaps—areas that have not been explored or are under-researched—and articulating how the proposed research project addresses these gaps.

 

The primary objectives of a literature review are:

  • 1. Surveying the existing literature in the chosen area of study.
  • 2. Summarizing and synthesizing the information found in the literature.
  • 3. Critically analyzing the gathered information by identifying knowledge gaps, highlighting limitations of theories and perspectives, and suggesting areas for further research or reviewing controversial topics.
  • 4. Presenting the literature in a well-organized manner to facilitate understanding and provide a foundation for the working thesis of the research paper.
Question 22
The formulation of a research problem can be compared to: (UGC NET 24 June 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Laying the foundation of a building.
  • B.Building the walls of a home.
  • C.Polishing the doors of a building.
  • D.Constructing the ceiling of a house.
Correct Answer: Laying the foundation of a building.

Just as laying the foundation is the initial step in constructing a building, the formulation of a research problem is the first crucial step in the research process. It sets the direction and provides a clear purpose for the entire study.

 

When researchers embark on a new study, they need to identify and define a specific research problem or question that they aim to address through their research. This problem is the focal point of the study and guides all subsequent decisions, including the research design, data collection methods, analysis, and interpretation of results.

 

The process of formulating a research problem involves identifying a gap in existing knowledge, recognizing an issue or challenge that requires investigation, or exploring a topic that warrants further exploration. Researchers need to clearly articulate the problem, ensuring that it is relevant, feasible, and can be adequately addressed within the scope of the study.

Question 23
After identifying the different variables and establishing the logical reasoning in theoretical framework, the next step in the research process is to (UGC NET 21 Jun 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Conduct survey
  • B.Generate hypothesis
  • C.Focus on group discussion
  • D.Use experiment in an investigation
Correct Answer: Generate hypothesis

After identifying the different variables and establishing the logical reasoning in the theoretical framework, the next step in the research process is to generate a hypothesis. A hypothesis is a tentative assumption made to draw out and test its logical or empirical consequences. It serves as a guiding proposition that sharpens the researcher's thinking and focuses attention on the important facets of the problem.

 

The research process involves several stages, starting with formulating the research problem and conducting an extensive literature survey to gain familiarity with the selected problem. The researcher then develops a working hypothesis based on the literature review, stating it in clear terms. This hypothesis helps delimit the area of research and determines the type of data required and methods of data analysis to be used.

 

After preparing the research design and determining the sample design, the researcher collects the relevant data through various methods. Once the data have been collected, they are analyzed through coding, tabulation, and statistical inference. Hypothesis testing is performed to assess whether the facts support or contradict the formulated hypotheses, using statistical tests like Chi-square, t-test, or F-test.

 

Based on the results and analysis, the researcher may arrive at generalizations or build a theory. Interpretation of findings may lead to new research questions and further investigations. Finally, the researcher prepares a report or thesis summarizing the entire research process, including the hypothesis, methodology, data analysis, and conclusions.

Question 24
In which of the following steps of research, the scope for creativity and imagination is utmost? (UGC NET 06 Dec 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Identifying the research problem and defining it
  • B.Figuring out the related studies and the techniques used by other researchers
  • C.Identifying variables and hypothesizing
  • D.Data analysis and presentation of results
Correct Answer: Identifying variables and hypothesizing

While a researcher cannot simply create a problem for the sake of studying it, there is significant room for creativity and imagination when it comes to identifying the variables to be studied and determining the specific aspects the research will target. This process directly contributes to the formulation of hypotheses for the research problem and shapes the researcher's perspective and approach to address the issue at hand.

Question 25
Which of the following sequences represents the most logical sequence in doing research? (UGC NET 03 Dec 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Identifying and defining a research problem, formulating a hypothesis, testing of hypothesis and reporting the results
  • B.Identify a research problem, defining the population and sample, collecting data and analysis of data
  • C.Survey of research, defining the research problem, collecting data and presenting the outcomes
  • D.Defining research variables, hypothesizing, testing of research and reporting of research outcomes
Correct Answer: Identifying and defining a research problem, formulating a hypothesis, testing of hypothesis and reporting the results

The sequence in doing research is as follows:

1. Perceive a broad problem.

2. Read literature on relevant theoretical and empirical work to narrow down the problem.

3. Discuss with peers and tutors to define a researchable problem.

4. Define the context of the problem to be researched.

5. Review any comparable case studies, especially for research questions and methodology.

6. Frame research questions.

7. Design an investigative procedure.

8. Select and retrieve appropriate data.

9. Proceed with analysis and interpretation.

10. Compare your findings and interpretations with other relevant studies reviewed earlier.

11. Draw tentative conclusions for your research questions or hypotheses.

 

This logical sequence starts with identifying a broad problem, then progressively narrows it down by reviewing existing literature and engaging in discussions with peers and tutors. It moves on to defining the research questions, designing the research methodology, collecting and analyzing data, and finally drawing conclusions based on the findings. Following this sequence helps ensure a systematic and well-structured research process.

Question 26
Match List I with List II (UGC NET 24 Sept 2020 Evening paper)List I (Key research terms)A. Research problemsB. Research hypothesisC. Sample of studyD. Research toolsList II (Description)I. Devices using which data are gatheredII. A subset drawn from a defined set or universeIII. A tentative solution or answer to a research questionIV. The research question which has to be answeredChoose the correct answer from the options given below
  • A.A - IV, B - III, C - II, D - I
  • B.A - III, B - II, C - I, D - IV
  • C.A - I, B - II, C- III, D - IV
  • D.A - III, B - IV, C - I, D – II
Correct Answer: A - IV, B - III, C - II, D - I

a. Research problems are the specific questions or issues that researchers seek to address through their study. They represent the research questions that need to be answered to fulfill the objectives of the research.

 

b. Research hypothesis is a tentative statement or educated guess about the relationship between variables or the expected outcomes of the research study. It provides a potential solution or answer to the research question.

 

c. Sample of study refers to a subset of the defined set or population from which data are collected. Researchers select a sample to gather information that represents the larger population in a manageable way.

 

d. Research tools are the devices or instruments used by researchers to gather data. These tools can include surveys, questionnaires, interviews, observations, or any other method used to collect information relevant to the research study.

Question 27
In establishing a research problem for a Ph. D level course, in the initial stage which of the following stages are crucial? (UGC NET 17 Oct 2020 Evening paper)I. Hypothesis testingII. Locating a problem area from a field through survey of related literatureIII. Defining the population of research and its characteristicsIV. Selecting a pointed issue called a problem by a process of logical analysisV. Defining and delimiting the problemChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.II, IV, V only
  • B.II, III, IV only
  • C.I, II, III only
  • D.III, IV, V only
Correct Answer: III, IV, V only

In the initial stage of establishing a research problem for a Ph.D. level course, the crucial stages are as follows:

1. Defining the population of research and its characteristics: This stage involves identifying the specific group or population that the research will focus on and understanding the characteristics of that population. Defining the population helps in ensuring the research is targeted and relevant.

 

2. Selecting a pointed issue called a problem by a process of logical analysis: At this stage, the researcher identifies a specific and well-defined research problem by analyzing various issues and logically narrowing down to the most relevant and feasible problem to study.

 

3. Defining and delimiting the problem: Defining the research problem clearly and precisely is essential. Additionally, delimiting the problem involves setting boundaries and specifying the scope of the study to ensure the research remains focused and manageable.

Question 28
Arrange the following steps of research in correct sequence: (UGC NET Dec 2012)1. Identification of research problem2. Listing of research objectives3. Collection of data4. Methodology5. Data analysis6. Results and discussion
  • A.1 – 2 – 3 – 4 – 5 – 6
  • B.1 – 2 – 4 – 3 – 5 – 6
  • C.2 – 1 – 3 – 4 – 5 – 6
  • D.2 – 1 – 4 – 3 – 5 – 6
Correct Answer: 1 – 2 – 4 – 3 – 5 – 6

The steps of research, arranged in the correct sequence, are as follows:

  • 1. Identification of research problem: This step involves reviewing the existing literature, identifying variables, and formulating a research problem. It sets the foundation for the research study.
  • 2. Listing of research objectives: Once the research problem is defined, specific research objectives are formulated. These objectives outline what the researcher aims to achieve through the study.
  • 3. Methodology: This step involves selecting the appropriate research design that aligns with the research objectives. The research design outlines the overall plan for conducting the study.
  • 4. Collection of data: In this step, data is collected based on the chosen research design and methodology. Various methods of data collection may be employed, such as surveys, interviews, or observations.
  • 5. Data analysis: After data collection, the gathered information is analyzed to draw meaningful conclusions. This involves editing, coding, and analyzing the data to identify patterns, trends, or relationships.
  • 6. Results and discussion: The analyzed data is presented in this step, accompanied by a discussion of the findings. The researcher interprets the results and relates them to the research objectives.
Question 29
Which sequence of research steps is logical in the list given below? (UGC NET Jan 2017)
  • A.Problem formulation, Analysis, Development of Research design, Hypothesis making, Collection of data, Arriving at generalizations and conclusions.
  • B.Development of Research design, Hypothesis making, Problem formulation, Data analysis, Arriving at conclusions and data collection.
  • C.Problem formulation, Hypothesis making, Development of a Research design, Collection of data, Data analysis and formulation of generalizations and conclusions.
  • D.Problem formulation, Deciding about the sample and data collection tools, Formulation of hypothesis, Collection and interpretation of research evidence.
Correct Answer: Problem formulation, Hypothesis making, Development of a Research design, Collection of data, Data analysis and formulation of generalizations and conclusions.

The logical sequence of research steps is as follows:

  • 1. Problem formulation: This is the initial step, which involves reviewing existing literature, identifying variables, constructing hypotheses, and formulating research objectives.
  • 2. Hypothesis making: Once the research problem is defined, specific hypotheses are formulated to test the relationship between variables.
  • 3. Development of a Research design: In this step, a suitable research design is chosen, which outlines the overall plan for conducting the study.
  • 4. Collection of data: Data is collected based on the chosen research design and methodology. This step involves selecting appropriate data collection methods, such as surveys, interviews, or observations.
  • 5. Data analysis: After data collection, the gathered information is analyzed to draw meaningful conclusions. Data editing, coding, analysis, and interpretation are performed to identify patterns, trends, or relationships.
  • 6. Formulation of generalizations and conclusions: The analyzed data is used to draw generalizations and arrive at conclusions, which are then related back to the research objectives.
Question 30
Which of the following is the first step in starting the research process? (UGC NET Jun 2010)
  • A.Searching sources of information to locate problem.
  • B.Survey of related literature
  • C.Identification of problem
  • D.Searching for solutions to the problem
Correct Answer: Identification of problem

The first step in starting the research process is the "Identification of problem."

In the research process, the initial step involves identifying a research problem. This entails reviewing the existing literature, exploring various sources of information, and pinpointing a specific issue or topic that requires investigation. The research problem serves as the foundation for the entire research study and defines the scope and direction of the research. Once the problem is identified, the researcher can proceed to formulate research objectives, construct hypotheses, and design the research study accordingly.

Question 31
Ability to see and size up the situation creatively is most relevant at which stage of research? ? (UGC NET 18 Dec 2018 Morning)
  • A.In formulating research hypotheses and procedures for testing them.
  • B.At the stage of identifying and defining a research problem.
  • C.In deciding and identifying the sampling procedures to ensure their representative
  • D.character.
Correct Answer: At the stage of identifying and defining a research problem.

The ability to see and size up the situation creatively is most relevant at the stage of identifying and defining a research problem.

At this stage, researchers need to carefully assess and understand the research context, subject area, and the issues that need investigation. This requires creative thinking to identify gaps in existing knowledge, potential research questions, and areas where new insights can be gained. Researchers must be able to approach the problem from different angles, consider various perspectives, and think innovatively to formulate a clear and meaningful research problem.

 

Identifying and defining a research problem is a critical step as it lays the foundation for the entire research process. The way the problem is framed will influence the research design, data collection methods, and the overall direction of the study. Therefore, creative thinking and the ability to see the situation from different angles are crucial to ensure that the research problem is well-defined and relevant to address the research objectives effectively.

Question 32
Identify the CORRECT sequence of empirical steps in the linear model of the research process: (UGC NET 28 Nov Morning 2021)
  • A.Sampling → theory → interpretation → collection → validation → hypotheses
  • B.Theory → hypotheses → sampling → collection → interpretation → validation
  • C.Validation → theory → hypotheses → collection → sampling → interpretation
  • D.Collection → sampling → hypotheses → theory → interpretation → operationalization
Correct Answer: Theory → hypotheses → sampling → collection → interpretation → validation

The linear model of the research process involves several empirical steps that need to be followed in a logical sequence:

1. Theory: The research process typically begins with the development of a theoretical framework or a theory. The theory serves as a foundation for the research, providing a conceptual basis for formulating hypotheses and guiding the study.

 

2. Hypotheses: Based on the theory, specific research hypotheses are formulated. Hypotheses are testable statements that predict the relationship between variables or the expected outcomes of the study.

 

3. Sampling: After formulating hypotheses, researchers proceed to select a suitable sample from the target population. The sample should be representative of the population and allow generalization of the findings.

 

4. Collection: Once the sample is selected, data is collected from the participants using various methods such as surveys, interviews, observations, or experiments.

 

5. Interpretation: After data collection, the next step is to analyze and interpret the data. Data analysis involves using statistical or qualitative techniques to make sense of the data and test the hypotheses.

 

6. Validation: Finally, the findings and interpretations are validated, which involves assessing the reliability and validity of the research results. Validation ensures that the study's conclusions are supported by the data and that the research is sound and trustworthy.

Question 33
Identify the correct sequence of steps in the research process as identified by David Nachmias: (UGC NET 04 Dec Morning 2021)a. Research design.b. Data collection.c. Formulation of hypothesis.d. Data analysis and generalisation.e. Problem identification.Choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, c, d, e
  • B.b, c, d, e, a
  • C.c, d, e, a, b
  • D.e, c, a, b, d
Correct Answer: e, c, a, b, d

The correct sequence of steps in the research process as identified by David Nachmias is as follows:

1. Problem identification: The research process begins with identifying a research problem or topic of interest. This involves recognizing an area that needs further investigation or where gaps in knowledge exist.

 

2. Formulation of hypothesis: Once the research problem is identified, researchers develop specific research hypotheses or research questions to guide their study. Hypotheses are testable predictions about the relationship between variables.

 

3. Research design: After formulating hypotheses, researchers proceed to design the research study. Research design involves planning the overall approach, strategy, and methods that will be used to collect and analyze data.

 

4. Data collection: With the research design in place, researchers collect relevant data from the selected sample using various data collection methods such as surveys, experiments, interviews, or observations.

 

5. Data analysis and generalization: After data collection, researchers analyze the data using appropriate statistical or qualitative techniques. The results are then generalized to the larger population, drawing conclusions and implications from the findings.

Question 34
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 21 Nov 2021 Morning)List I (Research Steps)a. Defining a research problem.b. Hypothesis making.c. Drawing a research sample.d. Hypothesis testing.List II (Main features)i. Appropriate statistical techniques for data analysis.ii. Representativeness of the units chosen.iii. Identifying the variables for setting up a plausible relationship.iv. Carefully chosen terms and concepts with operational descriptions, if need be.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.a‐i, b‐ii, c‐iii, d‐iv
  • B.a‐ii, b‐i, c‐iv, d‐iii
  • C.a‐iii, b‐iv, c‐i, d‐ii
  • D.a‐iv, b‐iii, c‐ii, d‐i
Correct Answer: a‐iv, b‐iii, c‐ii, d‐i

a. Defining a research problem- When defining a research problem, researchers need to precisely and clearly articulate the key terms and concepts they will be investigating. Operational descriptions are essential when abstract concepts need to be measured or observed in a concrete manner, ensuring clarity and consistency in the study.

 

b. Hypothesis making- Hypothesis making involves formulating specific statements that predict the relationship between variables. Before creating hypotheses, researchers must identify the variables involved in the study and determine how they are related, setting up a plausible and testable relationship.

 

c. Drawing a research sample- When drawing a research sample, it is crucial to select participants or units that represent the larger population under study. A representative sample increases the generalizability of the findings and allows researchers to make inferences about the entire population.

 

d. Hypothesis testing- Hypothesis testing involves analyzing the collected data to determine whether the research hypotheses are supported or not. This requires the application of appropriate statistical techniques to draw meaningful conclusions from the data and assess the significance of the relationships between variables.

Question 35
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 03 Dec Morning 2021)List I (Research Steps)a. Research problem definition.b. Formulation of research hypothesis.c. Design of research.d. Data AnalysisList II (Characteristics)i. Appropriateness of techniques and their application.ii. Development of a conceptual framework which is in accord with hypothesis of research.iii. c. Design of research is influenced by both the research problem and the formulated hypotheses. It involves planning the overall approach and methods for data collection, ensuring they align with the research problem and are capable of testing the formulated hypotheses.

 

d. Data analysis is the culmination of the research process, where the collected data is examined and analyzed to draw meaningful conclusions, verify or reject the research hypotheses, and provide insights into the research problem.

Question 36
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 20 Nov Morning 2021)List I (Steps of research )a. Problem formulationb. Hypothesis makingc. Selecting a sampling procedured. Data AnalysisList II (Techniques used)i. Tabular and graphical representation of data.ii. Drawing a subset from a larger set.iii. Raising pivotal question in a field of enquiry.iv. Setting up relationship among variables of research.Choose the correct answer from the option given below:Codes
  • A.a‐iii, b‐iv, c‐ii, d‐i
  • B.a‐i, b‐ii, c‐iii, d‐iv
  • C.a‐ii, b‐iii, c‐i, d‐iv
  • D.a‐iii, b‐i, c‐ii, d‐iv
Correct Answer: a‐iii, b‐iv, c‐ii, d‐i

a. Problem formulation- When formulating a research problem, researchers identify significant questions that need to be addressed in a specific field of inquiry. These pivotal questions serve as the foundation for the research study and help focus the investigation.

 

b. Hypothesis making- Hypothesis making involves formulating specific statements that predict the relationship between variables in the study. Researchers set up relationships based on their theoretical understanding and prior knowledge to be tested through data analysis.

 

c. Selecting a sampling procedure- Selecting a sampling procedure involves choosing a subset (sample) from a larger group or population. The sample should be representative of the larger set to ensure the findings can be generalized to the entire population.

 

d. Data Analysis- Data analysis involves processing and interpreting the collected data to draw meaningful conclusions. Researchers often use tabular and graphical representation techniques to present data visually, making it easier to understand patterns, trends, and relationships.

Question 37
The exercise of reviewing the relevant literature is most closely related for which one of the following? (UGC NET 29 Nov Morning 2021)
  • A.Formulating research problems.
  • B.In drawing a sample for the study.
  • C.For analysing quantitative data.
  • D.Generalization of the finding.
Correct Answer: Formulating research problems.

The exercise of reviewing the relevant literature is most closely related to formulating research problems. When conducting a research study, it is essential to review the existing literature on the topic to understand what has already been studied, what gaps exist in the current knowledge, and what research questions or problems need to be addressed.

 

By reviewing the relevant literature, researchers can identify the key concepts, theories, and findings related to their topic of interest. This helps them refine and formulate research questions or hypotheses based on the gaps and knowledge deficits identified in the literature. It also ensures that the research study builds upon existing knowledge and contributes meaningfully to the field.

Question 38
A process in which scientific research and ideas are evaluated by experts of the field, is called (UGC NET 04 Mar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Literature Review
  • B.Conceptual Review
  • C.Peer Review
  • D.General Review
Correct Answer: Peer Review

Peer review is a process in which scientific research and ideas are evaluated by experts (peers) in the field. These experts assess the quality, validity, and significance of research papers or proposals submitted for publication or funding. Peer review helps ensure the credibility and quality of scientific work before it is published or funded, making it an essential component of the scientific research process

Question 39
A research paper evaluated by other experts either for publication or presentation at a conference is considered to have undergone: (UGC NET 05Mar 2023 Morning)
  • A.Peer Review
  • B.Public Review
  • C.Private Review
  • D.Research Review
Correct Answer: Peer Review

A research paper that is evaluated by other experts in the field for publication or presentation at a conference typically undergoes a process known as "Peer Review." In peer review, knowledgeable individuals (peers) assess the quality, validity, and significance of the research work before it is accepted for publication or presentation. This process helps ensure the credibility and quality of scientific and academic research.

Question 40
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 28 Mar 2023 Morning)Statement I:Debriefing invoices revealing the purposes of the research to the participants.Statement II:Debriefing of participants takes place at the beginning of a study.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect.
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.
Correct Answer: Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.

Statement I: This statement is correct. Debriefing in research is a process that occurs after the participants have completed their participation in a study. During debriefing, researchers typically provide participants with information about the true purpose and objectives of the research, especially if any deception was involved. This is done to ensure that participants are fully informed about the study's goals and to address any concerns or questions they may have.

 

Statement II: This statement is incorrect. Debriefing does not take place at the beginning of a study. Instead, it occurs after the study is completed, usually during the concluding phase, to provide participants with post-study information.

Question 41
Independent verification of a research effort is known as: (UGC NET Dec 2021)
  • A.Enquiry
  • B.Probe
  • C.Replication
  • D.Investigation
Correct Answer: Replication

In the context of research, replication refers to the process of conducting a study again, using the same methods and procedures as the original study, to see if the results can be reproduced or confirmed.

 

Replication is an essential aspect of the scientific method and is used to validate the findings of a study. When researchers replicate a study and obtain similar results, it adds credibility to the original findings and increases confidence in the reliability of the conclusions. On the other hand, if the replication study produces different results, it raises questions about the robustness of the original findings and may warrant further investigation.

Question 42
When a researcher is interested only in general indications, not in data collection for statistical tests, he may opt for: (UGC NET 21 Oct 2022 Morning)
  • A.Null hypothesis
  • B.Quantification of data.
  • C.Research questions
  • D.Research problems
Correct Answer: Research questions

Research questions are specific inquiries that a researcher wants to answer through their study. These questions guide the research process and help the researcher focus on what information they want to gather and analyze.

 

Research questions are often used in qualitative research or exploratory studies where the aim is to understand a phenomenon, explore relationships between variables, or gain insights into a particular topic. Unlike hypothesis testing, which involves specific predictions and statistical tests, research questions are more open-ended and do not require quantification of data for statistical analysis.

b. Research design: The research design is crucial for the practical significance of the study. It outlines the overall plan and structure of the research, including data collection methods and data analysis techniques.

 

c. Research method: The research method refers to the specific techniques and tools used to collect and analyze data. The choice of research method affects the reliability and validity of the research findings.

Question 44
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 22 Oct 2022 Morning)Statement I:A systematic review of literature defines the purpose of the review in explicit terms.Statement II:The systematic review can be applied to qualitative research since it is not evidence based.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Statement I is true but Statement II is false.

Statement I: This statement is true. A systematic review is a type of literature review that follows a rigorous and structured approach to identify, appraise, and synthesize all relevant studies on a specific topic. One of the key characteristics of a systematic review is that it defines a clear research question or objective before conducting the review.

 

Statement II: This statement is false. A systematic review is evidence-based and aims to provide an unbiased and comprehensive summary of the available evidence on a particular research question or topic. While systematic reviews are commonly used in quantitative research, they can also be applied to qualitative research studies. In fact, systematic reviews can be conducted on various types of evidence, including qualitative studies, if they meet the inclusion criteria and contribute to answering the research question.

 

Quiz Attempt #119758

Total Questions: 17
Question 1
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 14 Mar 2023 Morning)Statement I:Different research designs have different advantages. For example, the one-shot design is known for quick results and efficiency.Statement II:A longitudinal design is to study the same respondents over different periods of time and tracks changes over the period of study.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Statement I: This statement is true. Different research designs have various advantages and disadvantages. The one-shot design, also known as cross-sectional research, is often chosen when researchers need to collect data at a single point in time. It can be efficient for obtaining a snapshot of a particular situation or phenomenon, and it provides quick results.

 

Statement II: This statement is also true. A longitudinal design involves studying the same group of respondents (or subjects) over an extended period, with multiple measurements or data collection points. It allows researchers to track changes, developments, or trends over time within the same group, making it useful for understanding the dynamics of phenomena that evolve over extended periods.

Question 2
Given below are two statements:Statement I:A research design is blueprint that guides the use of a research method and analysis of data.Statement II:A research design is in no way connected with the expression of causal relations between variables.In light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below: (UGC NET 01 Oct 2022 Evening)
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect.
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.
Correct Answer: Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.

Statement I: "A research design is a blueprint that guides the use of a research method and analysis of data." This statement is incorrect. A research design is not the same as a blueprint; rather, it is a plan or strategy that outlines how a research study will be conducted, including the methods and procedures that will be used to collect and analyze data. A research design is a systematic and structured approach to conducting research.

 

Statement II: "A research design is in no way connected with the expression of causal relations between variables." This statement is correct. While a research design does play a crucial role in determining the type of data to be collected and the methods of analysis, it is not directly responsible for establishing causal relations between variables. The establishment of causal relationships often involves specific research methods like experimental design, which goes beyond the general research design.

Question 3
The components of a research design are: (UGC NET 22 Dec 2018)(a)Comparison(b)Control(c)Reactivity(d)Manipulation(e) Non-representativeness(f) GeneralisationOptions:
  • A.(a), (b), (d) and (f)
  • B.(a), (c), (e) and (f)
  • C.(c), (d), (e) and (f)
  • D.(b), (c), (d) and (e)
Correct Answer: (a), (b), (d) and (f)

A research design typically consists of four important components:

Comparison: This component allows researchers to demonstrate the relationship between the independent and dependent variables.

Control: Involves some form of control over the introduction of the independent variables to determine the time order of variables.

Manipulation: Refers to the control over the independent variables to establish cause-and-effect relationships.

Generalisation: Requires the findings of the research to be applicable to natural settings and populations under investigation.

Question 4
What is a Research Design? (UGC NET Dec 2014)
  • A.A way of conducting research that is not grounded in theory.
  • B.The choice between using qualitative or quantitative methods.
  • C.The style in which you present your research findings e.g. a graph.
  • D.A framework for every stage of the collection and analysis of data.
Correct Answer: A framework for every stage of the collection and analysis of data.

A research design encompasses the methods and procedures applied for the collection and analysis of variables specified in the research problem. The research design defines the type and sub-type of the study, research problem, hypotheses, independent and dependent variables, experimental design (if applicable), data collection methods, and a statistical analysis plan. It serves as a systematic and structured approach to finding answers to research questions.

Question 5
When we design the experiment in such a way that the variations caused by extraneous factors can all be combined under the general concept of "chance", it represents which principle? (UGC NET 28 Nov Morning 2021)
  • A.Principle of randomization
  • B.Principle of replication
  • C.Principle of local control
  • D.Principle of operational control
Correct Answer: Principle of randomization

Randomization involves randomly assigning participants or subjects to different experimental conditions or groups. By doing so, we distribute the effects of extraneous factors equally across the groups, and any differences observed between the groups can be attributed to the manipulation of the independent variable.

 

The Principle of randomization is crucial in experimental design as it helps control for confounding variables and increases the internal validity of the study. It ensures that the groups are comparable at the outset and allows us to make cause-and-effect inferences based on the results.

Question 6
The conceptual framework in which a research is conducted is called a: (UGC NET 26 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Synopsis of research
  • B.Research design
  • C.Research hypothesis
  • D.Research paradigm
Correct Answer: Research design

Research design refers to the plan and structure that a researcher creates to guide the entire research process. It acts as a blueprint that outlines how the research will be conducted, including the methods, techniques, and procedures that will be used to collect and analyze data. Research design is crucial as it helps ensure that the research is conducted efficiently and effectively, addressing the research questions and objectives.

 

A well-thought-out research design allows the researcher to make informed decisions about data collection methods, sampling techniques, data analysis approaches, and the overall implementation of the study. It provides a clear path for the researcher to follow, ensuring that the study is organized and systematic.

Question 7
The research design is specifically related to which of the following features in research?(i) Sample Selection(ii) Formulation of a plan(iii) Deciding about the tool for data collection(iv) Hypothesis making(v) Choice of a field of inquirySelect your answer from the options given below: (UGC NET 24 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.(ii), (iii) and (iv)
  • B.(i), (ii) and (iii)
  • C.(ii), (iv) and (v)
  • D.(iii), (iv) and (v)
Correct Answer: (i), (ii) and (iii)

The research design is specifically related to the following features in research:

(i) Sample Selection: The research design determines how the sample for the study will be selected. It outlines the criteria for inclusion and exclusion of participants, the sampling method to be used (e.g., random sampling, stratified sampling), and the size of the sample to be collected.

 

(ii) Formulation of a Plan: Research design involves the formulation of a detailed plan for conducting the study. It outlines the step-by-step approach that the researcher will follow to collect data, analyze it, and draw conclusions. The plan includes various research activities and their sequencing to ensure a coherent and systematic investigation.

 

(iii) Deciding about the Tool for Data Collection: The research design guides the selection of appropriate data collection methods and tools. It helps in deciding whether to use surveys, interviews, observations, experiments, or a combination of methods to gather data that aligns with the research objectives.

Question 8
Match List I with List II (UGC NET 12 Nov 2020 Morning paper)List I (Key Terms used in Research)a) Hypothesisb) Samplec) Research Designd) Research ToolList II (Description of Terms)i) Techniques used for collection of facts and informationii) Devices for arriving at conclusionsiii) A tentative statement indicating potential solution of the problem of studyiv) A subset drawn from a defined setv) Conceptual framework for conducting researchSelect the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a-i, b-ii, c-iii, d-iv
  • B.a-ii, b-iii, c-iv, d-v
  • C.a-i, b-ii. c-iv, d-iii
  • D.a-iii, b-iv, c-v, d-i
Correct Answer: a-iii, b-iv, c-v, d-i

a) Hypothesis is a tentative statement that proposes a potential solution to the research problem or question. It serves as a proposition that can be tested and either supported or refuted through research and data analysis.

 

b) Sample refers to a subset of the defined set or population from which data is collected. Researchers select a sample to gather information that represents the larger population in a manageable way.

 

c) Research Design is the conceptual framework or plan that outlines the overall structure and strategy for conducting the research. It includes decisions on data collection methods, sample selection, data analysis techniques, and other essential elements of the research process.

 

d) Research Tool involves the techniques and methods used for the collection of data and information. Researchers use various tools such as surveys, questionnaires, interviews, observations, etc., to gather relevant data for their study.

Question 9
A study in which a group of participants is observed and measured over a period of time, refers to (UGC NET 22 Mar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Longitudinal Research
  • B.Archival Research
  • C.Cross-sectional Research
  • D.Correlational Research
Correct Answer: Longitudinal Research

Longitudinal research is a study method where a group of participants is observed and measured at multiple points in time to track changes or developments over an extended period. It allows researchers to examine how variables or behaviors evolve over the course of months, years, or even decades, providing valuable insights into trends, growth, and potential causal relationships over time.

Question 10
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET10 Oct 2022 Evening)Statement I:Exploratory research is conducted for data indications.Statement II:The goal of exploratory research is to gather final data to find out causality.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Statement I is true but Statement II is false.

Statement I: Exploratory research is conducted to explore and gain insights into a research problem or topic. It aims to gather preliminary data, ideas, and understanding to formulate research questions, hypotheses, or establish the scope of the study. Exploratory research is often conducted in the early stages of a research project to provide a foundation for further investigation.

 

Statement II: This statement is false. The goal of exploratory research is not to gather final data or establish causality. Instead, exploratory research is primarily concerned with discovering new ideas, concepts, patterns, or relationships that can be further investigated in subsequent studies. It does not aim to establish causality directly, but rather to provide a basis for the formulation of hypotheses and research questions for further research.

Question 11
An exploratory research on a small scale is called: (UGC NET09 July 2022 Evening)
  • A.Sample test
  • B.Pre-test
  • C.Pilot test
  • D.Informal test
Correct Answer: Pilot test

A pilot test is an exploratory research conducted on a small scale before the actual full-scale research or study. It involves testing the research methods, data collection instruments, and procedures to identify potential issues and make necessary adjustments before implementing the main study.

The purpose of a pilot test is to:

  • Assess Feasibility: Determine whether the research plan and methods are feasible and practical to implement on a larger scale.
  • Identify Problems: Identify any issues, ambiguities, or errors in the research design, data collection instruments, or procedures that need to be addressed before the main study.
  • Refine Procedures: Refine and improve data collection procedures, questionnaire design, or experimental protocols based on the insights gained during the pilot test.
  • Estimate Sample Size: Obtain initial data to estimate the required sample size for the main study.
  • Validate Measures: Assess the reliability and validity of measurement tools to ensure they provide accurate and consistent data.
  • Familiarize Researchers: Familiarize researchers with the research process and potential challenges, helping them better prepare for the main study.

 

A pilot test is typically conducted on a small sample of participants, which could be similar to the target population of the main study. However, the main purpose of the pilot test is not to draw definitive conclusions or generalizations but rather to refine and validate the research approach before proceeding to the larger study.

Question 12
When a research study is conducted to know about an unknown area and collect information, it is known as: (UGC NET08 Oct 2022 Evening)
  • A.Pilot Study
  • B.Feasibility study
  • C.Explanatory research
  • D.Explanatory research
Correct Answer: Explanatory research

Exploratory research is conducted to explore and investigate relatively unknown or poorly understood areas or phenomena. It aims to gather preliminary information, insights, and understanding about a subject or problem. The primary goal of exploratory research is to generate hypotheses or research questions for further investigation and to provide a foundation for more in-depth research in the future.

 

Let's briefly explain why the other options are incorrect:

(A) Pilot Study: A pilot study is a small-scale preliminary study conducted before the main research to test and refine research methods, instruments, and procedures. It is not necessarily conducted to explore unknown areas or gather new information.

 

(B) Feasibility Study: A feasibility study is conducted to assess the practicality and viability of a proposed research project. It involves evaluating whether the research can be realistically carried out, given available resources, time constraints, and ethical considerations. It is not primarily focused on exploring unknown areas.

 

(C) Explanatory Research: Explanatory research aims to explain the relationships between variables and establish cause-and-effect relationships. It is conducted to understand why certain events or phenomena occur and why specific outcomes happen. It is not the primary purpose of explanatory research to explore unknown areas or collect information about them.

Question 13
The elements of a cross-sectional design are: (UGC NET 04 Dec 2021 Evening)a. Absence of quantitative data.b. Domination of qualitative data.c. A sample of cases with inter-related variations.d. Data are collected at a single point time.e. Examination of relationships between variables.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, c only
  • B.b, c, d only
  • C.c, d, e only
  • D.a, c, e only
Correct Answer: c, d, e only

A sample of cases with inter-related variations - This is a key element of a cross-sectional design. In a cross-sectional study, data is collected from a sample of participants or cases at a single point in time, and variations among the cases are examined to understand relationships between variables.

 

b. Data are collected at a single point in time - This is another essential element of a cross-sectional design. Cross-sectional studies involve collecting data from participants or cases at a specific moment, providing a snapshot of the variables' status at that time.

 

c. Examination of relationships between variables - This is a primary objective of a cross-sectional design. Researchers use cross-sectional data to examine relationships, associations, or correlations between variables to gain insights into potential patterns or connections.

Question 14
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 26 Nov Evening 2021)Statement I:Exploratory studies mainly aim at developing hypotheses or questions for further research.Statement II:The goal of formal study is to test the hypotheses or answer the questions posed.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:

  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Statement I: This statement is true. Exploratory studies are typically conducted when the researcher wants to gain a better understanding of a research problem or a new topic that has not been extensively studied before. The main goal of exploratory studies is to explore and identify potential hypotheses, research questions, or areas of interest that can be further investigated in future research.

 

Statement II: This statement is also true. Formal studies, often referred to as confirmatory studies, are conducted to test specific hypotheses or answer well-defined research questions.
