Question 15
The characteristics of longitudinal studies are: (UGC NET 25 Nov Morning 2021)a. Limited results.b. Do not need heavy investment.c. Provide alternative choices.d. Allow insight into the time order of variables.e. Focuses on individual or institutional developments.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b and c only
  • B.b, c and d only
  • C.c, d and e only
  • D.a, d and e only
Correct Answer: c, d and e only

a. Provide alternative choices - Longitudinal studies may provide alternative choices in terms of data collection methods and analytical approaches. Researchers can choose various methods to collect data and analyze it longitudinally, depending on the research objectives and available resources.

 

b. Allow insight into the time order of variables - This is a fundamental characteristic of longitudinal studies. By following participants over time, researchers can establish the temporal sequence of events, which is essential in determining cause-and-effect relationships between variables.

 

c. Focuses on individual or institutional developments - Longitudinal studies often focus on tracking individual or institutional changes and developments over time. They are well-suited for examining changes in behaviors, attitudes, and outcomes within specific individuals or groups.

Question 16
The study of 'why does stressful living result in heart attack'? can be classified as: (UGC NET 24 June 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Descriptive research
  • B.Explanatory research
  • C.Correlational research
  • D.Feasibility research
Correct Answer: Explanatory research

Explanatory research aims to establish connections between different ideas and seeks to comprehend the various reasons, causes, and their subsequent effects. It often follows exploratory research and descriptive research. While exploratory research explores a topic and descriptive research provides factual information about it, explanatory research delves into the "why" behind the observed phenomenon.

 

Examples of explanatory research include:

 

  • 1. Descriptive research may reveal that 20% of students failed in an exam, while explanatory research investigates the underlying reasons for this failure.
  • 2. Descriptive research might indicate that a computer system with more RAM operates at a higher speed, but explanatory research would explore why this is the case compared to a computer system with less RAM.
Question 17
Nine year olds are taller than seven year olds. This is an example of a reference drawn from (UGC NET Jun 2012)
  • A.Vertical study
  • B.Cross-sectional study
  • C.Time series study
  • D.Experimental study
Correct Answer: Cross-sectional study

Cross-sectional studies are a type of research design used to collect data at a specific point in time from a sample or population. In this type of study, researchers gather information from individuals or groups at a particular moment, allowing them to compare different groups or variables at that specific instance. In the given example, researchers likely measured the heights of children who were seven years old and nine years old at a particular time to determine that nine-year-olds are generally taller than seven-year-olds.

  • Vertical learning refers to the transformation of one's thinking, emotions, and understanding of the world, increasing complexity and emotional intelligence. It is not applicable in the context of the given example.
  • Time-series analysis is a statistical methodology used for longitudinal research designs where data is collected repeatedly at regular intervals over time. It is not relevant to the comparison of heights between nine-year-olds and seven-year-olds at a single point in time.
  • Experimental studies involve manipulating variables to observe cause-and-effect relationships. However, the example provided does not involve any manipulation or control of variables; it simply presents a comparison of heights between two age groups at a specific moment, making it a cross-sectional study.

Question 1
Which of the following features of research are associated with qualitative-inquiring? (UGC NET 30 Sept 2020 Evening paper)(i) Actual settings as the direct source of data(ii) Data collection under controlled conditions(iii) Concern with process rather than simply with outcomes(iv) Establishing relationships and explaining the causes of changes(v) Concerned with what are called participant perspectivesChoose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.(i), (iii) and (iv) only
  • B.(i), (iii) and (v) only
  • C.(ii), (iii) and (iv) only
  • D.(iii), (iv) and (v) only
Correct Answer: (i), (iii) and (v) only

The features of research, which are associated with qualitative-inquiring are:

(i) Actual settings as the direct source of data: In qualitative research, researchers gather data by directly observing and immersing themselves in real-life settings. They aim to understand the phenomena within their natural context, often studying human behavior, interactions, or social processes in their authentic environments. This approach allows researchers to gain rich and in-depth insights into the subject under investigation.

 

(ii) Concern with process rather than simply with outcomes: Qualitative research is primarily interested in understanding the underlying processes and dynamics that lead to certain outcomes. It delves into the "how" and "why" behind phenomena, aiming to uncover the complexities of human behavior and social phenomena. This is in contrast to quantitative research, which often focuses more on measuring and analyzing outcomes and associations.

 

(iii) Concerned with what are called participant perspectives: In qualitative research, understanding the subjective perspectives and experiences of the participants is crucial. Researchers often interact with individuals or groups, collecting data through methods like interviews, focus groups, or participant observation. By incorporating the perspectives of the people involved, qualitative research aims to gain a holistic understanding of the studied phenomenon.

Question 2
Arrange the steps in a hypothetico-deductive research in the correct sequence: (UGC NET 24 Sept 2020 Evening paper)A. Identifying and defining a research problemB. Defining the population and drawing a sub-set therefromC. Data collection using appropriate research tasks followed by data analysesD. Hypothesis formulation and developing a design of researchE. Taking a decision on the substantive research hypothesis via testing of the Null hypothesis (H0)Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, D, B, C, E
  • B.A, B, C, D, E
  • C.A, C, B, D, E
  • D.B, A, C, D, E
Correct Answer: A, D, B, C, E

The hypothetico-deductive research method involves several steps, and the correct sequence is as follows:

1. Identifying and defining a research problem: This is the initial step where researchers identify a specific area of interest and define the research problem they want to investigate.

 

2. Hypothesis formulation and developing a design of research: In this step, researchers formulate a testable hypothesis or theory that provides a potential explanation for the research problem. They also develop a research design, which outlines the methods and procedures for data collection and analysis.

3. Defining the population and drawing a sub-set therefrom: Researchers define the target population for their study and then draw a subset, known as the sample, from this defined population. The sample represents a smaller, manageable group that researchers will collect data from.

 

4. Data collection using appropriate research tasks followed by data analyses: In this step, researchers collect data from the chosen sample using appropriate research methods such as surveys, interviews, observations, etc. Once data is gathered, it undergoes analysis to derive insights and conclusions.

 

5. Taking a decision on the substantive research hypothesis via testing of the Null hypothesis (H0): Finally, researchers test the formulated hypothesis by comparing it with the observed data or experimental results. They use statistical methods to assess whether the null hypothesis (H0) can be accepted or rejected. The decision on the substantive research hypothesis is based on the outcomes of this hypothesis testing.

Question 3
In using the hypothetico-deductive research paradigm which of the following sequences is considered appropriate? (UGC NET 24 Sept 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Hypothesis making, hypothesis testing, arriving at generalization and conclusive
  • B.Establishing a research problem, hypothesis making, hypothesis testing arriving at generalisation and conclusion
  • C.Hypothesis making, establishing a research problem, hypothesis testing, arriving at generalisation and conclusion.
  • D.Hypothesis testing, hypothesis making, finalizing the research problem, arriving at the generalisation and conclusion.
Correct Answer: Establishing a research problem, hypothesis making, hypothesis testing arriving at generalisation and conclusion

The hypothetico-deductive research paradigm, also known as the H-D method, involves three main parts: hypothesis making, hypothesis testing, and comparison with observations or experiment results. The process begins by establishing a research problem or identifying an area of interest that requires investigation. Researchers then formulate a hypothesis or theory that they propose to test.

 

Next, testable consequences are deduced from the hypothesis. These consequences serve as the basis for hypothesis testing, where researchers compare the observed data or experimental results with the expected outcomes based on the hypothesis. The hypothesis is evaluated through statistical analysis, and researchers draw conclusions based on the results.

 

The appropriate sequence for the hypothetico-deductive research paradigm is as follows:

  • 1. Establishing a research problem: Identifying the area of interest and the specific question to be addressed through research.
  • 2. Hypothesis making: Formulating a testable hypothesis or theory that provides a potential explanation for the research problem.
  • 3. Hypothesis testing: Deducing testable consequences from the hypothesis and comparing them with the observed data or experimental results.
  • 4. Arriving at generalization and conclusion: Based on the results of the hypothesis testing, researchers draw conclusions and make generalizations about the research problem.
Question 4
Given below are two statements, one is labelled as Assertion A and the other is labelled as Reason R (UGC NET 25 Sept 2020 Morning paper)Assertion A:Empirico-inductive paradigm in research focuses on meaning-giving subjective perspectives to depict realityReason R:The purpose of research in this paradigm is not to arrive at generalizations but to discover the reality as lived.In light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both A and R are correct and R is the correct explanation of A
  • B.Both A and R are correct but R is NOT the correct explanation of A
  • C.A is correct but R is not correct
  • D.A is not correct but R is correct
Correct Answer: Both A and R are correct and R is the correct explanation of A

Empirico-inductive paradigm in research refers to an approach that emphasizes understanding subjective perspectives and meanings attributed to experiences to depict reality. In this paradigm, researchers engage with the data inductively, deriving insights and patterns directly from the empirical observations and experiences of individuals or groups. The focus is on capturing the depth and complexity of human experiences and behaviors from their lived perspectives.

 

The reason provided, R, explains the purpose of research within the empirico-inductive paradigm. The primary goal is not to arrive at generalizations or universal laws but rather to explore and discover the reality as it is lived by individuals or communities. This paradigm recognizes that reality can be context-specific and may vary across different situations and contexts. Therefore, researchers using the empirico-inductive paradigm seek to uncover the unique qualities and meanings that individuals attribute to their experiences, without necessarily aiming for broad generalizations.

 

Both the assertion and the reason are correct, and reason R provides an accurate explanation of assertion A. It highlights the key characteristic of the empirico-inductive paradigm in research, which is to understand subjective perspectives and the lived reality of individuals or groups rather than seeking generalizable laws or theories.

Question 10

Question 15

Question 16
Which of the following represent the Quantitative Research methodology? (UGC NET 14 Oct 2022 Morning)a. One to One Interviewb. Survey researchc. Focus groupsd. Correlation researche. Descriptive researchChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, d, e Only
  • B.b, d, e Only
  • C.b, c, d Only
  • D.c, d, e Only
Correct Answer: b, d, e Only

a. One to One Interview: One-to-one interviews are commonly used in qualitative research rather than quantitative research. In qualitative research, one-to-one interviews allow for in-depth exploration of participants' perspectives and experiences.

 

b. Survey research: Survey research is a hallmark of quantitative research methodology. Surveys involve collecting data from a large sample using standardized questionnaires or structured interviews. The data collected is often numerical, enabling statistical analysis.

 

c. Focus groups: Focus groups are also commonly used in qualitative research rather than quantitative research. Focus groups involve group discussions to explore shared experiences, opinions, and perceptions among participants.

 

d. Correlation research: Correlation research is a quantitative research method used to examine the relationship between two or more variables. It involves measuring the strength and direction of the relationship between variables.

 

e. Descriptive research: Descriptive research is a quantitative research method used to describe and summarize characteristics of a population or phenomenon. It focuses on providing an accurate and detailed representation of the research subject.

 

So, the correct answer is B.

Question 17
Which of the below mentioned approaches fall under the Quantitative Approach? (UGC NET 28 Nov Morning 2021)1. Simulation approach2. Projective technique3. Inferential approach4. Depth interview5. Experimental approachChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.1, 3 and 5 only
  • B.2, 3 and 5 only
  • C.2, 3 and 4 only
  • D.1, 2 and 3 only
Correct Answer: 1, 3 and 5 only

The correct answer is A.

The Quantitative Approach in research involves the collection and analysis of numerical data to test hypotheses, make predictions, and draw statistical inferences. It emphasizes the use of quantifiable data and statistical techniques to draw objective conclusions about the population being studied. Let's analyze each approach mentioned in the options:

 

Simulation Approach - Quantitative (Correct)

The simulation approach involves creating a model or imitation of a real-world system or process to study its behavior over time. It often uses mathematical equations and numerical data to simulate and analyze complex systems. The simulation approach is a quantitative method as it deals with numerical data and uses statistical analysis to draw conclusions from the simulations.

 

Projective Technique - Not Quantitative

Projective techniques are qualitative research methods used to uncover hidden or subconscious thoughts, feelings, or motivations of participants. These techniques, such as the Rorschach inkblot test or thematic apperception test (TAT), rely on participants projecting their thoughts onto ambiguous stimuli. Projective techniques do not involve numerical data or statistical analysis and are considered qualitative.

 

Inferential Approach - Quantitative (Correct)

The inferential approach is a quantitative method used to draw conclusions about a population based on sample data. Inferential statistics involves making inferences, predictions, or generalizations about a larger population using sample data. This approach uses numerical data and statistical tests to make objective and generalizable statements.

 

Depth Interview - Not Quantitative

Depth interviews are qualitative research methods that involve in-depth and open-ended interviews with participants. The goal is to explore their perspectives, experiences, and emotions related to a specific topic. Depth interviews generate rich and detailed qualitative data, but they do not involve numerical data or statistical analysis, making them a qualitative approach.

 

Experimental Approach - Quantitative (Correct)

The experimental approach involves manipulating independent variables to observe their effects on dependent variables, while controlling other variables. It is a fundamental quantitative research design used to establish cause-and-effect relationships. Experimental research uses numerical data and statistical analysis to determine the significance of the observed effects and test hypotheses.

Question 18
Given below are two statements:- (UGC NET 29 Nov Morning 2021)Statement I:Sample sizes for qualitative research vary by technique but are generally small.Statement II:Qualitative research involves non‐probability sampling.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Statement I: This statement is true. In qualitative research, the sample sizes often depend on the research design, the specific qualitative technique used (e.g., interviews, focus groups, case studies), and the depth of analysis required. Generally, qualitative research involves smaller sample sizes compared to quantitative research, as the emphasis is on in-depth exploration rather than statistical generalization.

 

Statement II: This statement is also true. Qualitative research typically uses non-probability sampling techniques. Non-probability sampling means that the selection of participants is based on non-random methods, and every individual in the population does not have an equal chance of being selected. Instead, qualitative researchers purposefully select participants based on their relevance to the research question and their ability to provide rich and meaningful insights into the research topic.

Question 19
A major focus in quantitative research is on: (UGC NET 29 Oct 2022 Evening)
  • A.Historicity
  • B.Causality
  • C.Social reflections
  • D.Creating an artificial environment.
Correct Answer: Causality

A major focus in quantitative research is on causality. Quantitative research aims to establish cause-and-effect relationships between variables. Researchers use statistical methods to analyze data and determine whether changes in one variable (independent variable) cause changes in another variable (dependent variable). By establishing causality, researchers can make predictions and draw conclusions about the impact of specific factors on outcomes.

 

Quantitative research is designed to test hypotheses and examine relationships between variables using rigorous methods and experimental or non-experimental designs. The goal is to identify patterns, trends, and associations that provide evidence of causation.

  • Historicity: Historicity refers to the factuality or authenticity of historical events and documents. While historical data can be used in quantitative research, historicity itself is not a primary focus of quantitative research.
  • Social reflections: Social reflections are not a major focus in quantitative research. While quantitative research may explore social phenomena and behaviors, its primary emphasis is on quantifying and testing relationships between variables rather than interpreting social reflections.
  • Creating an artificial environment: Creating an artificial environment is more common in experimental research, which is a subset of quantitative research. However, it is not a major focus of all quantitative research. Quantitative research can also be conducted in natural or real-world settings without artificially manipulating the environment.
Question 20
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 26 Dec Morning 2021)Statement I: If we are interested in the worldview of members of a certain social group, a qualitative research strategy that is sensitive to how participants interpret their social world may be preferable.Statement II: If a researcher is interested in a topic on which little or no research has been done in the past, quantitative research may be easy to employ because there is little prior literature from which to draw leads.In light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect.
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.
Correct Answer: Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.

Statement I: This statement is correct. Qualitative research is well-suited for exploring and understanding the worldview, perspectives, and interpretations of individuals or social groups. Through qualitative methods such as interviews, focus groups, or ethnographic observations, researchers can gain in-depth insights into how participants interpret and make sense of their social world.

 

Statement II: This statement is incorrect. If little or no research has been done on a topic, it may actually make quantitative research more challenging. Quantitative research often relies on established theories, concepts, and prior literature to inform the formulation of hypotheses and the design of research instruments. When there is limited existing literature, it may be difficult to develop a solid theoretical framework or hypotheses for quantitative research.

Question 21
Which of the following are disadvantages of qualitative research? (UGC NET 12 July 2022 Morning)a. Too sensitive to the context.b. Open to debate.c. Too subjective.d. Difficult to generalise.e. Issue of replication.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, d and e only
  • B.b, c and d only
  • C.c, d and e only
  • D.a, b and c only
Correct Answer: c, d and e only

a. Too subjective: One of the main disadvantages of qualitative research is its subjectivity. Qualitative research relies heavily on the researcher's interpretation and judgment in data collection, analysis, and reporting. This subjectivity can introduce bias and affect the validity and reliability of the findings.

 

b. Difficult to generalize: Generalizability is a limitation of qualitative research. Due to its small sample sizes and context-specific nature, the findings of qualitative studies cannot be easily generalized to a larger population or other settings. The emphasis in qualitative research is on in-depth exploration rather than statistical representativeness.

 

c. Issue of replication: Replication is challenging in qualitative research. Replicating qualitative studies to validate the findings can be difficult due to the uniqueness of the research context and the subjective nature of data interpretation. Unlike quantitative research, where replication is more straightforward, qualitative research may not yield the same results when repeated in different settings.

Question 22
One of the aims of qualitative data analysis is to: (UGC NET 14 Oct 2022 Evening)
  • A.Expand the Selected text or material.
  • B.Analyse the researcher's credentials.
  • C.Describe a phenomenon.
  • D.Focus on binary dissection.
Correct Answer: Describe a phenomenon.

Qualitative data analysis is a method used to interpret and make sense of non-numeric data, such as text, interviews, observations, and open-ended survey responses. It is commonly employed in social sciences, humanities, and other fields to understand human experiences, behaviors, and the social world.

 

The main aim of qualitative data analysis is to describe a phenomenon or explore the meanings and perspectives of individuals or groups. It goes beyond simply counting or categorizing data; instead, it seeks to uncover deeper insights and understandings by examining the context, themes, and relationships present in the data.

Question 23
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 29 Oct 2022 Evening)Statement I:Often qualitative studies provide too many details of the setting that are investigated.Statement II:Critics point out that qualitative research suffers from the issue of replication.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Statement I: Qualitative studies are known for their in-depth exploration of the research setting. Researchers often immerse themselves in the context to understand the phenomenon from multiple perspectives. As a result, they may provide rich and detailed descriptions of the setting, which is a characteristic feature of qualitative research.

 

Statement II: Replication in research refers to the ability to repeat a study's methods and procedures to assess the consistency and reliability of the findings. In the context of qualitative research, it is often challenging to achieve exact replication because of the unique and context-bound nature of qualitative data. Critics argue that the specific conditions and context of qualitative studies make it difficult to reproduce the same study in a different setting. However, qualitative research can still achieve a form of replication through techniques like triangulation, where multiple sources of data are used to corroborate findings, increasing the study's reliability.

Question 24
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 03 Dec Morning 2021)One is labelled as Assertion A and the other is labelled as Reason R:Assertion ‘A’:Actual settings are the direct source of data and the researcher is the key instrument in qualitative research.Reason ‘R’:The purpose underlying qualitative researches is relatively more directed at depiction of reality rather than arriving at context free generalizations.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A.
  • B.Both A and R are true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A.
  • C.A is true but R is false.
  • D.A is false but R is true.
Correct Answer: Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A.

Assertion A: In qualitative research, the researcher typically collects data directly from the actual settings where the phenomenon of interest occurs. This may involve conducting interviews, observations, or analyzing documents and artifacts in their natural context. Moreover, the researcher plays a central role in the data collection and interpretation process, often referred to as the "instrument" of the research. The researcher's personal characteristics, experiences, and interactions with participants influence the data gathering and analysis, making them a crucial aspect of qualitative research.

 

Reason R: The primary aim of qualitative research is to gain an in-depth understanding of the phenomenon being studied. Qualitative researchers are interested in exploring the complexity and richness of real-life situations, experiences, and perspectives. Instead of seeking universal or context-free generalizations, qualitative research seeks to depict the reality of a specific setting or social context. It emphasizes context and context-bound interpretations to capture the uniqueness of each research setting.

Question 25
Given below are two statements: One is labelled as Assertion A and the other is labelled as Reason R: (UGC NET 05 Jan Evening 2022)Assertion ‘A’:Unique case orientation is possible in qualitative research which may later lead to cross — case analysis.Reasons ‘R’:Design flexibility is the hallmark of qualitative research as it is open to situational changes.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A.
  • B.Both A and R are true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A.
  • C.A is true but R is false.
  • D.A is false but R is true.
Correct Answer: Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A.

Assertion A: In qualitative research, researchers often focus on unique cases or individual contexts to gain a deep understanding of a particular phenomenon. Each case is considered in its own right, and the emphasis is on exploring the intricacies and complexities of that specific case. However, as researchers gather data from multiple unique cases, they can later engage in cross-case analysis, where they compare and contrast the findings across different cases to identify patterns, common themes, or variations. This allows qualitative researchers to derive more comprehensive insights and develop broader understandings of the phenomenon under study.

 

Reason R: One of the key characteristics of qualitative research is its design flexibility. Unlike quantitative research, which typically follows a rigid and predefined research design, qualitative research allows for adaptability and responsiveness to the research context. Qualitative researchers are open to situational changes, which means they can modify their research questions, data collection methods, and even theoretical frameworks during the research process to better suit the unfolding situation and gather more relevant and rich data.

Question 26
Identify those statements which describe the characteristic features of qualitative research paradigm (UGC NET 29 Sept 2020 Morning paper)A. Researchers tend to analyze their data inductivelyB. The substantive research hypothesis is tested via Null hypothesisC. Data take the form of words or picturesD. Actual settings are the direct source of dataE. It assumes that there are social facts with a single objective realityChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B and C only
  • B.A, B and E only
  • C.B, C and E only
  • D.A, C and D only
Correct Answer: A, C and D only

The characteristic features of qualitative research paradigm are:

a. Researchers tend to analyze their data inductively: In qualitative research, data analysis is often conducted inductively, where researchers immerse themselves in the data and derive patterns, themes, and insights directly from the data itself. It is a bottom-up approach, allowing researchers to generate new theories or interpretations based on the data collected, rather than starting with pre-existing hypotheses.

 

b. The substantive research hypothesis is tested via Null hypothesis: Qualitative research does not typically involve testing substantive research hypotheses using null hypothesis testing. Instead, it focuses on understanding the phenomena and generating insights, rather than confirming or refuting specific hypotheses through statistical testing.

 

c. Data take the form of words or pictures: Qualitative research data is primarily textual or visual in nature. Researchers collect data in the form of words (interview transcripts, field notes, narratives) or pictures (photographs, videos, visual representations) to capture the rich and nuanced details of human experiences and social phenomena.

Question 27
In qualitative research paradigm, which of the following features may be considered critical? (UGC NET Jul 2016)
  • A.Data collection with standardised research tools.
  • B.Sampling design with probability sample techniques.
  • C.Data collection with bottom-up empirical evidences.
  • D.Data gathering to take place with top-down systematic evidences.
Correct Answer: Data collection with bottom-up empirical evidences.

Qualitative research is closely associated with the social constructivist paradigm, which recognizes the socially constructed nature of reality. The main focus of qualitative research is to record, analyze, and uncover the deeper meanings and significance of human behavior and experiences, including contradictory beliefs, behaviors, and emotions.

 

The term "bottom-up approach" refers to the way qualitative researchers start with specific data and then work towards generating broader themes or theories. They move from the specific observations and experiences of individuals to the development of more general understandings or theories. This bottom-up process allows researchers to uncover nuances and complexities that may not be apparent through standardized research tools or predefined hypotheses.

Question 28
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 30 Sept 2020 Morning paper)Statement I:Qualitative research is an umbrella term to refer to various research strategies that share certain characteristicsStatement II:The research-data collected in qualitative research has been termed soft i.e, rich in description of people, places and conversation etc.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is false
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is true
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true

Statement I: Qualitative research is a broad and inclusive category that encompasses diverse research strategies, methodologies, and approaches. It is not limited to a single method but rather includes a range of techniques that share some common characteristics. These characteristics typically revolve around the focus on understanding human behavior, experiences, interpretations, and social phenomena. Qualitative research aims to explore the "why" and "how" of a particular phenomenon, allowing researchers to gain insights into the complexities of human life.

 

Statement II: Qualitative research data is often described as "soft" because it provides rich, descriptive, and detailed information about the subjects under study. Researchers using qualitative methods collect data through techniques such as interviews, observations, focus groups, and open-ended surveys, among others. These methods allow researchers to capture the participants' perspectives, thoughts, emotions, and behaviors in their natural settings.

Question 29
From the following list identify the qualitative research characteristics and select your answer from the codes given below:(i) Creating purpose statements and research questions.(ii) Stating the purpose and research questions in a broad way.(iii) Collecting data based on words from a small number of individuals.(iv) Collecting numeric data and statistical analysis.(v) Using text analysis and Interpreting larger meanings of the findings. (UGC NET 20 June 2019 Evening Paper)Code:
  • A.(ii), (iii) and (v)
  • B.(i), (ii) and (iii)
  • C.(i), (ii) and (iv)
  • D.(i), (iii) and (v)
Correct Answer: (ii), (iii) and (v)

(i) Stating the purpose and research questions in a broad way: In qualitative research, the purpose and research questions are typically stated in a broad and open-ended manner. This allows the researcher to explore the phenomenon deeply and comprehensively without limiting the scope of the study. The focus is on understanding the complexity of the subject under investigation and gaining insights into the various aspects of the research topic.

 

(ii) Collecting data based on words from a small number of individuals: Qualitative research often involves collecting data through methods such as interviews, focus groups, or observations. The data collected are usually in the form of words, narratives, or descriptions rather than numerical values. The emphasis is on gaining rich and detailed information from a small number of participants, which allows for in-depth exploration of individual perspectives and experiences.

 

(iii) Using text analysis and interpreting larger meanings of the findings: Text analysis is a critical aspect of qualitative research. Researchers analyze the textual data obtained from interviews, observations, or other sources to identify themes, patterns, and underlying meanings. The goal is to interpret the data in a way that provides a deeper understanding of the research topic and generates insights into the larger context or implications of the findings.

Question 30
What are the characteristic features of the Quantitative Research paradigm? (UGC NET 01 Oct 2020 Morning paper)a. It is hypothetico-deductiveb. It is focused on natural settingsc. It lays stress on generalizations to the population characteristicsd. It emphasizes numeric data from a large number of peoplee. It says that the literature review plays a minor role but justify the problemChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, c and d only
  • B.a, b and c only
  • C.b, c and d only
  • D.c, d and e only
Correct Answer: a, c and d only

The characteristic features of the Quantitative Research paradigm are as follows:

a. It is hypothetico-deductive: Quantitative research follows a deductive approach, where researchers formulate hypotheses based on existing theories and knowledge. These hypotheses are then tested through empirical data collection and statistical analysis to either support or refute them.

 

b. It lays stress on generalizations to the population characteristics: Quantitative research aims to make generalizations and inferences about a larger population based on data collected from a sample. The goal is to draw conclusions that can be applied to a broader context beyond the immediate study participants.

 

c. It emphasizes numeric data from a large number of people: Quantitative research relies on collecting numerical data from a large and representative sample of participants. The data are often gathered through structured surveys, experiments, or other quantitative methods that yield measurable and quantifiable results.

Question 31
Given below are two statements (UGC NET 01 Oct 2020 Morning paper)Statement I: Qualitative research paradigm emphasizes participant perspectives and uses an empirico-inductive approachStatement II: In the same research project, it is neither possible nor desirable to use both Qualitative and Quantitative research paradigmsIn light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct
Correct Answer: Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect

Statement I is correct because it accurately describes the characteristics of the qualitative research paradigm. Qualitative research emphasizes understanding participant perspectives and experiences and often uses an empirico-inductive approach, where theories and insights are developed from the data collected during the research process.

 

Statement II is incorrect because it suggests that it is neither possible nor desirable to use both qualitative and quantitative research paradigms in the same research project. In reality, many research projects can benefit from a mixed-methods approach, where both qualitative and quantitative methods are used to provide a comprehensive and nuanced understanding of the research topic.

Question 32
Identify the qualitative research characteristics from the following: (UGC NET 05 Nov 2020 Morning paper)(i) Exploring a problem and developing a detailed understanding of a central phenomenon.(ii) Having the literature review play a minor role but justifying the problem.(iii) Describing a research problem through a description of trends.(iv) Collecting numeric data from a large number of people using instruments with present questions.(v) Collecting data based on words from a small number of individuals.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.(i), (ii) and (iii) only
  • B.(i), (ii) and (v) only
  • C.(ii), (iii) and (iv) only
  • D.(iii), (iv) and (v) only
Correct Answer: (i), (ii) and (v) only

Qualitative research characteristics can be identified from the following options:

(i) Exploring a problem and developing a detailed understanding of a central phenomenon.

(ii) Having the literature review play a minor role but justifying the problem.

(iii) Collecting data based on words from a small number of individuals.

 

These characteristics align with the nature of qualitative research. It involves delving into a specific problem to gain in-depth insights and understanding of the central phenomenon. While the literature review is considered, it does not play a dominant role, and the focus is more on the direct experiences of individuals, making the data collection primarily word-based and from a smaller number of participants. This approach allows researchers to embrace the complexity of real-world settings, adopt inductive reasoning, and be flexible in the research design based on the discovery process.

Question 33
Identify the features of qualitative research from the following: (UGC NET 11 Nov 2020 Morning paper)(i) Researcher becomes immersed in the situation present or past(ii) Researcher is detached from the study to avoid bias(iii) It develops context-bound generalizations(iv) It is based on logical positivist philosophy(v) It uses an emergent research designChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.(i), (ii) and (iii) only
  • B.(ii), (iii) and (iv) only
  • C.(i), (iii) and (v) only
  • D.(iii), (iv) and (v) only
Correct Answer: (i), (iii) and (v) only

Qualitative research is a naturalistic and in-depth inquiry that aims to understand social phenomena within their natural setting. It emphasizes the "why" rather than the "what" of social phenomena and relies on direct human experiences as a means of generating meaning in everyday life.

 

Key features of qualitative research are as follows:

  • 1. Naturalistic: Qualitative research takes place in real-world, natural settings without manipulation or strict control. It is commonly used in soft sciences or social sciences.
  • 2. Dialectic and Inductive Reasoning: Qualitative research seeks to establish truth through a discourse between multiple perspectives, arriving at conclusions through reasoned argumentation (dialectic). Researchers immerse themselves in the details and inductively derive findings. It involves an iterative process of data collection and analysis.
  • 3. Holistic Perspective: The study of the whole phenomenon as it occurs, without excessive control of variables. This approach aims to understand complex issues by broadly defining and studying the subject.
  • 4. Data: Qualitative research involves detailed and rich descriptions designed to capture the perspectives of the participants. The primary element of analysis is words rather than numerical data.
  • 5. Personal Contact: Researchers have direct contact with participants and the research setting, and their insights and perspectives are crucial in understanding the phenomenon.
  • 6. Dynamic: Qualitative research pays attention to ongoing changes in the participants and settings, recognizing that social phenomena are dynamic and subject to change.
  • 7. Unique Case Orientation: Each case in qualitative research is seen as unique, necessitating a thorough capture of details before exploring issues of transferability—the extent to which findings can be generalized or applied to other contexts or settings.
  • 8. Context Sensitivity: The social, historical, and temporal contexts of the research setting are important and need to be carefully considered. Transferability is approached with caution
  • 9. Subjective: Qualitative research focuses on seeking neutral understandings of individual participants, the research setting, and the self. Researchers aim to understand and interpret the subjective experiences of participants.
  • 10. Design Flexibility: Qualitative research allows for flexibility in research design, adapting to emerging discoveries and new insights.
Question 34
Given below are 2 Statements: (UGC NET 11 Nov 2020 Evening paper)Statement I:Qualitative research is an umbrella term to refer to various research strategies that share certain characteristics. The data collected have been termed 'soft' i.e. rich in description.Statement II:Quantitative research is mainly hypothetico deductive and employs mostly statistical techniques for data analysis.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:

  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is false
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is true
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true

Statement I state that qualitative research is an umbrella term that encompasses various research strategies sharing certain characteristics. The data collected in qualitative research are often described as 'soft' because they are rich in description, providing in-depth insights into the phenomenon being studied.

 

Statement II affirms that quantitative research is primarily hypothetico-deductive in nature. It formulates hypotheses based on existing theories and employs statistical techniques for data analysis. In quantitative research, researchers typically test theories and aim to draw objective conclusions from numerical data.

Question 36
Read the following statements – one labelled as Assertion “A” and the other as Reason “R”: (UGC NET Sep 2013)Assertion “A”:Qualitative research in India has a long way to go to reach international standards.Reason “R”:Because the funding agencies do not support qualitative research in academic institutions.Find the correct answer from the codes given below:
  • A.Both “A” and “R” are true and “R” is the correct explanation of “A”.
  • B.Both “A” and “R” are true, but “R” is not the correct explanation of “A”.
  • C.“A” is true, but “R” is false.
  • D.Both “A” and “R” are false.
Correct Answer: “A” is true, but “R” is false.

The assertion A is true, as qualitative research in India may still need further development and recognition to meet the standards set by international research. India's research publication output in both quantitative and qualitative research is increasing, but it may not have reached the same level as countries from North America, Europe, and the Pacific.

 

However, the reason R provided is false. While funding support can influence research initiatives, it is not the sole reason for the state of qualitative research in India. Funding agencies do invest in academic research programs, but other factors like the availability of highly specialized laboratory surroundings and the presence of skilled personnel also play crucial roles in the progress of qualitative research.

Question 37
Which among the following is NOT related to qualitative research? (UGC NET 04 Dec 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Thematic analysis
  • B.Case study
  • C.Discourse analysis
  • D.Survey method
Correct Answer: Survey method

(a) Thematic analysis: Thematic analysis is a method used in qualitative research to analyze textual data, such as interview transcripts or written documents. Researchers closely examine the data to identify recurring themes, patterns, and meanings, allowing for a deeper understanding of the subject of study.

 

(b) Case study: A case study is a qualitative research method commonly used in social sciences. It involves an in-depth examination of a specific subject, such as a person, group, place, event, organization, or phenomenon. Case studies provide detailed insights into the complexities and nuances of the chosen subject within its real-life context.

 

(c) Discourse analysis: Discourse analysis is another qualitative research method used to study written or spoken language in relation to its social context. Researchers analyze language use to understand how meaning is constructed and conveyed within specific social settings or interactions.

 

(d) Survey method: Unlike the other options, the survey method is NOT related to qualitative research. Surveys are a quantitative research tool used to collect data from a large number of respondents, typically through standardized questionnaires. Surveys aim to gather numerical data that can be analyzed statistically to identify patterns, trends, and relationships.

Question 38
Which of the following are characteristics of quantitative research? (UGC NET 24 Nov Evening)a. Questions are open‐ended.b. Identified variables are measured.c. Questions are standardized.d. If the sample size is large, the findings can be easily generalised.e. It is difficult to fix the level of measurement.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b and c only
  • B.b, c and d only
  • C.c, d and e only
  • D.a, c and e only
Correct Answer: b, c and d only

a. Identified variables are measured. - This is a characteristic of quantitative research. Quantitative research involves the collection of numerical data and the measurement of identified variables.

 

b. Questions are standardized. - This is a characteristic of quantitative research. In quantitative research, questions are typically structured and standardized to ensure consistency and comparability across participants or cases.

 

c. If the sample size is large, the findings can be easily generalized. - This is a characteristic of quantitative research. Large sample sizes in quantitative research increase the likelihood of generalizing the findings to the broader population from which the sample was drawn.

Question 39
Identify the key features of qualitative research: (UGC NET 04 Nov 2020 Evening paper)I. Actual settings as the source of dataII. Control, observe and measure as main operationsIII. Data take the forms of words or picturesIV. Concerned with participant perspectiveV. Hypothesis making and hypothesis testingChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.I, III, IV only
  • B.I, II, III only
  • C.II, III, IV only
  • D.III, IV, V only
Correct Answer: I, III, IV only

Qualitative research is a naturalistic inquiry that aims to gain in-depth understanding of social phenomena within their natural setting. It focuses on the "why" rather than the "what" of social phenomena and relies on the direct experiences of individuals as meaning-making agents in their everyday lives. Some key features of qualitative research are as follows:

 

a. Actual settings as the source of data: Qualitative research is conducted in real-world, naturalistic settings without manipulation or control. The researchers observe and gather data from the actual contexts where the phenomenon of interest occurs.

 

b. Control, observe, and measure as main operations: Unlike quantitative research, qualitative research does not primarily focus on control, observation, and measurement of variables. Instead, it emphasizes gaining insights through immersion and understanding of the subject matter.

 

c. Data take the forms of words or pictures: The fundamental element of analysis in qualitative research is words. Researchers use detailed and thick descriptions to capture the participants' perspectives. Sometimes, visual data like pictures or videos are also used to supplement the textual data.

 

d. Concerned with participant perspective: Qualitative research is centered on understanding the perspectives of the participants involved in the study. It seeks to capture their thoughts, feelings, and experiences related to the phenomenon being investigated.

 

e. Hypothesis making and hypothesis testing: Hypothesis making and formal hypothesis testing are not typical features of qualitative research. Instead, qualitative research focuses on generating rich and nuanced descriptions and explanations of social phenomena.

Question 40
Which of the following sequences correctly represents the steps of research using a quantitative paradigm? (UGC NET 13 Nov 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Hypothesis framing, Hypothesis testing, Conclusions and Reporting.
  • B.Establishing a research problem, Hypothesis framing, Hypothesis testing, Generalization and conclusions and Implications of results
  • C.Problem identification, Sample selection, Developing a research design and Field work.
  • D.Defining a problem, Survey of related studies, Sampling, Data collection and Data analysis
Correct Answer: Establishing a research problem, Hypothesis framing, Hypothesis testing, Generalization and conclusions and Implications of results

A quantitative research paradigm involves a structured and systematic approach to gather numerical data and analyze it using statistical methods. The correct sequence of steps for such research is as follows:

 

  • 1. Establishing a research problem: Identifying and defining a specific research question or problem that the study aims to address.
  • 2. Hypothesis framing: Formulating a clear and testable hypothesis or a set of hypotheses that provide potential answers to the research problem.
  • 3. Hypothesis testing: Collecting data and conducting statistical analysis to test the formulated hypotheses and determine whether they are supported or rejected by the data.
  • 4. Generalization and conclusions: Drawing general conclusions based on the results of the data analysis and discussing the findings in the context of the research problem.
  • 5. Implications of results: Discussing the practical implications of the research findings, potential applications, and their significance in the broader context.

 

Question 41
Which of the following are features of the qualitative research paradigm? (UGC NET 25 Sept 2020 Evening paper)A. The research is concerned with understanding the social phenomena from the participant's perspectiveB. It seeks to establish relationships, among variables and explains the causes of changes in measured social factsC. It is conducted in actual settings as the direct source of data and the researcher is the key instrumentD. It is concerned with the process rather than simply with outcomes or products E. It attempts to establish universal context free generalizationChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B and C only
  • B.B, C and D only
  • C.A, C and D only
  • D.C, D and E only
Correct Answer: A, C and D only

The features of the qualitative research are:

a. The qualitative research paradigm places a strong emphasis on understanding social phenomena from the perspectives of the participants involved. Researchers aim to explore the meanings, interpretations, and experiences of individuals or groups within their natural contexts. This approach allows for a comprehensive and nuanced understanding of the studied phenomena.

 

b. Qualitative research is typically conducted in actual settings where the phenomena occur. Researchers immerse themselves in the natural environments or social contexts to directly collect data. The researcher serves as a key instrument in the data collection process, meaning their interpretations, interactions, and subjectivity play a vital role in shaping the research.

 

c. The qualitative research paradigm is concerned with exploring the process of social phenomena, understanding how and why certain events or behaviors occur, rather than solely focusing on the final outcomes or products. This allows researchers to gain insights into the underlying dynamics and complexities of the studied phenomena.

Question 42
Which one of the following is the main feature of qualitative research? (UGC NET 20 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Avoids positivist assumptions and data analysis.
  • B.Subscribes to preexisting categories.
  • C.Collects data in numerical form.
  • D.Uses empirical method of data analysis.
Correct Answer: Avoids positivist assumptions and data analysis.

Qualitative research is a process of naturalistic inquiry that seeks to gain in-depth understanding of social phenomena within their natural setting. It focuses on exploring the "why" rather than the "what" of social phenomena and aims to understand the experiences and perspectives of individuals as meaning-making agents in their everyday lives.

 

In contrast to quantitative research, which relies on positivist assumptions that there is a single objective reality that can be measured and known through numerical data, qualitative research embraces a different paradigm. Qualitative researchers believe that reality is complex and context-dependent, and there is no single objective truth. They emphasize the need to understand the subjective interpretations and experiences of individuals to gain insights into the underlying meanings and motivations behind their actions.

 

Qualitative research involves methods such as interviews, observations, focus groups, and content analysis to collect rich, descriptive data. Researchers engage in an iterative process of data collection and analysis, constantly revisiting and refining their research questions based on emerging themes and patterns from the data.

Question 43
Which of the following are considered major types of qualitative research questions? (UGC NET 01 Mar 2023 Morning)A. Non-purposiveB. Causes and consequencesC. PredictiveD. EvaluativeE. Descriptive
  • A.A, B and C only
  • B.A, C and D only
  • C.A, D and E only
  • D.B, C, D and E only
Correct Answer: B, C, D and E only

a. Causes and Consequences: These questions aim to explore the factors or reasons (causes) behind a particular phenomenon and the potential outcomes or effects (consequences) it may have. Qualitative researchers might investigate the underlying causes and how they lead to specific consequences, providing a deeper understanding of complex social processes.

 

b. Predictive: Predictive questions are not typically associated with qualitative research. Instead, they are more aligned with quantitative research methods, where researchers use statistical analysis to make predictions based on numerical data. Qualitative research primarily seeks to understand and describe social phenomena rather than predict future outcomes.

 

c. Evaluative: Evaluative questions seek to assess the quality, effectiveness, or value of a particular program, intervention, policy, or phenomenon. Qualitative research can involve evaluating the success or impact of these elements by gathering rich, contextual data to form judgments and recommendations.

 

d. Descriptive: Descriptive questions focus on providing detailed descriptions or accounts of a particular phenomenon, setting, or group. Qualitative research excels in capturing the nuances, behaviors, and characteristics of a subject, offering a comprehensive portrayal that goes beyond mere statistics.

Question 44
Quantitative Research is also called the: (UGC NET 25 June 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Ethnographic Approach
  • B.Unstructured Approach
  • C.Descriptive Approach
  • D.Structured Approach
Correct Answer: Structured Approach

Quantitative research is characterized as a systematic investigation that involves gathering quantifiable data and utilizing statistical, mathematical, or computational techniques for analysis. It collects information through sampling methods, online surveys, polls, or questionnaires, and the results are presented in numerical form. Researchers carefully analyze these numbers to make predictions about the future of a product or service and make appropriate changes accordingly.

  • Ethnographic research is a qualitative method where researchers observe and interact with study participants in their real-life environment. It is widely used in social sciences, particularly anthropology.
  • An unstructured approach provides some guidelines and best practices but allows employees to collaborate and use internal tools and platforms in a relatively unregulated manner. It is also qualitative in nature.
  • Descriptive research is a type of research that describes a population, situation, or phenomenon being studied, focusing on answering questions such as how, what, when, and where. It is also a qualitative approach.
Question 45
The term ‘phenomenology’ is associated with the process of (UGC NET Dec 2010)
  • A.Qualitative Research
  • B.Analysis of Variance
  • C.Correlational Study
  • D.Probability Sampling
Correct Answer: Qualitative Research

Phenomenology is a research approach based on the academic disciplines of philosophy and psychology. It is widely accepted as a qualitative research method that aims to describe and understand how human beings experience a certain phenomenon. In phenomenological research, the focus is on exploring the subjective experiences, perceptions, and meanings that individuals ascribe to a particular situation or event.

Question 46
Identify the characteristic features of ‘Hypothetico‐deductive research’ paradigm: (UGC NET 21 Nov Evening 2021)a. Researcher is detached from the study to avoid bias.b. Researcher becomes immersed in the research situation present or past.c. The researcher seeks to establish relationships and explains causes of changes in measured social facts.d. Actual settings are the direct source of data.e. An attempt is made to set up universal context free generalizations.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b and c only
  • B.b, c and d only
  • C.a, c and e only
  • D.c, d and e only
Correct Answer: a, c and e only

a. Researcher is detached from the study to avoid bias - This characteristic does not align with the hypothetico-deductive research paradigm. In hypothetico-deductive research, the researcher actively engages in formulating hypotheses and designing experiments to test those hypotheses. While the researcher maintains objectivity in data collection and analysis, they are not detached from the study.

 

b. The researcher seeks to establish relationships and explains causes of changes in measured social facts - This characteristic is a fundamental feature of the hypothetico-deductive research paradigm. In this approach, the researcher formulates hypotheses and designs experiments to test the relationships between variables and establish causality.

 

c. An attempt is made to set up universal context-free generalizations - This characteristic does not align with the hypothetico-deductive research paradigm. Hypothetico-deductive research focuses on testing specific hypotheses and making inferences about particular relationships between variables, rather than seeking universal generalizations.

Question 47
Which of the following is not the critical feature of qualitative research? (UGC NET Aug 2016)
  • A.Actual settings are the direct source of data.
  • B.Data take the forms of words or pictures.
  • C.Seeking to establish relationships among measured social facts.
  • D.Researcher becomes immersed in the situation, present or past related to the phenomena.
Correct Answer: Seeking to establish relationships among measured social facts.

The critical feature of qualitative research is to gain insights into attitudes, beliefs, motivations, and behaviors of individuals to explore a social or human problem. Qualitative research involves methods such as focus groups, in-depth interviews, observation research, and case studies.

 

Seeking to establish relationships among measured social facts: This statement is not a critical feature of qualitative research. Rather, it is more relevant to quantitative research, which aims to establish relationships among measured variables using statistical analyses.tical test: After implementing the above procedures, researchers use statistical tests to analyze the data and determine the significance of the relationship between the independent and dependent variables. Statistical tests help identify if the observed effects are likely due to the manipulation of the independent variable rather than chance.

Question 48
Both qualitative and quantitative research are concerned with: (UGC NET 01 Oct 2022 Evening)
  • A.Data reduction
  • B.Artificial settings
  • C.Uniformity of data.
  • D.Social fantasy
Correct Answer: Data reduction

Data reduction refers to the process of organizing, summarizing, and analyzing large volumes of data to identify patterns, trends, and key insights. In both qualitative and quantitative research, researchers collect extensive data related to their research questions or objectives. However, this data can be vast and complex, making it essential to reduce or condense it into manageable and meaningful information.

  • In qualitative research, data reduction involves techniques such as thematic analysis, coding, and categorization to identify recurring themes and patterns in the data.
  • In quantitative research, data reduction involves statistical techniques that summarize and analyze data, such as mean, median, standard deviation, and regression analysis.

Both qualitative and quantitative researchers engage in data reduction to draw meaningful conclusions and address their research objectives effectively.

Question 49
When it comes to data arrangement, qualitative research - must guard against the error of: (UGC NET 11 July 2022 Evening)
  • A.Segregation
  • B.Reduction
  • C.Expansion
  • D.Control
Correct Answer: Segregation

In qualitative research, data arrangement involves organizing and structuring the collected data for analysis and interpretation. Researchers must be cautious to avoid the error of segregation in this process.

Segregation refers to the practice of isolating or separating data into distinct categories or groups without considering the interconnectedness or interrelationships between different data points. This can lead to oversimplification and loss of context, potentially resulting in a superficial understanding of the research phenomenon.

 

In qualitative research, the goal is to explore the complexities and nuances of the data to gain deeper insights. Researchers should avoid segregating data and instead focus on identifying themes, patterns, and connections that emerge from the data as a whole.

By maintaining a holistic and inclusive approach to data arrangement, qualitative researchers can ensure a comprehensive understanding of the research subject and avoid the error of segregation.

Question 50
The quantitative research is based on: (UGC NET 20 Oct 2022 Evening)
  • A.Reductionism
  • B.Grounded theory
  • C.Field notes
  • D.Expansionism
Correct Answer: Reductionism

Quantitative research is based on reductionism. Reductionism is the philosophical approach of breaking down complex phenomena into simpler and more manageable components. In quantitative research, researchers use measurable variables and numerical data to analyze and test relationships between variables. This involves breaking down complex social or natural phenomena into quantifiable units that can be easily analyzed using statistical methods.

 

Quantitative research aims to establish cause-and-effect relationships, and reductionism helps researchers isolate specific variables and control for confounding factors to identify the relationship between the variables of interest.

  • Grounded theory: Grounded theory is a qualitative research methodology that involves generating theories and concepts based on empirical data, whereas quantitative research focuses on testing hypotheses using numerical data.
  • Field notes: Field notes are records made by researchers during qualitative research, typically involving observations, interviews, or interactions in the research setting. Field notes are associated with qualitative methods rather than quantitative research.
  • Expansionism: Expansionism is not directly related to quantitative research. It is a concept related to political or economic ideologies, but it does not represent the basis of quantitative research.
Question 51
Qualitative researchers criticize quantitative research for its tendency towards: (UGC NET 20 Dec 2018 Evening)
  • A.Reductionism
  • B.Emphasis on Evidence
  • C.Obsession with Creativity
  • D.Focus on Empiricism
Correct Answer: Reductionism

Qualitative researchers criticize quantitative research for its tendency towards reductionism. Reductionism in quantitative research refers to the practice of breaking down complex phenomena into simpler, measurable variables and focusing on isolated aspects of the research subject. This reductionist approach may overlook the broader context and intricate interconnections that qualitative research aims to capture. Qualitative researchers argue that reductionism limits the understanding of complex social phenomena and may lead to oversimplification of reality. They advocate for a more holistic and in-depth exploration of the social world, which is characteristic of qualitative research methods.

Question 1
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 14 Mar 2023 Evening)Statement I:Coding is an important process in grounded theory in which data are classified into well- defined categories.Statement II:The researchers interpretations decide his or her emergent codes in grounded theory, and different types of coding are identified.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:Both Statement I and Statement II are true.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Statement I: Coding is an important process in grounded theory in which data are classified into well-defined categories. In grounded theory, coding is a fundamental step where researchers systematically analyze and classify data into categories or codes that emerge from the data itself. It's a key process in the development of theory.

 

Statement II: The researcher's interpretations decide his or her emergent codes in grounded theory, and different types of coding are identified. Grounded theory allows for different types of coding, such as open coding, axial coding, and selective coding. The researcher's interpretations and analysis of the data guide the emergence of these codes and categories, which are not predetermined but rather emerge during the research process.

Question 2
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 11 Mar 2023 Morning)Statement I:In experimental research, we cannot eliminate extraneous factors that influence the outcome.Statement II:In survey research, a vast amount of rich and diverse data can be collected.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Statement I is false but Statement II is true.

Statement I: This statement is false. In experimental research, researchers use various techniques such as randomization, control groups, and manipulation of variables to minimize the influence of extraneous factors (also known as confounding variables) and enhance the internal validity of the study. While it's challenging to eliminate all extraneous factors, experimental design aims to control and minimize their impact.

 

Statement II: This statement is true. Survey research allows researchers to collect a vast amount of data from a large and diverse sample of participants. Surveys can gather information on a wide range of topics, making it a valuable method for exploring and understanding various issues.

Question 3

  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Statement I is true but Statement II is false.

Statement I is true. One of the advantages of survey research is the ability to sample a large number of respondents, which can provide valuable data for analysis and generalization.

 

Statement II is false. Researchers have multiple options for administering surveys, including online surveys, mail surveys, telephone surveys, and in-person surveys. While researchers can choose to administer surveys themselves, they also have the option to use various survey administration methods or platforms, depending on their research goals and resources.
