Question 5
Which of the following are experimental manipulations? (UGC NET 15 Mar 2023 Morning)A. Environmental manipulationB. Stimulus manipulationC. Instructional manipulationD. Planning manipulationE. Decision manipulationChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B and C only
  • B.B, C and D only
  • C.C, D and E only
  • D.A, D and E only
Correct Answer: A, B and C only

Experimental manipulations typically involve altering certain aspects of the experimental environment or conditions to observe their effects on the variables of interest.

a. Environmental manipulation: This is a common experimental manipulation where the researcher changes the environmental conditions to study their impact on the dependent variables.

b. Stimulus manipulation: This involves altering the stimuli or inputs that participants are exposed to as part of the experiment. It's a form of manipulation often used in psychology and sensory perception studies.

c. Instructional manipulation: This manipulation involves providing specific instructions or information to participants to influence their behavior or responses during the experiment.

Question 6
When knowledge becomes replicable and verifiable, it is then called (UGC NET 05 Mar 2023 Morning)
  • A.Humanistic
  • B.Impressionistic
  • C.Scientific
  • D.Subjective
Correct Answer: Scientific

When knowledge becomes replicable and verifiable, it is considered to be following the principles of the scientific method. Scientific knowledge is characterized by its reliance on empirical evidence, systematic observation, experimentation, and the ability to be tested and verified by others. It aims to be objective and free from personal bias, making it replicable and verifiable.

Question 7
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 28 Mar 2023 Evening)Statement I:Applied research is concerned with generalization and the formulation of theory.Statement II:Fundamental research aims at finding a solution for an immediate problem facing a society.In light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect

Statement I: "Applied research is concerned with generalization and the formulation of theory."

This statement is incorrect. Applied research is typically focused on addressing practical, real-world issues and finding solutions to specific problems. It aims to provide practical solutions or recommendations rather than generalizing findings into theories.

 

Statement II: "Fundamental research aims at finding a solution for an immediate problem facing a society." This statement is incorrect. Fundamental research, often referred to as basic or pure research, is primarily concerned with advancing scientific knowledge and understanding fundamental principles. It is not typically focused on finding immediate solutions to societal problems.

Question 8
When a researcher has no control over the variables; he she can only report what has happened or what is happening. Such research is called as: (UGC NET 28 Mar 2023 Morning)
  • A.Clinical Research
  • B.Diagnostic Research
  • C.Ex post facto research
  • D.De facto research
Correct Answer: Ex post facto research

Ex post facto research, also known as retrospective research or causal-comparative research, is a type of non-experimental research design. In this approach, researchers observe and analyze pre-existing conditions or events to understand their effects on a particular outcome or phenomenon. The key characteristics of ex post facto research include:

a. No Control over Variables: Researchers do not manipulate or control the independent variables in ex post facto research. Instead, they observe and analyze variables as they naturally occur or have occurred in the past.

 

b. Observational and Descriptive: Ex post facto research is primarily observational and descriptive in nature. Researchers collect data by observing or measuring variables without introducing interventions.

 

c. Retrospective Analysis: The research design often involves a retrospective analysis of historical data or existing conditions. Researchers may examine past records, surveys, or archival data to draw conclusions.

 

d. Causality Inference: While ex post facto research can identify associations or correlations between variables, it is limited in establishing causality. It can suggest relationships between variables but cannot prove cause-and-effect relationships.

 

e. Use of Control Groups: Researchers may use control groups or comparison groups to make meaningful comparisons between different conditions or groups.

 

f. Exploratory and Hypothesis-Generating: Ex post facto research is often used in exploratory research to generate hypotheses or initial insights into potential causal relationships.

 

g. Common in Social Sciences: This research design is commonly used in social sciences, psychology, education, and health-related fields to study factors like the impact of socioeconomic status on educational achievement or the effects of a historical event on a population's health.

Question 9
In participant observation, the researcher has to act as a: (UGC NET10 Oct 2022 Morning)
  • A.Professional organiser
  • B.Professional stranger
  • C.Professional publicist
  • D.Cultural agent
Correct Answer: Professional stranger

In participant observation, the researcher immerses themselves in the social setting or group being studied and actively participates in their activities. However, the researcher must maintain a sense of detachment and objectivity to accurately observe and record the behavior, interactions, and culture of the group. By acting as a "professional stranger," the researcher maintains an outsider's perspective while being actively present within the group, allowing them to observe and understand the group's dynamics and behavior more effectively. This approach helps researchers avoid becoming too embedded or biased in the group, ensuring the credibility and validity of the observations made during participant observation.

Question 10
In case the focus of research is to improve a school in which students are participants and research supervisors are teachers, such research is termed as: (UGC NET 14 Mar 2023 Morning)
  • A.Basic research
  • B.Traditional research
  • C.Supervisory research
  • D.Action research
Correct Answer: Action research

Action research is a form of applied research that is conducted in real-world settings, often by practitioners or professionals, to address specific issues or problems within their own context. In this case, teachers (research supervisors) are actively involved in conducting research to bring about improvements in the school environment and educational outcomes for students. It emphasizes practical solutions and actionable findings that can lead to positive changes.

Question 11
The ethnographic research is mostly conducted in: (UGC NET 13 Mar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Simulated environment
  • B.Natural environment
  • C.Virtual environment only
  • D.Artificial environment
Correct Answer: Natural environment

Ethnographic research involves the systematic observation and study of people and cultures in their natural or real-life settings. Researchers immerse themselves in the field of study, typically spending extended periods in the actual environments and communities they are researching. This approach allows them to gain in-depth insights into the culture, behavior, and social interactions of the people being studied in their natural context. Conducting ethnographic research in a natural environment is essential for understanding the nuances of human behavior and culture as they occur in everyday life.

Question 12

  • A.Case studies
  • B.Applied research
  • C.Textual analysis
  • D.Phenomenology

This often involves collaboration with stakeholders or participants who have a vested interest in the research outcomes. Their insights, perspectives, and input are valuable during the interpretation phase to ensure that the research findings are relevant and actionable in practical settings.

Question 13

Question 14

A case study is a research method where a researcher closely examines one or a few subjects or cases in great detail. It involves a comprehensive and detailed exploration of a specific individual, group, or situation. Case studies are often used to gain a deep understanding of unique or complex phenomena.

 

B. Observational Research - II. Study of behaviors in their natural settings without intervention

Observational research involves observing and recording behaviors, events, or phenomena as they naturally occur in their real-world settings. Researchers do not intervene or manipulate variables but rather act as passive observers. This method is often used to study human or animal behavior in its natural context.

 

C. Longitudinal Research - IV. Study in which a group of participants is observed and measured over time.

Longitudinal research involves studying a group of participants over an extended period, often years or even decades. Researchers collect data at multiple points in time to track changes, trends, or developments within the group. This approach is valuable for understanding how variables evolve over time.

 

D. Experimental Research - I. Variables are actively manipulated, and the environment is controlled as possible.

Experimental research is a controlled research method where researchers actively manipulate one or more independent variables to observe their effects on dependent variables while controlling for other factors. This type of research is conducted in controlled environments to establish cause-and-effect relationships.

Question 17
When in a process of reasoning observation is followed by theory, hypotheses and interpretation, that approach to research is known as (UGC NET 02 Mar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Formulative
  • B.Standardised
  • C.Inductive
  • D.Deductive

Question 18
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 13 Mar 2023 Evening)Statement I:Operational definitions are used to get the meaning of abstract concepts.Statement II:Operational definitions do not define how a variable is measured.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement l and Statement II are correct.
  • B.Both Statement l and Statement II are incorrect.
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.
Correct Answer: Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.

Statement I: This statement is correct. Operational definitions are used in research to provide clear and specific definitions for abstract or complex concepts, allowing researchers to measure and manipulate these concepts in a concrete and practical way. Operational definitions help translate abstract ideas into observable and measurable variables.

 

Statement II: This statement is incorrect. Operational definitions do define how a variable is measured. They specify the procedures, methods, or criteria used to measure or manipulate a variable. Operational definitions provide the practical details needed to ensure consistency and accuracy in research measurements.

Question 19
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 15 Mar 2023 Morning)Statement I:The conceptual variable to be converted into a scientifically researchable variable involves redefining the abstraction of a conceptual variable into an empirical one.Statement II:Clear and detailed procedures and instruments to make the actual observations should be specified so that other researchers/scientists do not duplicate the observations.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Statement I is true but Statement II is false.

Statement I: This statement is correct. In research, conceptual variables often represent abstract ideas or concepts that need to be translated into measurable and observable variables. This process involves defining and operationalizing the conceptual variables so that they can be studied empirically. Researchers must establish clear definitions and measures for these variables to make them researchable.

 

Statement II: This statement is not accurate. While it's essential to specify clear procedures and instruments for research, the primary purpose is not to prevent duplication by other researchers. Instead, it ensures that research is conducted systematically, consistently, and with transparency. This clarity in methodology helps researchers obtain reliable and replicable results and allows other scholars to understand and potentially replicate the study to validate its findings. The main goal is to maintain the scientific rigor of the research, not to prevent duplication.

Question 20
In correlational research, a dependent variable is also referred to as (UGC NET 13 Mar 2023 Morning)
  • A.Predictor variable
  • B.Critical variable
  • C.Criterion variable
  • D.Extraneous variable
Correct Answer: Criterion variable

The dependent variable in correlational research is the one that is being studied or predicted based on its relationship with one or more independent variables (predictor variables). It is often called the criterion variable because researchers are interested in understanding how changes in the independent variables may predict or relate to variations in the dependent variable.

Question 21
In much of social research, the variables used are (UGC NET 12 Mar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Manipulable
  • B.Experimental
  • C.Non-manipulable
  • D.Deviational
Correct Answer: Non-manipulable

Non-manipulable variables, also known as non-experimental or non-manipulated variables, are characteristics or attributes that researchers cannot directly manipulate or control. In social research, many variables, such as demographic traits, attitudes, beliefs, or historical events, are non-manipulable because researchers cannot change them experimentally. Instead, researchers observe and analyze these variables as they naturally occur.

Question 22
An example of participant or subject variable can be (UGC NET 11 Mar 2023 Morning)
  • A.Time order
  • B.Recollection
  • C.Political affiliation of a person
  • D.Manipulation
Correct Answer: Political affiliation of a person

A participant or subject variable in research refers to a characteristic or trait of an individual participant in a study that is not manipulated by the researcher. In this case, the political affiliation of a person is an example of a participant variable because it is an inherent characteristic of the individual and is not subject to manipulation by the researcher. Time order, recollection, and manipulation are not examples of participant variables.

Question 23
Which of the following are types of error in Survey research? (UGC NET 29 Oct 2022 Evening)a. Sample errorb. Source errorc. Observational errord. Data collection errore. Data processing errorChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, c only
  • B.b, c, d only
  • C.b, d, e only
  • D.a, d, e only
Correct Answer: a, d, e only

a. Sample error: This is a type of error that occurs due to the variability between the characteristics of the sample and the characteristics of the population it represents. It is also known as sampling error.

 

b. Data collection error: This is a type of error that occurs during the process of collecting data, such as errors in recording responses, interviewer bias, or non-response bias.

 

c. Data processing error: This is a type of error that occurs during the data processing phase, such as errors in data entry, data coding, or data analysis.

Question 24
When original participants in a longitudinal study drop out midway, it is called: (UGC NET 11 July 2022 Morning)
  • A.Experimental distancing
  • B.Respondent deviation
  • C.Mortality
  • D.Sample redundancy
Correct Answer: Mortality

When original participants in a longitudinal study drop out midway, it is referred to as "mortality" or "experimental mortality." Mortality occurs when participants leave the study before it is completed, leading to a reduction in the sample size over time. It can be caused by various factors, such as loss of interest, inability to continue participation, or changes in circumstances.

 

Mortality can be a significant concern in longitudinal studies because it may introduce bias and affect the generalizability of the results. Researchers often use various strategies to handle mortality, such as conducting follow-up assessments, using statistical methods to account for missing data, or recruiting new participants to replace those who dropped out.

Question 25
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 23 Oct 2022 Morning)Statement I:In historical research, external criticism is necessary to establish the authenticity of data.Statement II:Various tests of authenticity are there in historical research but there is no need to use them.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Statement I is true but Statement II is false.

Statement I: External criticism is a critical aspect of historical research. It involves the evaluation and verification of the authenticity of historical sources and data. Historians need to examine the external characteristics of the sources, such as their origin, authorship, date, and context, to establish their credibility and reliability. By subjecting the sources to external criticism, historians can ensure that the data they use in their research is trustworthy and accurate.

 

Statement II: This statement is false. Various tests and methods of authenticity are essential in historical research to ensure the reliability of historical sources. Historians use techniques such as source triangulation, internal consistency checks, cross-referencing with other sources, and contextual analysis to assess the authenticity of the data they work with. Using these tests is necessary to avoid relying on inaccurate or misleading information in historical research.

Question 26
Which of the following are the actions of an ethnographic researcher? (UGC NET 08 Oct 2022 Morning)a. He gets immersed in the Social Setting.b. He avoids Collecting documents about the group members he is researching upon.c. He observes the behaviour of group members.d. He listens to their conversation.e.   • B.a, c, d only
  • C.b, c, d only
  • D.c, d, e only

a. He gets immersed in the Social Setting - This is a fundamental action of an ethnographic researcher. Ethnographic researchers immerse themselves in the social setting they are studying, often for an extended period. This immersive approach allows them to gain a deep understanding of the culture, behavior, and interactions of the group being researched.

 

b. He observes the behavior of group members - This is a key action of an ethnographic researcher. Researchers carefully observe and record the actions, interactions, and activities of the participants within their natural setting.

 

c. He listens to their conversation - This is another essential action of an ethnographic researcher. Listening to the conversations and interactions of the group members helps the researcher understand their communication patterns, language use, and social dynamics.

Question 27
The characteristics of experimental studies are: (UGC NET 21 Oct 2022 Morning)a. Absence of researcher's bias.b. Absence of conditioned environment.c. Evidence of causality.d. Control of experimental elements.e. Possibility of replication.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b and c only
  • B.b, c and d only
  • C.a, c and d only
  • D.c, d and e only
Correct Answer: c, d and e only

a. Evidence of causality - This is a key characteristic of experimental studies. The experimental design allows researchers to establish cause-and-effect relationships between variables, providing strong evidence of causality.

 

b. Control of experimental elements - This is an essential characteristic of experimental studies. Researchers carefully control and manipulate the independent variable(s) to isolate their effects on the dependent variable(s) while minimizing the influence of other factors.

 

c. Possibility of replication - Experimental studies are designed to be replicable. Replication allows other researchers to repeat the experiment with the same or similar methods and conditions to verify the findings and enhance the credibility of the study.

Question 28
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 21 Oct 2022 Morning)List I (Method)a. Case Studyb. Longitudinal Studyc. Snap-shotd. Question 29
The advantages of research based on field experiments are: (UGC NET 29 Oct 2022 Morning)a. A strong external validityb. Subjects behave normally and naturally.c. The experiment takes place in a natural setting.d. Generation of primary data.e. Non-requirement of elaborate logistics.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:

  • B.b, c and d only
  • C.c, d and e only
  • D.a, e and e only
Correct Answer: b, c and d only

a. Subjects behave normally and naturally - This is a key advantage of field experiments. In field experiments, participants are observed in their natural environment, leading to more genuine and realistic behavior compared to laboratory settings.

 

b. The experiment takes place in a natural setting - This is another advantage of field experiments. Researchers conduct field experiments in real-world settings, which enhances the ecological validity of the study and allows for a better understanding of how the variables interact in a natural context.

 

c. Generation of primary data - Field experiments involve direct data collection from the participants in the real setting, leading to the generation of primary data. This is valuable as it ensures that the data collected is specific to the research question and context.

Question 30
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET11 July 2022 Morning)List I (Types of Research)a. Applied researchb. Basic researchc. Quantitative researchd. Qualitative researchList II (Research Purpose)i. Exploration and description of concepts.ii. To focus on objective assessment.iii. Contribution to knowledge.iv. To find practical solutions to everyday issues.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.a- i, b- ii, c- iv, d- iii

  • C.a- iii, b- iv, c- i, d- ii
  • D.a- ii, b- i, c- iii, d- iv
Correct Answer: a- iv, b- iii, c- ii, d- i

a. Applied research - (iv) To find practical solutions to everyday issues.

Applied research aims to solve real-world problems and provide practical solutions that can be directly applied to everyday issues or challenges.

 

b. Basic research - (iii) Contribution to knowledge.

Basic research, also known as pure or fundamental research, is conducted to expand existing knowledge and understanding of various phenomena without any immediate practical application in mind.

 

c. Quantitative research - (ii) To focus on objective assessment.

Quantitative research involves the systematic collection and analysis of numerical data to quantify relationships and patterns between variables. It focuses on objective assessment and relies on statistical analysis for interpretation.

 

d. Qualitative research - (i) Exploration and description of concepts.

Qualitative research is used to explore and describe complex phenomena, concepts, or experiences in-depth, often using methods such as interviews, observations, and open-ended surveys to gather rich, non-numerical data.

Question 31
Virtual ethnography is located in a/an: (UGC NET14 Oct 2022 Evening)
  • A.Natural environment
  • B.Technical environment
  • C.Political environment
  • D.Economic environment
Correct Answer: Technical environment

Virtual ethnography is a research approach that involves conducting ethnographic studies in online or digital environments. It is situated in the technical environment because it utilizes various digital tools, platforms, and technologies to observe and interact with individuals or communities in virtual spaces. Researchers in virtual ethnography use online forums, social media, virtual communities, or other digital platforms to gather data and study social interactions, behaviors, and cultures in these digital spaces. The technical environment plays a crucial role in facilitating data collection, analysis, and communication in virtual ethnography.

Question 32
Relics such as fingerprints are considered credible by which of the following Research methodology? (UGC NET14 Oct 2022 Morning)
  • A.Experimental
  • B.Quantitative
  • C.Historical
  • D.Descriptive
Correct Answer: Historical

Relics such as fingerprints are considered credible in the context of historical research methodology. Historical research involves the systematic collection, analysis, and interpretation of past events, actions, and phenomena to understand their significance and relevance. In historical research, relics, artifacts, documents, and other sources from the past are examined to reconstruct historical events and gain insights into historical processes.

 

Fingerprints, as relics, can be valuable in historical research when studying ancient civilizations, historical figures, or events from the past. They serve as tangible evidence of past individuals and their activities, contributing to a more comprehensive understanding of historical contexts and occurrences. Historical researchers use various relics, including fingerprints, as credible sources to validate their findings and draw conclusions about past societies and cultures.

Question 33
Which of the following are true in the case of participatory observation method? (UGC NET 20 Oct2022Morning)a. The apparently obvious incidents can be overlooked.b.   • C.c, d and e only

a. It is a good method to study the daily operations of organizations - This statement is true. Participatory observation is an excellent method for studying the daily operations, routines, and practices within organizations. By being actively involved in the organization, the researcher gains firsthand experience and insights into the day-to-day activities and dynamics of the group.

 

b. The decision-making process can be observed - This statement is true. Question 34
Which of the following are excluded in scientific research? (UGC NET10 Oct 2022 Morning)a. Empiricismb. Removal of errors.c. Subjectivityd. Unethical practicese. Non-predictive inferences.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, c only
  • B.b, c, d only
  • C.c, d, e only
  • D.a, c, e only
Correct Answer: c, d, e only

In scientific research, certain aspects are excluded to ensure the rigor, validity, and ethical integrity of the study. The excluded aspects are as follows:

 

a. Subjectivity - Scientific research aims to minimize subjectivity and bias in the data collection, analysis, and interpretation process. Researchers strive to use objective methods and measures to obtain reliable and valid results.

 

b. Unethical practices - Ethical considerations are paramount in scientific research. Unethical practices, such as deception of participants, invasion of privacy, or harm to subjects, are strictly excluded in scientific research.

 

c. Non-predictive inferences - Scientific research emphasizes making testable and predictive inferences based on empirical evidence. Non-predictive inferences or speculative conclusions without empirical support are excluded in scientific research.

Question 36
Which of the following are the characteristics of case study research? (UGC NET10 Oct 2022 Evening)a. It is simulated in a laboratory.b. It is particularistic.c. It is descriptive.d. It is inductive.e. It is disruptive.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b and c only
  • B.b, c and d only
  • C.c, d and e only
  • D.a, b and e only
Correct Answer: b, c and d only

a. It is particularistic - This statement is true. Case study research focuses on studying specific individuals, groups, organizations, or events in detail. It seeks to understand the unique characteristics and specific context of the case under investigation.

 

b. It is descriptive - This statement is true. Case study research is often descriptive in nature, aiming to provide a comprehensive and detailed account of the phenomenon being studied. It involves the collection and analysis of qualitative data to describe the case's characteristics, behaviors, and interactions.

 

c. It is inductive - This statement is true. Case study research often follows an inductive approach, where researchers generate theories or generalizations based on the specific observations and data collected from the case. It involves building explanations and theories from the ground up based on the detailed examination of the case.

Question 37
Population census can be an example of: (UGC NET10 Oct 2022 Evening)
  • A.Historical Study
  • B.Case Study
  • C.Longitudinal Study
  • D.Experimental Study
Correct Answer: Longitudinal Study

Population census can be considered an example of a longitudinal study. Longitudinal studies involve collecting data from the same group of individuals or subjects over an extended period, often at multiple time points. In the case of a population census, data is collected from the entire population of a country or region at regular intervals, usually every ten years.

 

The purpose of a longitudinal study, such as a population census, is to track changes and trends in the population over time. By collecting data at different points in time, researchers can observe how various demographic, social, and economic characteristics of the population evolve and change over the years.

Question 39
Which of the following are the products of grounded theory? (UGC NET01 Oct 2022 Evening)a. Experimental frameworkb. Conceptsc. Hypothesesd. Attributes of a category.e. Theoretical dilutionChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b and c only
  • B.b, c and d only
  • C.c, d and e only
  • D.a, b and e only
Correct Answer: b, c and d only

a. Concepts - This statement is true. In grounded theory, one of the main products is the development of concepts. Concepts are abstract ideas or categories that emerge from the data during the process of constant comparison and theoretical coding. These concepts represent key themes, patterns, or phenomena that are relevant to the research question.

 

b. Hypotheses - This statement is true. Grounded theory often leads to the formulation of hypotheses. These hypotheses are not derived from pre-existing theories but are developed from the emergent concepts and relationships identified in the data.

 

c. Attributes of a category - This statement is true. Grounded theory involves the development of categories, and each category is characterized by its attributes or defining characteristics. These attributes help to define and distinguish one category from another.

Question 40
Which one of the following is a tool of grounded theory? (UGC NET08 Oct 2022 Morning)
  • A.Constant comparison
  • B.Auditing
  • C.Deconstruction of narratives.
  • D.Use of uncritical language.
Correct Answer: Constant comparison

Grounded theory is a qualitative research method that aims to develop theories or explanations from the data itself, rather than starting with pre-existing theories. The process of constant comparison is a central tool of grounded theory. In constant comparison, researchers compare data points, categories, and incidents to identify patterns, similarities, and differences. This iterative process helps researchers to refine and develop concepts and categories that emerge from the data.

Question 41
Which of the following are sources of data in historical research? (UGC NET08 Oct 2022 Morning)a. Personal observationb. Focused group discussionc. Oral testimonyd. Relicse. ActuariesChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, c only
  • B.b, c, d only
  • C.a, c, d only
  • D.c, d, e only
Correct Answer: c, d, e only

a. Oral testimony is an important source of data in historical research, especially when studying events or experiences that may not be well-documented in written records. Oral histories and interviews with individuals who have firsthand knowledge of historical events can provide valuable insights.

 

b. Relics refer to physical artifacts, objects, or remains from the past. Historical research often involves the examination and analysis of relics to gain insights into past cultures, societies, and events.

 

c. Actuaries are records or documents that provide information about past events, transactions, or activities. These may include official records, legal documents, financial records, and other written sources that provide data for historical research.

Question 42
Coding paradigm is extensively used in: (UGC NET01 Oct 2022 Morning)
  • A.Language analysis
  • B.Conversational analysis
  • C.Grounded theory research
  • D.Covert observation
Correct Answer: Grounded theory research

The coding paradigm is extensively used in Grounded Theory research. Grounded Theory is a qualitative research approach developed by sociologists Barney Glaser and Anselm Strauss. It aims to build theories directly from the data without starting with preconceived hypotheses.

 

In Grounded Theory, coding is a crucial process that involves systematically analyzing qualitative data (such as interviews, observations, or documents) to identify concepts, categories, and relationships that emerge from the data itself. The coding paradigm in Grounded Theory involves the following key steps:

  • Open Coding: In the initial stage, researchers engage in open coding, where they break down the data into smaller segments and assign descriptive codes to these segments. This process allows researchers to identify the main ideas and concepts present in the data.
  • Axial Coding: After open coding, researchers move to axial coding, where they explore the relationships between the codes and start organizing them into broader categories. Axial coding helps to uncover the connections and interactions between the concepts.
  • Selective Coding: In the final stage, researchers engage in selective coding, where they refine and integrate the categories into a coherent theory. The goal is to develop a core category or central theme that explains the main phenomenon under investigation.

By using the coding paradigm, Grounded Theory researchers can build theories that are directly grounded in the data, allowing for rich and nuanced understandings of the phenomena being studied.

 

In contrast, the other options mentioned are not necessarily centered around the coding paradigm:

Language analysis: While coding may be used in some language analysis methods, it is not exclusive to this field. Language analysis encompasses a broad range of approaches that study language in various contexts.

Conversational analysis: Conversational analysis primarily focuses on the systematic analysis of naturally occurring conversations to understand the structure and organization of talk in interaction.

Covert observation: Covert observation involves observing participants without their knowledge or consent. While data from covert observation can be analyzed using coding techniques, the use of coding is not unique to covert observation studies.

Question 43
When a variable leads to a spurious interpretation of research results, it is called: (UGC NET 12 July 2022 Morning)
  • A.Control variable
  • B.External variable
  • C.Conflicting variable
  • D.Confounding variable
Correct Answer: Confounding variable

Confounding variables are extraneous variables that are not of primary interest in the study but are related to both the dependent variable and the independent variable. They can create a false or misleading association between the variables being studied and may lead to incorrect conclusions. Controlling for confounding variables is essential in research to ensure that the relationship between the variables of interest is accurately assessed.

Question 44
The 'Age' of a respondent is an example of: (UGC NET 12 July 2022 Morning)
  • A.Parallel variable
  • B.Monadic variable
  • C.Dyadic variable
  • D.Simple variable
Correct Answer: Monadic variable

Monadic variables are those that involve single elements or individuals, and 'Age' is a characteristic that can be measured for each individual respondent in a study without any comparison or pairing with other respondents. It is a basic or simple variable that stands on its own without any relational aspect.

Question 45
Which of the following techniques are used to control extraneous variables in research? (UGC NET 05 Jan Evening 2022)a. Change of instrument.b. Randomisationc. Matchingd. Removing variables.e. Changing the research method.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, c only
  • B.b, c, d only
  • C.c, d, e only
  • D.a, b, e only
Correct Answer: b, c, d only

Techniques used to control extraneous variables in research are:

a. Randomisation: Random assignment of participants or treatments to different groups helps ensure that extraneous variables are equally distributed among the groups, reducing their impact on the results.

b. Matching: Matching participants in different groups based on certain characteristics helps to ensure that those groups are equivalent with respect to those characteristics, thus controlling for their influence on the results.

c. Removing variables: Researchers can control for extraneous variables by removing their influence from the data analysis. This can be done through statistical techniques like regression analysis, where the effects of extraneous variables are accounted for.

Question 46
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 05 Jan Morning 2022)List I (Variables)a. Independentb. Dependentc. Controld. DiscreteList II (Characteristic features)i. Can be used to divide subjects into specific categories.ii. Cannot be divided into subparts.iii. Represents the cause.iv. The variable that is affected.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.a- i, b- ii, c- iii, d- iv
  • B.a- ii, b- iii, c- iv, d- i
  • C.a- iii, b- iv, c- i, d- ii
  • D.a- iv, b- i, c- ii, d- iii
Correct Answer: a- iii, b- iv, c- i, d- ii

a. Independent Variable: This is the variable that is manipulated or controlled by the researcher. It represents the cause in an experiment and is expected to have an effect on the dependent variable. For example, in a study investigating the effect of a new drug on blood pressure, the independent variable would be the administration of the drug.

 

b. Dependent Variable: This is the variable that is measured or observed in the experiment. It represents the effect or outcome of the manipulation of the independent variable. Using the same example, the dependent variable in the blood pressure study would be the blood pressure readings of the participants after they receive the drug.

 

c. Control Variable: This is a variable that is held constant or controlled by the researcher to minimize its influence on the dependent variable. Control variables help ensure that the effect observed in the dependent variable is due to the independent variable and not other extraneous factors. For instance, in the drug study, the researcher might control factors like age, gender, and diet to ensure they don't confound the results.

 

d. Discrete Variable: This refers to a type of variable that has distinct and separate values. It usually represents categories or groups and cannot be broken down into smaller units. Discrete variables are typically measured in whole numbers. For example, the number of children in a family is a discrete variable, as it can only take on specific integer values (e.g., 1, 2, 3).

Question 47
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 01 Oct 2022 Morning)Statement I:A discrete variable can represent only finite set of values.Statement II:A continuous variable can be broken into subparts including fractions.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Statement I: A discrete variable can represent only a finite set of values. This statement is true. A discrete variable is one that has separate and distinct values and does not allow for intermediate values between these distinct points. For example, the number of students in a class can only take on whole numbers, such as 0, 1, 2, 3, etc.

 

Statement II: A continuous variable can be broken into subparts, including fractions. This statement is false. A continuous variable is one that can take on an infinite number of values within a given range and can include fractional or decimal values. It does not have distinct subparts. For example, height can be measured with any precision, including fractions like 165.5 cm, 170.2 cm, etc.

Question 48
Identify the sequence of basic procedures to control the extraneous variables in an experiment: (UGC NET 21 Oct 2022 Morning)a. Randomizationb. Elimination of spurious relations.c. Matchingd. Introduction of additional variable.e. Statistical testChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, c, d, e
  • B.b, c, d, e, a
  • C.c, d, e, a, b
  • D.d, e, a, b, c
Correct Answer: a, b, c, d, e

The correct sequence of basic procedures to control extraneous variables in an experiment is:

(A) a, b, c, d, e

 

(a) Randomization: Randomization involves randomly assigning participants to different experimental conditions. This helps ensure that any extraneous variables are equally distributed among the groups, reducing the potential for bias and allowing for more accurate conclusions about the effects of the independent variable.

 

(b) By eliminating these spurious relations, we can ensure that any observed effects are more likely to be attributed to the independent variable.

 

(c) Matching: Matching involves selecting participants for different experimental conditions such that they are similar in terms of certain extraneous variables that could potentially affect the outcome. By matching participants based on these variables, we can reduce the influence of these extraneous factors on the results.

 

(d) Introduction of additional variable: This refers to the process of introducing a control variable into the experiment to account for the effects of specific extraneous variables. By including these additional variables, we can statistically control for their impact on the dependent variable.

 

(e) Statistical test: After implementing the above procedures, researchers use statistical tests to analyze the data and determine the significance of the relationship between the independent and dependent variables. Statistical tests help identify if the observed effects are likely due to the manipulation of the independent variable rather than chanceaccount for the effects of specific extraneous variables. By including these additional variables, we can statistically control for their impact on the dependent variable.

 

(e) Statistical test: After implementing the above procedures, researchers use statistical tests to analyze the data and determine the significance of the relationship between the independent and dependent variables. Statistical tests help identify if the observed effects are likely due to the manipulation of the independent variable rather than chance.

Quiz Attempt #119761

Total Questions: 31
Question 1
Creating purpose statements, research questions and hypotheses that are narrow and measurable would mark the characteristic features of which research type? (UGC NET 21 Nov 2021 Morning)
  • A.Narrative research
  • B.Ethnographic research
  • C.Grounded theory research
  • D.Experimental research
Correct Answer: Experimental research

Experimental research is characterized by creating purpose statements, research questions, and hypotheses that are narrow and measurable. In experimental research, researchers design controlled experiments to manipulate one or more independent variables and observe their effects on dependent variables. By formulating precise and specific research questions and hypotheses, experimental researchers can test the causal relationships between variables and draw valid and reliable conclusions. The emphasis on narrow and measurable statements helps ensure the clarity and rigor of the experimental design and analysis.

Question 2
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 01 Dec Evening 2021)List I (Contexts)a. Context of discoveryb. Inductive reasoningc. Abductive reasoningd. Context of justificationList II (Examples)i. From the particular to a generalisation.ii. Testing or verifying the hypothesis.iii. Hypothesis generation.iv. Inference based on some observations.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.a-ii, b-i, c-iv, d-iii
  • B.a-iv, b-iii, c-i, d-ii
  • C.a-i, b-iii, c-ii, d-iv
  • D.a-iii, b-i, c-iv, d-ii
Correct Answer: a-iii, b-i, c-iv, d-ii

Let's provide a more detailed explanation of each context of reasoning and its corresponding example:

 

a. Context of discovery - Hypothesis generation (iii)

The context of discovery refers to the initial phase of the scientific process where researchers explore and generate new ideas, theories, or hypotheses. During this stage, researchers may make observations, perform experiments, or engage in creative thinking to formulate new hypotheses that can explain certain phenomena or relationships. These hypotheses are potential explanations that have not been fully tested or verified yet. The focus is on generating ideas and exploring possible avenues for further investigation.

 

b. Inductive reasoning - From the particular to a generalization (i)

Inductive reasoning involves making generalizations or drawing conclusions based on specific observations or evidence. Researchers use inductive reasoning when they have collected a set of observations or data and then generalize the findings to a broader context. For example, after observing several instances of a phenomenon, researchers might infer a general principle or pattern that applies beyond the specific observations.

 

c. Abductive reasoning - Inference based on some observations (iv)

Abductive reasoning is a form of logical inference where researchers make an educated guess or inference based on the available evidence or observations. It involves using the most likely or plausible explanation, even though it may not be certain or proven. Abductive reasoning is common in situations where there might be incomplete information or uncertainty. Researchers use this type of reasoning to propose hypotheses or explanations that fit the observed data.

 

d. Context of justification - Testing or verifying the hypothesis (ii)

The context of justification is the later phase of the scientific process, where researchers aim to test and verify the hypotheses generated in the context of discovery. Researchers design experiments, collect data, and use statistical methods to analyze the data and determine whether the evidence supports or refutes the proposed hypotheses. This process involves subjecting the hypotheses to rigorous testing to draw valid conclusions and support scientific claims based on empirical evidence.

Question 3
Analytic Induction is a method of: (UGC NET 25 Nov Morning 2021)b. Generating hypothesisc. Testing hypothesisd. Freestyle interpretatione. Testing null hypothesis only.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b and c only
  • B.b, c and d only
  • C.c, d and e only
  • D.a, b and e only
Correct Answer: a, b and c only

Analytic induction is an approach used in qualitative research to develop and refine theoretical explanations based on the systematic interpretation of events or observations. It involves generating hypotheses and testing them against empirical evidence to arrive at meaningful conclusions about a phenomenon.

Question 4
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 04 Dec Morning 2021)Statement I:Manipulation and control are two important possibilities in natural science research.Statement II:Not many phenomena can be manipulated and controlled by social scientists.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Statement I: In natural science research, researchers often have the opportunity to manipulate variables and control the experimental conditions. This allows them to establish cause-and-effect relationships and draw more definitive conclusions about the phenomena they are studying. The ability to manipulate and control variables is a hallmark of experimental research in the natural sciences.

 

Statement II: Social science research deals with complex and dynamic human behaviors, social systems, and cultural contexts. Unlike natural science research, many social phenomena cannot be easily manipulated or controlled due to ethical, practical, or contextual constraints. For example, social scientists cannot ethically manipulate certain variables in studies involving human subjects. Therefore, not many phenomena can be manipulated and controlled in social science research compared to natural science research.

Question 5
A scientific approach in social science research should take into account: (UGC NET 04 Dec Morning 2021)a. Metaphysical elementsb. Spurious relationsc. The factor of co-variation.d. Time ordere. The possibility of theorisation.Choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, c only
  • B.b, c, d only
  • C.c, d, e only
  • D.a, b, e only
Correct Answer: c, d, e only

a. The factor of co-variation - Co-variation is an essential consideration in social science research. It refers to the relationship between variables, where changes in one variable are associated with changes in another variable. Co-variation is central to establishing correlations and making causal inferences in social science research.

 

b. Time order - Time order is a critical element in establishing causal relationships between variables. In social science research, researchers must determine the temporal sequence of events to infer causality properly. The cause must precede the effect in time for a causal relationship to be plausible.

 

c. The possibility of theorization - Theorization is a fundamental aspect of social science research. Researchers develop and utilize theories to explain and interpret social phenomena. Theories provide frameworks for understanding and organizing observations and are an integral part of the scientific approach in social science research.

 

Question 6
Given below are two statements, one is labelled as Assertion A and the other is labelled as Reason R: (UGC NET 27 Nov Morning 2021)Assertion ‘A’:In experimental research, the effect of independent variable is examined on the dependent variable.Reason ‘R’:Causal relation between two variables can be established only by the experimental method.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A.
  • B.Both A and R are true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A.
  • C.A is true but R is false.
  • D.A is false but R is true.
Correct Answer: Both A and R are true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A.

Assertion A: This assertion is true. In experimental research, researchers manipulate the independent variable to observe its effect on the dependent variable. The independent variable is the variable that the researcher controls or manipulates, while the dependent variable is the variable that is measured to assess the outcome or response to the manipulation of the independent variable. Experimental research is designed to establish cause-and-effect relationships between variables.

 

Reason R: This reason is not entirely true. While experimental research is one of the most robust methods for establishing causal relationships between variables, it is not the only method. Experimental studies, with their random assignment and control over variables, allow researchers to make stronger causal inferences. However, there are other research designs, such as quasi-experimental and correlational studies, that also contribute to understanding causal relationships to some extent, even if they may not provide as strong evidence as true experimental studies.

Question 7
Hypothesis testing which results into either affirmation or disaffirmation is the explicit concern in which methods of research? (UGC NET 20 Nov Morning 2021)a. Descriptive methodb. Experimental methodc. Ex Post Facto methodd. Historical methode. Exegetical methodChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a and b
  • B.b and c
  • C.c and d
  • D.d and e
Correct Answer: b and c

The correct answer is B.

Hypothesis testing, which results in either affirmation or disaffirmation of a hypothesis, is an explicit concern in the following methods of research:

a. Experimental method: The experimental method involves manipulating an independent variable to observe its effect on a dependent variable while controlling for other variables. Hypothesis testing is a fundamental component of experimental research, as researchers formulate a null hypothesis and an alternative hypothesis to be tested based on their research question. The goal of the experiment is to either affirm or disaffirm the null hypothesis, which leads to conclusions about the presence or absence of the effect being studied.

 

b. Ex Post Facto method: The Ex Post Facto method, also known as the "causal-comparative" method, is a type of non-experimental research design where the independent variable has already occurred, and the researcher cannot manipulate it. Instead, the researcher examines the effects of the independent variable on the dependent variable retrospectively. In this method, hypothesis testing is used to determine whether there is a significant relationship or difference between groups based on the prior occurrence of the independent variable.

 

The other methods mentioned do not explicitly revolve around hypothesis testing:

Descriptive method: Descriptive research is concerned with describing and analyzing the characteristics of a population or phenomenon. While it may involve hypothesis generation, hypothesis testing is not necessarily a primary focus in this method.

Historical method: The historical method involves the systematic study and interpretation of past events and developments. While historical research may involve forming hypotheses for investigation, hypothesis testing is not a defining feature of this method.

Exegetical method: The exegetical method is primarily associated with the critical interpretation and analysis of religious texts and scriptures. While interpretation and analysis may involve forming hypotheses about the meaning of the text, hypothesis testing is not a prominent aspect of this method.

Question 8
Which type of research encourages participant's perspective? (UGC NET 20 Nov Morning 2021)
  • A.Ethnographic method
  • B.Historical research
  • C.Exegetic research
  • D.Experimental research
Correct Answer: Ethnographic method

Ethnographic research encourages the participant's perspective. In ethnographic research, the researcher immerses themselves in the culture and community being studied. They spend time with the participants, observe their daily activities, and often participate in their social life. The aim is to gain an in-depth understanding of the participants' perspectives, experiences, beliefs, and behaviors from their own point of view.

 

By adopting a participant's perspective, ethnographic researchers seek to avoid imposing their preconceived notions or biases on the study. Instead, they aim to understand the cultural context and social meanings from the perspective of the participants themselves. Ethnographic research is commonly used in anthropology and other social sciences to explore and document the nuances of human cultures and societies.

Question 9
Sometimes, subjects who know that they are in a control group may work hard to excel against the experimental group. Such a phenomenon is known as: (UGC NET 25 Nov Morning 2021)
  • A.Controlled Competition
  • B.Motivational Contest
  • C.Compensatory Rivalry
  • D.Inspirational Influence
Correct Answer: Compensatory Rivalry

Compensatory rivalry, also known as the "John Henry effect," refers to a phenomenon where participants in the control group of an experiment may work harder or put in more effort to excel compared to the experimental group. This can happen when participants in the control group become aware that they are not receiving the treatment or intervention being tested in the study. In an effort to compensate for this perceived disadvantage, they may put in extra effort to perform better or achieve better outcomes.

 

This effect can potentially influence the results of the study by affecting the differences between the control and experimental groups. Researchers need to be aware of this possibility and take measures to minimize its impact, such as using blinding techniques where participants are unaware of their group assignment or employing placebo controls.

Question 10
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 22 Nov Morning 2021)Statement I:Action Research is used primarily to improve a given situation by a practitioner.Statement II:Applied Research is directed at exploring applicability of principles already established.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect.
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.

Statement I: This statement is true. Action research is a type of research approach where practitioners or individuals directly involved in a particular context conduct research to address and improve specific issues or problems within that context. The main goal of action research is to bring about practical and positive changes in the given situation.

 

Statement II: This statement is also true. Applied research is focused on using existing theories, principles, or knowledge to address practical problems or provide solutions in real-world settings. It involves the application of established theoretical concepts to specific contexts or situations to understand their applicability and usefulness.

Question 11
Constant comparison is a tool used in: (UGC NET 05 Dec Morning 2021)
  • A.Grounded theory
  • B.Feministic theory
  • C.Relational theory
  • D.Grand theory
Correct Answer: Grounded theory

Constant comparison is a key methodological tool used in Grounded Theory, a qualitative research approach developed by sociologists Barney Glaser and Anselm Strauss. Grounded Theory aims to generate theories directly from the data without starting with preconceived hypotheses. The process of constant comparison is at the core of how Grounded Theory is conducted.

 

In Grounded Theory, researchers collect and analyze data in a systematic and iterative manner. The constant comparison involves comparing the data collected with the data already analyzed, constantly moving back and forth between data collection and analysis. This process allows researchers to identify concepts, categories, and relationships that emerge from the data itself.

 

Here's how the constant comparison method works in Grounded Theory:

1. Data Collection: Researchers begin by collecting qualitative data, such as interviews, observations, or documents, related to the phenomenon they are studying.

2. Open Coding: In the initial stage of analysis, researchers engage in open coding, where they break down the data into smaller units, such as phrases or sentences, and assign descriptive codes to these segments.

3. Constant Comparison: As new data is collected and analyzed, researchers continuously compare the new data with the codes and categories already identified. They look for similarities, differences, and relationships between the data segments and the emerging codes.

4. Developing Categories: Through this constant comparison process, researchers start to develop categories or themes that represent the recurring patterns found in the data. These categories are more abstract and capture the essence of the data.

5. Theoretical Sampling: Researchers use the emerging categories to guide further data collection. They purposefully select new participants or data sources that will provide rich information related to the developing theory.

6. Theoretical Saturation: The process of constant comparison and data collection continues until theoretical saturation is reached. Theoretical saturation occurs when no new significant insights or categories emerge, and the theory is well-developed based on the data collected.

 

Question 12
Data of research take the forms of words or pictures with the researcher as the key instrument in which of the following studies? (UGC NET 21 Nov Evening 2021)
  • A.Participant observation based Studies .
  • B.Ex Post Facto Studies
  • C.Experimental Studies
  • D.Descriptive survey Studies
Correct Answer: Participant observation based Studies .

In participant observation based studies, the researcher directly observes and immerses themselves in the social setting or group being studied. The researcher acts as the key instrument and collects data in the form of words (observations, field notes, interviews, etc.) or pictures (photographs, visual documentation) to understand the behavior, interactions, and culture of the group under study. The researcher's presence and active involvement in the setting allow them to gather rich and contextual data that can provide valuable insights into the research topic.

Question 13
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 21 Nov Evening 2021)List I (Research Types)a. Fundamental Researchb. Applied Researchc. Action of Researchd. Evaluative ResearchList II (Goal of Research)i. Appraising impact of interventions.ii. Amelioration of a given situation.iii. Exploring applicability of already established principles.iv. Advancing the corpus of knowledge in a field.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.a‐i, b‐ii, c‐iii, d‐iv
  • B.a‐iv, b‐iii, c‐ii, d‐i
  • C.a‐iii, b‐iv, c‐i, d‐ii
  • D.a‐ii, b‐i, c‐iv, d‐iii
Correct Answer: a‐iv, b‐iii, c‐ii, d‐i

a. Fundamental Research - Goal: Advancing the corpus of knowledge in a field.

Fundamental research, also known as basic or pure research, is driven by the desire to expand the understanding of fundamental principles and concepts in a specific field of study. The primary goal of fundamental research is to advance theoretical knowledge without any immediate practical application in mind. Researchers in this category seek to explore and uncover new theories, principles, or relationships that contribute to the overall body of knowledge in their field. Fundamental research lays the groundwork for applied research and serves as the basis for future investigations and innovations.

 

b. Applied Research - Goal: Exploring the applicability of already established principles.

Applied research aims to use existing knowledge, theories, and principles to address specific real-world problems or situations. The primary goal of applied research is to find practical solutions and insights that can be directly applied to improve or solve specific issues or challenges. Researchers conducting applied research work with a clear problem statement and attempt to use their findings to inform policy, decision-making, or practical applications in various fields such as technology, healthcare, education, and more.

 

c. Action Research - Goal: Amelioration of a given situation.

Action research is a type of research that focuses on making improvements and bringing about positive change within a particular setting or context. The primary goal of action research is to identify and address specific problems or challenges faced by a community, organization, or group. Researchers and practitioners collaborate closely to collect data, analyze the findings, and implement interventions to improve the situation actively. The cyclical nature of action research allows for ongoing evaluation and adjustment of interventions to achieve the desired outcomes.

 

d. Evaluative Research - Goal: Appraising the impact of interventions.

Evaluative research is conducted to assess the effectiveness, efficiency, and impact of programs, interventions, policies, or practices. The primary goal of evaluative research is to provide evidence-based feedback on the success or failure of a particular intervention or program. Evaluative research helps stakeholders and decision-makers understand whether the intended outcomes were achieved and identifies areas for improvement. It plays a crucial role in determining the effectiveness of social programs, educational initiatives, healthcare interventions, and other projects.

 

The correct matching of the research types with their corresponding goals is:

a - iv, b - iii, c - ii, d - i. Therefore, the correct answer is option .

Question 14
Which of the following is an example of qualitative research? (UGC NET 03 Dec Morning 2021)
  • A.Experimental research
  • B.Ex post facto research
  • C.Descriptive survey research
  • D.Grounded theory research
Correct Answer: Grounded theory research

Grounded theory research is an example of qualitative research. Grounded theory is a research method used to develop theory or conceptual frameworks based on the data collected from the field. In grounded theory research, researchers gather and analyze data through interviews, observations, or other qualitative methods, and they iteratively develop theories and concepts based on the patterns and themes emerging from the data.

 

The other options listed are examples of quantitative research methods:

  • Experimental research - Experimental research is a quantitative research method that involves manipulating variables and measuring their effects on other variables under controlled conditions.
  • Ex post facto research - Ex post facto research is also a quantitative research method that involves studying the effects of independent variables that have occurred naturally (without manipulation) and determining their impact on dependent variables.
  • Descriptive survey research - Descriptive survey research is a quantitative research method used to describe and analyze the characteristics, attitudes, behaviors, or opinions of a population using surveys and questionnaires.
Question 15
Given below are two statements:(UGC NET 03 Dec Morning 2021)Statement I:Scientific research is systematic, controlled, empirical and critical investigation of hypothetical propositions.Statement II:Population of research need not be defined in qualitative and quantitative researches.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Statement I is true but Statement II is false.

Statement I: This statement is true. Scientific research refers to a structured and methodical investigation conducted to expand knowledge, test hypotheses, and answer specific research questions. It follows a systematic approach, employs controls to minimize bias, relies on empirical evidence, and involves critical evaluation of existing theories or hypotheses.

 

Statement II: This statement is false. In both qualitative and quantitative research, it is essential to define the population or the group of interest to which the research findings will be generalized. The population represents the larger group from which the research sample is drawn, and it helps researchers make inferences about the broader context based on the collected data.

Question 16
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 20 Nov Evening 2021)List I (Methods of research)a. Experimentalb. ExPost Factoc. Descriptived. HistoricalList II (Features emphasized)i. Primary and secondary sources tapped with emphasis on internal criticism.ii. Status of facts and conditions are ascertained.iii. A variable is manipulated to see its effect on other variable.iv. The differences are noted and factors causal or otherwise are determined.Choose the correct answer from the options given below :Codes
  • A.a‐ i, b‐ ii, c‐ iii, d‐ iv
  • B.a‐ ii, b‐ i, c‐ iv, d‐ iii
  • C.a‐ iii, b‐ iv, c‐ ii, d‐ i
  • D.a‐ iv, b‐ iii, c‐ i, d‐ ii
Correct Answer: a‐ iii, b‐ iv, c‐ ii, d‐ i

a. Experimental - (iii) A variable is manipulated to see its effect on other variable.

Experimental research involves manipulating one or more independent variables to observe their effects on dependent variables while controlling for other factors. The emphasis is on causality and determining cause-and-effect relationships.

 

b. ExPost Facto - (iv) The differences are noted, and factors causal or otherwise are determined.

ExPost Facto research, also known as causal-comparative research, involves examining existing differences between groups or conditions to determine possible causal factors that led to those differences.

 

c. Descriptive - (ii) Status of facts and conditions are ascertained.

Descriptive research focuses on describing and presenting the status of facts, conditions, or phenomena as they exist in a particular context without manipulating any variables.

 

d. Historical - (i) Primary and secondary sources tapped with emphasis on internal criticism.

Historical research involves the critical examination and analysis of primary and secondary sources from the past to understand historical events and phenomena. The emphasis is on internal criticism to ensure the reliability and validity of historical evidence.

 

Question 17
Identify the features of empirico-inductive paradigm or research: (UGC NET 22 Nov Morning 2021)Research is concerned with the process rather than simply with outcomes or products.Based on logical positivist philosophy which assumes a single objective reality.Researchers are concerned with what are called ‘participant perspectives’.Attempts to establish universal context free generalizations.Choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.a and b only
  • B.b and c only
  • C.c and d only
  • D.a and c only
Correct Answer: a and c only

Research is concerned with the process rather than simply with outcomes or products - This is a feature of the empirico-inductive paradigm. In this approach, researchers focus not only on the final outcomes or results but also on the process of conducting the research and how data is collected, analyzed, and interpreted.

 

Researchers are concerned with what are called ‘participant perspectives’ - This is also a feature of the empirico-inductive paradigm. In this approach, researchers emphasize understanding the perspectives, experiences, and viewpoints of the participants being studied. The researcher aims to gain insights from the participants' own viewpoints, often through qualitative methods.

Question 18
In which method of research an independent variable is manipulated with an intent to observe concomitant changes in dependent variables? (UGC NET 22 Nov Evening 2021)
  • A.ExPost Facto method
  • B.Case study method
  • C.Descriptive survey method
  • D.Experimental method
Correct Answer: Experimental method

The correct answer is D.

In the Experimental method of research, an independent variable is deliberately manipulated or controlled by the researcher with the intent of observing the concomitant changes in the dependent variable. The goal of an experiment is to establish a cause-and-effect relationship between the independent variable and the dependent variable.

 

Here's a brief explanation of each research method mentioned:

ExPost Facto method: This method is also known as the "after the fact" research design. In ExPost Facto research, the independent variable is not manipulated by the researcher; rather, the researcher observes and examines the effects of pre-existing differences or conditions on the dependent variable.

 

Case study method: The case study method is an in-depth, qualitative research approach that focuses on investigating a particular individual, group, or situation. In case studies, the researcher may not necessarily manipulate variables but seeks to understand the complexities of a specific case.

 

Descriptive survey method: The descriptive survey method involves collecting data from a sample to describe or document the characteristics of a population. While this method may identify relationships between variables, it typically does not involve manipulating the independent variable to observe changes in the dependent variable.

 

Experimental method: In the experimental method, researchers actively manipulate the independent variable(s) to observe the effects on the dependent variable(s). This manipulation is typically done by creating different experimental conditions or groups, where participants are exposed to different levels of the independent variable. The researcher then measures the changes in the dependent variable(s) to determine whether there is a causal relationship.

Question 19
Given below are two statements, one is labelled as Assertion A and the other is labelled as Reason R: (UGC NET 01 Dec Morning 2021)Assertion ‘A’:In the case study method, the researcher collects detailed information from a limited number of participants.Reason ‘R’:Findings based on case study research can be used to develop research hypotheses/questions for subsequent studies.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A.
  • B.Both A and R are true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A.
  • C.A is true but R is false.
  • D.A is false but R is true.
Correct Answer: Both A and R are true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A.

Assertion ‘A’: This assertion is true. In the case study method, researchers focus on in-depth investigations of a single individual, group, organization, or event. They collect detailed and rich information from a limited number of participants or cases to gain a comprehensive understanding of the specific phenomenon under study.

 

Reason ‘R’: This reason is also true. The findings obtained from case study research can indeed serve as a valuable basis for generating research hypotheses or questions for subsequent or follow-up studies. The rich and context-specific data obtained from case studies can provide insights, patterns, or relationships that can be explored further in larger, more generalizable studies.

 

While both the assertion and reason are true, Reason ‘R’ is not the correct explanation of Assertion ‘A’. The reason provides a general benefit of case study research, but it does not directly explain why researchers collect detailed information from a limited number of participants in the case study method. Therefore, the correct answer is B.

Question 20
Scientific research has the ultimate goal of explaining any phenomenon by:(UGC NET 03 Dec Evening 2021)
  • A.Conditional laws
  • B.Laws of uniqueness
  • C.Laws of intuition
  • D.Laws of generalisation
Correct Answer: Laws of generalisation

Scientific research aims to explain any phenomenon by establishing general principles or laws that can be applied to a broader range of situations. These general principles are known as laws of generalisation. They help in making predictions and inferences about other similar phenomena beyond the specific context of the research study. Laws of generalisation are essential for developing a comprehensive understanding of natural and social phenomena and for advancing scientific knowledge.
