Question 22
Which among the following methods is commonly used in anthropological research? (UGC NET 26 Nov Evening 2021)
  • A.Survey method
  • B.Case study method
  • C.Life history method
  • D.Ethnographic method
Correct Answer: Ethnographic method

The ethnographic method is commonly used in anthropological research. Ethnography is a qualitative research approach that involves the systematic study and observation of people and their cultures in their natural settings. Anthropologists often use ethnographic methods to immerse themselves in the lives and practices of the communities they study. They typically spend extended periods of time in the field, living with the community, observing their daily activities, and participating in their social life. Ethnography allows researchers to gain an in-depth understanding of the culture, beliefs, values, and behaviors of the people they are studying. It is a widely used and valuable method in anthropological research for providing rich and contextual insights into human societies and cultures.

Question 23
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 28 Nov Morning 2021)List Ia. Ex post facto Researchb. Applied Researchc. Conceptual Researchd. Exploratory ResearchList IIi. Finding a solution for an immediate problem facing a society or an industrial/business organisation.ii. Related to some abstract idea(s) or theory.iii. Development of hypotheses rather than their testing.iv. No control over variables, reports only what has happened or what is happening.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.a- iv, b‐ i, c‐ iii, d‐ ii
  • B.a‐ iii, b‐ ii, c‐ i, d‐ iv
  • C.a‐ iv, b‐ i, c‐ ii, d‐ iii
  • D.a‐ i, b‐ iii, c‐ ii, d‐ iv
Correct Answer: a‐ iv, b‐ i, c‐ ii, d‐ iii

a. Ex post facto Research - (iv) No control over variables, reports only what has happened or what is happening.

Ex post facto research involves studying existing conditions or events without the researcher having control over the variables. The researcher reports on what has already happened or is happening without manipulating any variables.

 

b. Applied Research - (i) Finding a solution for an immediate problem facing a society or an industrial/business organization.

Applied research focuses on addressing practical problems or issues faced by society, industries, businesses, or organizations. It aims to find solutions that can be applied to real-world situations and improve current practices or situations.

 

c. Conceptual Research - (ii) Related to some abstract idea(s) or theory.

Conceptual research is concerned with abstract ideas, concepts, or theories rather than empirical observations. It involves the study of theoretical frameworks, models, and concepts to develop a deeper understanding of specific topics.

 

d. Exploratory Research - (iii) Development of hypotheses rather than their testing.

Exploratory research is primarily focused on exploring and gaining insights into a research problem or topic. It involves the development of research questions or hypotheses rather than their testing or verification.

Question 24
In which method of research an independent variable is manipulated with an intent to observe concomitant changes in dependent variable? (UGC NET 22 Nov Morning 2021)
  • A.ExPost Facto method
  • B.Case study method
  • C.Descriptive survey method
  • D.Experimental method
Correct Answer: Experimental method

In the experimental method of research, an independent variable is manipulated by the researcher with the intention of observing concomitant changes in the dependent variable. In experimental studies, the researcher designs and controls the conditions to test the cause-and-effect relationship between variables. The independent variable is the factor that is deliberately changed or manipulated by the researcher, while the dependent variable is the factor that is observed and measured to assess the effects of the independent variable.

 

Experimental research allows researchers to draw causal inferences and establish relationships between variables by controlling for other potential influences. It is a powerful method for examining cause-and-effect relationships and is commonly used to investigate hypotheses in various scientific fields.

Question 25
In which of the following researches, attempts are made to establish context‐free generalizations? (UGC NET 20 Nov Evening 2021)
  • A.Phenomenology
  • B.Grounded theory
  • C.Symbolic interactionism
  • D.Experimental Studies
Correct Answer: Experimental Studies

In experimental studies, attempts are made to establish context-free generalizations. Experimental research involves manipulating one or more independent variables and observing their effects on dependent variables while controlling for other factors. The goal of experimental studies is to draw general conclusions and establish cause-and-effect relationships that can be applied to a broader population or context. By controlling for potential confounding variables, researchers aim to establish context-free generalizations and make inferences about the relationship between variables that hold true beyond the specific experimental conditions. Experimental studies are considered to have a high level of internal validity, allowing for confident generalizations under specific conditions.

Question 26
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 24 Nov Morning 2021)Statement I: A variable measured at the nominal level can be used in higher‐level statistics if it is converted into another form.Statement II: The result of the conversion process is called dummy variable.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Statement I: Variables measured at the nominal level can be converted into other forms for use in higher-level statistics. For example, nominal variables can be converted into dummy variables to represent different categories or groups.

 

Statement II: The result of the conversion process of a nominal variable into another form is called a dummy variable. Dummy variables are binary variables that take the value of 0 or 1 to represent different categories or groups in statistical analysis. They are commonly used in regression analysis and other statistical models to represent categorical data.

Question 27
An extraneous variable is also known as: (UGC NET 24 Nov Morning 2021)
  • A.Artifact
  • B.Dependent variable
  • C.Intervener
  • D.Contiguous factor
Correct Answer: Intervener

An extraneous variable is also known as an "intervening variable" or "confounding variable." It is a variable that is not the main focus of a study but may still have an influence on the outcome of the study.

Artifact: An artifact refers to an unintended outcome or result that is not a true representation of the underlying phenomenon, often caused by the way the study is conducted or the measurement methods used.

Dependent variable: The dependent variable is the variable that is measured or observed in an experiment, and its value depends on the independent variable.

Intervener: As mentioned above, an intervener or extraneous variable is a variable that is not part of the main research question but can affect the relationship between the independent and dependent variables.

Contiguous factor: This term is not commonly used in the context of extraneous variables in research.

Question 28
Given below are two statements, one is labelled as Assertion A and the other is labelled as Reason R: (UGC NET 27 Nov Evening 2021)Assertion ‘A’: Causal relationship between the independent variable and the dependent variable cannot be established beyond doubt, if the researcher fails to control the conditions.Reason ‘R’: A set of confounding variables are likely to influence the value of the dependent variable, if they are not controlled by the researcher.In light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.Both A and R are correct and R is the correct explanation of A.
  • B.Both A and R are correct and R is NOT the correct explanation of A.
  • C.A is correct but R is not correct.
  • D.A is not correct but R is correct.
Correct Answer: Both A and R are correct and R is the correct explanation of A.

In experiment research, a causal relationship is cause-and-effect is conditions between two variables. Researchers call independent and dependent variables when one variable causes or contributes to change in another. The cause is an independent variable, while the consequence is a dependent variable. The researcher tries to control the different variables and tries to manipulate the independent variable and tries to observe the effect on the dependent variable. In case, is the researcher don't able to control the conditions then unable to establish the causal relationship between variables and created doubt.

Therefore, Assertion A is Correct.

 

A confounding variable is an unmeasured third variable that affects both the purported cause and effect in research. It is extraneous variables that affect the independent and dependent variables in a study. Confounding variables must be taken into account to ensure the internal validity of your study. If you don't, your results might not accurately reflect the link between the variables you're interested in.

So, Reason R is Correct and the explanation of A.

Question 29
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 27 Nov Evening 2021)Statement I:A moderating variable is a second independent variable that is included because it is believed to have a significant contingent effect on the original independent variable and dependent variable relationship.Statement II:An extraneous variable may conceivably affect a given relationship between the independent variable and the dependent variable.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

Both Statement I and Statement II are true.

 

Statement I explain the concept of a moderating variable, which is an additional independent variable included in a study to examine its contingent effect on the relationship between the original independent variable and the dependent variable.

 

Statement II defines an extraneous variable, which is a variable that may potentially impact the relationship between the independent variable and the dependent variable in a study. These variables need to be controlled or accounted for to ensure the validity and accuracy of the research findings.

Question 30
Given below are two statements: (26 Nov Evening)Statement I:Open coding is achieved by linking codes to contacts to consequences to patterns of interaction and to causes.Statement II:Axial coding is the process of breaking down, examining, comparing, conceptualizing, and categorizing data.In light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect.
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect.

Statement I is incorrect because it misrepresents the process of open coding in grounded theory. Open coding involves breaking down data into discrete parts and labeling them with codes to identify concepts, not linking them to contacts, consequences, patterns of interaction, or causes.

 

Statement II is incorrect because it describes axial coding inaccurately. Axial coding is the process of connecting codes to categories and subcategories and examining relationships between them, not breaking down, examining, comparing, and categorizing data.

Question 31
Match List I with List II: (26 Nov Evening)List Ia. Selective codingb. Initial codingc. Focused codingd. Theoretical codingList IIi. To discover the most significant or frequent initial code that makes the most analytical sense.ii. The procedure of selecting the core category, Systematically relating it to other categories, validating their relationships, and filling in categories that need further refinement and development.iii. It specifies possible relationships between categories, these are integrative.iv. Comparing data with data, staying close to and remain open to exploring what is happening in data, construct and keep the code short, simple, precise and active.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.a‐ ii , b‐ iv , c‐ i , d‐ iii
  • B.a‐ iv , b‐ i , c‐ iii , d‐ ii
  • C.a‐ i , b‐ iii , c‐ ii , d‐ iv
  • D.a‐ iii , b‐ ii , c‐ iv , d‐ i
Correct Answer: a‐ ii , b‐ iv , c‐ i , d‐ iii

a. Selective Coding - Selective coding is the process of selecting the core category, systematically relating it to other categories, validating their relationships, and filling in categories that need further refinement and development. In other words, it involves identifying the central theme or core category that best explains the phenomenon under study and then integrating other categories around it to build a comprehensive theoretical framework.

 

b. Initial Coding - Initial coding is the first step in the coding process where data is broken down into discrete segments and labeled with codes. The goal of initial coding is to discover the most significant or frequent initial codes that make the most analytical sense. It involves closely examining the data, comparing data with data, and staying open to exploring what is happening in the data to create meaningful codes.

 

c. Focused Coding - Focused coding involves specifying possible relationships between categories and integrating them into a more cohesive and organized framework. This type of coding is integrative, as it seeks to connect different categories and themes to understand how they interact and relate to each other.

 

d. Theoretical Coding - Theoretical coding goes beyond simply describing data and involves conceptualizing the relationships between categories at a higher level of abstraction. It aims to develop a theoretical understanding of the phenomenon under study by creating overarching concepts and theoretical models that explain the data.

Quiz Attempt #119762

Total Questions: 43
Question 1
The research wherein the focus of concern is the exploration of applicability of theories to newly emerging practices and domains of knowledge is called (UGC NET 13 Nov 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Practitioner’s research
  • B.Theoretical research
  • C.Situational research
  • D.Second level research
Correct Answer: Second level research

Second level research, also known as secondary research or desk research, involves the use of pre-existing data and information to address research objectives. Instead of collecting primary data through surveys or experiments, researchers rely on data that has already been published or made available by various sources, such as research reports, public libraries, websites, and surveys conducted by others.

 

In second level research, the researcher synthesizes and collates existing data to gain insights into the applicability of established theories and concepts in new or emerging areas of practice and knowledge. By utilizing existing theories, the research seeks to contribute to the understanding of how these theories can be adapted or extended to address contemporary issues and challenges.

Question 2
Which of the following research forms, aims primarily at putting to use the theoretical advances with an eye on exploring the potential for generalizability? (UGC NET 09 Oct 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Fundamental research
  • B.Evaluative research
  • C.Action research
  • D.Applied research
Correct Answer: Applied research

Applied research is focused on addressing specific real-world problems and finding solutions that can be implemented in practical settings. The main objective of applied research is to use existing theories, principles, and knowledge to solve practical issues and improve processes, products, or services. It is driven by the need to make immediate and tangible contributions to practical applications

Question 3
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 30 Sept 2020 Evening paper)Statement I:Action research is cyclic in so far as it involves 'Plan-Act-Observe-Reflect' cycle.Statement II:The purpose of Action research is to develop a theory to explain causal relationship among variables.In light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct
Correct Answer: Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect

Action research indeed follows a cyclic research process, consisting of four phases - Plan, Act, Observe, and Reflect. This cyclic nature allows researchers to continuously circle back to earlier phases within a cycle, such as going back and forth between reflection and planning. The cyclic process helps in iterative improvements and refining interventions.

 

However, the purpose of Action research is not to develop a theory to explain causal relationships among variables. Instead, the primary aim of Action research is to bring about practical and meaningful change in a specific context or setting. It focuses on identifying issues, implementing interventions, and observing the outcomes to make improvements based on the findings.

Question 4
"A university teacher plans to study the performance of students in implementing specific projects in terms of their creativity level".Which method of research will be appropriate to use in this context? (UGC NET 30 Sept 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Historical method
  • B.Descriptive survey method
  • C.Experimental method
  • D.Ex post facto method
Correct Answer: Ex post facto method

An ex post facto research design is a type of quasi-experimental method where existing groups with certain characteristics or traits are compared based on a dependent variable of interest. In this design, the researcher does not manipulate or control the independent variable but rather observes and analyzes the groups as they naturally exist.

Unlike a true experimental design, there is no random assignment of participants to different groups. Instead, the grouping is based on pre-existing characteristics or traits that are of interest to the researcher.

 

For instance, in the given scenario, the university teacher plans to study the performance of students in implementing specific projects in terms of their creativity level. The teacher will not manipulate the students' creativity levels or assign them randomly to different projects. Instead, the students will be grouped based on their existing creativity levels, and their performances in implementing the projects will be observed and analyzed accordingly.

 

For example, the teacher may categorize students into groups with high, moderate, and low creativity levels based on previous assessments or evaluations. Then, the teacher would observe and compare their performances on the specific projects assigned to each group.

 

Since the researcher is examining pre-existing characteristics (creativity levels) and their effects on the dependent variable (project performance), this study aligns with the principles of an ex post facto research design.

Question 5
For the following research problem, which of the listed research methods will be most appropriate?"School principal's influence on trust: Perspectives of mother's children with disabilities". (UGC NET 30 Sept 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Experimental method
  • B.Focused group discussion (FGD) based method
  • C.Descriptive survey method
  • D.Ex post facto method
Correct Answer: Focused group discussion (FGD) based method

The Focused Group Discussion is a qualitative research approach commonly used to gain in-depth insights and understanding of social issues. In this method, a purposely selected group of individuals, in this case, mothers of children with disabilities, are brought together to engage in open discussions and share their perspectives on the school principal's influence on trust. FGD allows researchers to explore participants' experiences, attitudes, and opinions in a group setting, promoting rich and interactive discussions that can lead to deeper understanding of the subject matter.

  • The Experimental method involves controlled manipulation of variables to determine cause-and-effect relationships, which may not be suitable for exploring perspectives and trust in a natural setting like this study.
  • Descriptive survey method focuses on describing characteristics of a population or phenomenon without explaining the reasons behind the observed trends. In this research problem, the objective is to gain insights into the perspectives of mothers of children with disabilities, which aligns better with the qualitative nature of FGD.
  • Ex post facto study involves comparing existing groups based on specific traits or characteristics, which is not directly relevant to exploring perspectives and trust in this context.

 

Question 6
In which research method manipulation of ‘independent variable’ and control of ‘extraneous variables’ are neither possible nor desirable? (UGC NET 29 Sept 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Experimental method
  • B.Ex post facto method
  • C.Historical method
  • D.Descriptive survey method
Correct Answer: Ex post facto method

The Ex post facto research design is a non-experimental method that shares some similarities with true experiments, particularly in terms of data analysis and group comparison. However, it is not an experimental design as the researcher does not have control over the independent variable.

 

In an Ex post facto research design, the researcher investigates problems or conditions after they have occurred. The independent variable is not manipulated, and the groups are not assigned randomly. Instead, the groups are formed based on existing characteristics or conditions of the participants, and the researcher observes and compares their outcomes without intervention.

 

Question 7
A university teacher proposes a research project on 'why parents are apathetic to the university programmes'. Which of the following research methods will be most appropriate for the project? (UGC NET 29 Sept 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Experimental method
  • B.Historical method
  • C.Participant-observation method
  • D.Ex post facto method
Correct Answer: Participant-observation method

The Participant-observation method, also known as ethnographic research, involves the researcher actively becoming a part of the group being studied to gather data and gain an in-depth understanding of a social phenomenon or problem. In this method, the researcher immerses themselves in the lives and experiences of the parents to comprehend their thoughts, feelings, and behaviors regarding their apathy towards university programs.

 

By being a participant observer, the researcher can gain unique insights into the perspectives and motivations of the parents, which might not be accessible through other research methods. This approach allows the researcher to understand the social context and cultural factors that influence parental attitudes towards university programs.

 

Question 8
Which of the following research is intervention-based, cyclic in nature and improvement focused? (UGC NET 25 Sept 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Case study research
  • B.Survey research
  • C.Experimental research
  • D.Action research
Correct Answer: Action research

Action research is characterized by its goal of bringing about practical and meaningful change through a continuous and iterative process. It uses a cyclic research process, typically consisting of four phases: Plan, Act (implementing plans), Observe (systematically), and Reflect. This cyclic nature allows researchers to continuously circle back to earlier phases within a cycle, such as going back and forth between reflection and planning.

 

The key features of Action research are:

  • 1. Intervention-based: Action research involves taking deliberate actions or interventions to address specific issues or problems in a practical setting, such as a classroom, organization, or community.
  • 2. Cyclic in nature: It follows a continuous and iterative cycle of planning, acting, observing, and reflecting. Each cycle allows for adjustments and improvements based on the outcomes and observations.
  • 3. Improvement-focused: The primary aim of Action research is to bring about positive changes and improvements in the context under study. It focuses on understanding and addressing real-world problems to enhance practices and outcomes.
Question 9
In the research method, generalisations may be made that will be applicable to other situations of the same type. What is this called? (UGC NET 25 June 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Cohort Study
  • B.Case Study
  • C.Panel Study
  • D.Blind Study
Correct Answer: Case Study

. A case study is a research design that allows researchers to gain concrete, contextual, and in-depth knowledge about a specific real-world subject. It involves intensive exploration of the key characteristics, meanings, and implications of the case under study.

 

In a case study, researchers focus on a single individual, group, organization, event, or phenomenon, delving deep into the details and context to understand its unique aspects. Despite its specific focus, a well-conducted case study can offer insights and findings that may be applicable to similar situations or cases of the same type.

 

This generalizability of findings from a case study to other comparable situations is one of the strengths of this research method. While case studies may not aim for broad generalizations like quantitative research, they do offer valuable information that can be used to inform and improve practices in similar contexts.

  • A cohort study is an observational study that follows a group of individuals over a period of time to study the occurrence of certain outcomes or events.
  • A panel study is a longitudinal study that involves repeatedly observing the same group of individuals over time to study changes or developments.
  • A blind study is an experimental study in which participants are unaware of the intervention or treatment they are receiving, designed to minimize bias in the results.

 

Question 10
Research that focuses on social inequality between men and women is called: (UGC NET 25 June 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Comparative Research
  • B.Longitudinal Research
  • C.Action Research
  • D.Feminist Research
Correct Answer: Feminist Research

Feminist research is grounded in the perspective that values women's experiences, needs, and perceptions of the social world. It aims to address and rectify gender disparities and bring about transformation in societal norms and practices. By adopting a feminist lens, this type of research seeks to understand and unpack the deliberate discrimination faced by women, even at the household level, which can lead to higher levels of unhappiness and morbidity among women.

 

The primary goal of feminist research is to achieve equitable social and economic development by shedding light on the issues and challenges faced by women. It emphasizes the importance of recognizing and addressing gender asymmetry in various aspects of society. Through feminist research, scholars and activists can advocate for policy changes and social reforms to promote gender equality and empower women.

 

Feminist research plays a crucial role in challenging traditional gender roles, advocating for women's rights, and promoting inclusivity in various domains, including education, politics, and the workplace. By elevating women's voices and perspectives, this research contributes to the broader goal of creating a more just and equitable society for all.

 

Question 11
The personalistic styles of writing a research report are permissible in which of the following research? (UGC NET 24 Sept 2020 Morning paper)A. Grounded theory researchB. Experimental researchC. Participant-observation based researchD. Historical researchE. Case study researchChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B and C only
  • B.B, C and D only
  • C.C, D and E only
  • D.A, C and E only
Correct Answer: A, C and E only

a. Grounded theory research: In grounded theory research, the focus is on collecting and analyzing data without any preconceived theoretical framework. The theory or explanation is developed "grounded" in the actual data collected during the research process. This approach encourages researchers to maintain a more personal and interpretive writing style while reporting their findings.

 

b. Participant-observation based research: This type of research involves the active participation of the researcher in the environment or group being studied. Researchers immerse themselves in the context of the study, observing and interacting with participants. This intimate involvement with the subject allows for a more personal and subjective account of the research, which can be reflected in the writing style of the research report.

 

c. Case study research: Case study research involves an in-depth examination of a specific subject or case within its real-life context. Researchers closely analyze the case, its complexities, and its contextual conditions. Due to the detailed and contextual nature of case studies, researchers often have the flexibility to use a personalistic writing style to better capture and convey the nuances and intricacies of the case under investigation.

Question 12

Action Research involves an iterative process, where the teacher can actively implement changes, observe the effects, and make further improvements based on the outcomes. It allows the teacher to take practical steps to bring about positive changes in the classroom environment and continuously refine the approach as needed. Question 13
Given below are two statements (UGC NET 24 Sept 2020 Evening paper)Statement I:All research adds to the corpus of knowledge by advancing a theory.Statement II:The focus of action research is basically on the amelioration of prevalent practices.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true

  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true
Correct Answer: Statement I is false but Statement II is true

Statement I: This statement is not entirely accurate. While research is a systematic process that contributes to the body of knowledge, not all research is specifically aimed at advancing a theory. Some types of research, like empirical research, are focused on gathering and analyzing data based on observations and experiences, without necessarily developing or proving a theory. Therefore, this statement is false.

 

Statement II: This statement is true. Action research is a type of research methodology that emphasizes practical problem-solving and continuous improvement in real-world settings. The primary focus of action research is to identify and address issues in existing practices to bring about positive changes and enhancements. It involves a cyclic process where data is collected, analyzed, and feedback is used to make improvements, and the cycle is repeated until the desired outcomes are achieved. The aim is to improve the current situation or practices rather than developing or testing theoretical frameworks.

Question 14
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 17 Oct 2020 Evening paper)Statement I: The goal of inquiry in fundamental research is directed at bringing an increment in the fund of knowledgeStatement II: Action research is a research by the practitioner, for the practitioner and of the practitioner.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are correct

Statement I: Fundamental research, also known as basic or pure research, is primarily driven by the pursuit of knowledge and understanding of underlying principles and concepts. Its main objective is to contribute to the existing pool of knowledge by advancing theoretical frameworks, developing new concepts, and gaining a deeper understanding of fundamental phenomena. The emphasis is on expanding the "fund of knowledge" within a particular field or discipline.

 

Statement II: Action research is a research approach that involves active participation and engagement of practitioners (often professionals or individuals working in real-world settings) in the research process. It is conducted by practitioners to address specific problems or challenges they encounter in their work environment. The research is aimed at bringing about practical improvements and positive changes within the context in which the practitioners operate. In other words, it is research that involves those who are directly affected by and involved in the practical implementation of the research outcomes.

Question 15
Given below are two statements: One is labelled as Assertion A and the other is labelled as Reason R: (UGC NET 17 Oct 2020 Morning paper)Assertion A: Data must be authentic before it can be of any value in a historical research, yet proof of authenticity does not establish its value, it must also be accurate.Reason R: External criticism is, therefore, referred to as lower criticism of the data.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both A and R are correct and R is the correct explanation of A
  • B.Both A and R are correct but R is NOT the correct explanation of A
  • C.A is correct but R is not correct
  • D.A is not correct but R is correct
Correct Answer: Both A and R are correct and R is the correct explanation of A

Historical research relies on various sources of data, including written narrative records of the past, diaries, letters, newspapers, minutes of meetings, reports, and even oral documentation. However, for the data to hold value in historical research, it must be authentic and accurate. Authenticity refers to the reliability and genuineness of the data, while accuracy indicates that the data is free from errors and represents the actual facts.

 

Reason R correctly states that the process of establishing the validity and authenticity of the data is referred to as external criticism. External criticism is a preliminary and preparatory step in historical research, where researchers evaluate the external features and form of the data to determine its authenticity. It involves examining the sources, checking for consistency, and ensuring that the data aligns with historical contexts and events.

Question 16
List I mentions various methods of research while List II offers their description.Match List I with List II (UGC NET 17 Oct 2020 Morning paper)List II. Experimental methodII. Ex-post facto methodIII. Descriptive survey methodIV. Ethnographic methodList II1. A detailed description of the way people believe and act in a particular society2. Studies designed to obtain information concerning the current status of phenomena3. Studying the effect of manipulating independent variable on dependent variable under appropriate control imposed4. Conducting a probe into casual factors on the basis of evidences manifest nowChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.I-1, II-2, III-3, IV-4
  • B.I-4, II-3, III-2, IV-1
  • C.I-2, II-1, III-4, IV-3
  • D.I-3, II-4, III-1, IV-2
Correct Answer: I-3, II-4, III-1, IV-2

a. Experimental Method: This research method involves studying the effect of manipulating an independent variable on a dependent variable while controlling other variables. It is typically conducted in a controlled setting to establish causal relationships between variables. Experimental research is commonly used in quantitative studies to test hypotheses and draw cause-and-effect conclusions. It helps researchers understand how changes in one variable influence another.

 

b. Ex-post facto Method: This type of research investigates situations or occurrences where the independent variables are not directly controlled by the researcher. These events or occurrences have already taken place, making them non-manipulable. Ex-post facto research is descriptive in nature and looks at cause-and-effect relationships without direct intervention. It involves studying already existing data to understand the relationships between variables and their impact.

 

c. Descriptive Survey Method: This research method is designed to obtain information about the current status of various phenomena. It involves collecting data from a sample or population through surveys, questionnaires, or interviews. Descriptive survey research helps researchers gain insights into attitudes, opinions, behaviors, and characteristics of a group or population. It provides a snapshot of the situation at a specific point in time.

 

d. Ethnographic Method: Ethnographic research involves a detailed description and study of the beliefs, behaviors, and practices of a particular society, culture, or group. Researchers immerse themselves in the natural setting of the subjects, engaging in long-term interactions and observations. Ethnographic studies seek to understand the cultural context and social dynamics, providing a holistic view of the group's way of life and its unique perspectives.

 

Question 17
Which argument may be advanced in support of action research in education? (UGC NET 17 Oct 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.The researcher breaks fresh ground in the field of enquiry
  • B.The knowledge is applied to extend further generalisations
  • C.Some new principles are formulated for explaining the events
  • D.The educational situation as well as the practitioner of education undergoes a change for the better.
Correct Answer: The educational situation as well as the practitioner of education undergoes a change for the better.

Action research is a systematic inquiry method in which teachers or practitioners engage as researchers in their own educational practice. When practitioners conduct action research, they find it to be an empowering experience with positive effects. One of the most significant reasons for this positive impact is that action research is always relevant to the participants. The researchers themselves, who are also the primary consumers of the findings, determine the focus of each research project. As a result, action research leads to positive changes and improvements in the educational situation and in the practices of the educators involved

Question 18
The critical difference between experimental and ex-post facto research lies in terms of: (UGC NET 17 Oct 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Selection of sample
  • B.Casual collection between two variables
  • C.Use of research tools
  • D.Control and manipulation of independent variable
Correct Answer: Control and manipulation of independent variable

Experimental research involves the manipulation of an independent variable by the researcher to observe its effect on the dependent variable while maintaining control over other variables. The researcher actively intervenes and controls the independent variable to establish cause-and-effect relationships.

 

On the other hand, ex-post facto research deals with variables that have already occurred, and the researcher does not have manipulative control over the independent variable. Instead, the researcher observes and studies the existing independent variable retrospectively in relation to its possible impact on the dependent variable. In ex-post facto research, the researcher must work with the variables as they naturally exist, and randomization, as commonly employed in experimental research, is not possible.

Question 19
There are two sets given below in which Set I offer Types of Research and Set 11 gives their description. Match the two sets: (UGC NET 13 Nov 2020 Morning paper)SET I (Types of Research)(a) Fundamental Research(b) Applied Research(c) Action Research(d) Case Study ResearchSET II (Description)(i) In-depth study with focus on typicality(ii) Intervention based ameliorative moves(iii) Exploring applicability of truths/principles to new situations(iv) Impact studies to watch effects(v) Adding to corpus of knowledge by formulating theory
  • A.(a) - (v), (b) - (iii), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
  • B.(a) - (i), (b) - (ii), (c) - (iii), (d) - (iv)
  • C.(a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (i), (d) - (v)
  • D.(a) - (ii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (v), (d) - (i)
Correct Answer: (a) - (v), (b) - (iii), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)

(a) Fundamental Research: Adding to corpus of knowledge by formulating theory

Fundamental research, also known as basic or pure research, aims to contribute to the existing body of knowledge by developing theories and improving our understanding of natural or other phenomena.

 

(b) Applied Research: Exploring applicability of truths/principles to new situations

Applied research is focused on finding practical solutions to immediate problems faced by society, industries, or organizations. It seeks to apply scientific knowledge and principles to real-world situations.

 

(c) Action Research: Intervention-based ameliorative moves

Action research combines action and research to examine specific questions or issues through observation, reflection, and deliberate intervention aimed at improving practices or solving problems in a particular context.

 

(d) Case Study Research: In-depth study with focus on typicality

Case study research involves in-depth and detailed examination of a subject of study and its contextual conditions. It aims to understand the unique characteristics and typicality of the case under investigation

Question 20
In which of the following research methods, manipulation and control of variables, and randomization of sample are two of the basic requirements? (UGC NET 13 Nov 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Ex-post facto research
  • B.Descriptive research
  • C.Case study research
  • D.Experimental research
Correct Answer: Experimental research

In experimental research, the primary goal is to establish causal relationships between variables. Researchers achieve this by actively controlling and manipulating the conditions that determine the events they are interested in studying. The experiment involves making changes in the value of one variable, known as the independent variable, and then observing the effect of that change on another variable, known as the dependent variable. The independent variable is the factor that is intentionally manipulated to observe its impact on the dependent variable.

 

Additionally, experimental research often involves randomization of the sample, which means that participants or subjects are randomly assigned to different experimental groups. Randomization helps ensure that any potential confounding factors are distributed evenly among the groups, making the results more reliable and generalizable.

 

Question 21
The personalized and contextualized references are permissible in which type of reporting of research? (UGC NET 13 Nov 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Experimental researches
  • B.Historical researches
  • C.Ethnographic researches
  • D.Survey based researches
Correct Answer: Ethnographic researches

Ethnography is a qualitative research approach that involves studying and observing the social interactions of individuals in a specific environment or cultural setting. In Ethnographic research, researchers immerse themselves in the context they are studying, often spending extended periods of time with the participants. They aim to gain an in-depth understanding of the participants' perspectives, beliefs, behaviors, and experiences.

 

Due to the immersive nature of Ethnographic research, researchers can include personalized and contextualized references in their reporting. They may provide detailed descriptions of the participants' views, actions, and experiences, as well as their interactions with the surrounding environment. These personalized and contextualized references enrich the research findings and offer a deeper insight into the world of the participants.

 

Question 22
A university teacher wants to study the relationship between socioeconomic status (SES) and achievement motivation of graduates enrolled for computer science. Which research method will be appropriate to use in this context? (UGC NET 13 Nov 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Experimental research method
  • B.Ex-post facto research method
  • C.Descriptive research method
  • D.Participant observation based method
Correct Answer: Ex-post facto research method

The ex post facto research design is a quasi-experimental method in which groups with pre-existing characteristics or qualities are compared on a dependent variable. In this case, the university teacher wants to study the relationship between socioeconomic status (SES) and achievement motivation of computer science graduates. Since the researcher cannot manipulate or assign participants randomly to different SES groups (as it is pre-existing), the ex-post facto design fits the context.

 

In an ex-post facto design, the researcher observes and analyzes the data based on the existing groups' characteristics (in this case, the socioeconomic status) and examines their impact on the dependent variable (achievement motivation). This type of research is valuable when randomization or manipulation of variables is not feasible or ethical, but researchers still want to understand the relationships between variables that have occurred naturallyThe ex post facto research design is a quasi-experimental method in which groups with pre-existing characteristics or qualities are compared on a dependent variable. In this case, the university teacher wants to study the relationship between socioeconomic status (SES) and achievement motivation of computer science graduates. Since the researcher cannot manipulate or assign participants randomly to different SES groups (as it is pre-existing), the ex-post facto design fits the context.

 

In an ex-post facto design, the researcher observes and analyzes the data based on the existing groups' characteristics (in this case, the socioeconomic status) and examines their impact on the dependent variable (achievement motivation). This type of research is valuable when randomization or manipulation of variables is not feasible or ethical, but researchers still want to understand the relationships between variables that have occurred naturally

Question 23
Which of the following shows the correct sequence in undertaking Action Research based studies? (UGC NET 12 Nov 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Planning, Acting on the plan. Observing and Reflecting
  • B.Acting on the plan. Observing. Planning and Reflecting
  • C.Reflecting, Planning. Acting on the plan and Observing
  • D.Acting on the plan. Reflecting, Planning and Observing
Correct Answer: Planning, Acting on the plan. Observing and Reflecting

Action Research is a research method characterized by its cyclical and participative nature. It involves a sequence of steps that tend to recur in a similar pattern. The key features of Action Research include its qualitative nature, focusing more on language than numbers, and its emphasis on critical reflection upon the process and outcomes at each cycle.

 

Stephen Kemmis has proposed a simple model of the typical action research process, which consists of four steps in each cycle:

 

  • 1. Planning: In this initial phase, the researcher devises a plan of action, outlining the steps to be taken to address the research problem.
  • 2. Acting on the plan: The researcher implements the planned interventions or actions based on the formulated plan.
  • 3. Observing: During this stage, the researcher observes and collects data on the outcomes of the implemented actions and interventions.
  • 4. Reflecting: The final step involves critical reflection upon the collected data and outcomes, evaluating the effectiveness of the actions, and identifying areas for improvement or further action.

 

 

 

Question 24
In which research design, the independent variable is 'selected' rather than 'manipulated'? (UGC NET 12 Nov 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Experimental research design
  • B.Historical research design
  • C.Ex post-facto research design
  • D.Descriptive survey research design
Correct Answer: Ex post-facto research design

The ex post facto research design is a non-experimental method that shares some similarities with a true experiment, especially regarding the separation of groups and the analysis of data. However, it is fundamentally non-experimental. In an ex post facto research design, the researcher does not have control over the independent variable.

 

Unlike experimental research designs where the researcher actively manipulates the independent variable to observe its effect on the dependent variable, ex post facto research designs are based on the existing attributes or characteristics of the subjects. The researcher selects participants based on pre-existing conditions or variables that have already occurred, rather than manipulating the variables.

 

Due to the absence of direct manipulation of the independent variable, ex post facto research cannot establish causality between variables definitively. However, it can suggest possible relationships or associations among variables. Ex post facto research is particularly useful when the researcher cannot or should not manipulate certain variables, especially in social sciences research where ethical considerations may preclude such manipulations.

Question 25
Given below are two statements, one is labelled as Assertion A and other is labelled as Reason R. (UGC NET 11 Nov 2020 Morning paper)Assertion A:The purpose of research is also to revisit the situations in a bid to ensure needed amelioration and improvement.Reason R:Action research is a format of research which is basically directed at bettering the situations.In the light of the above statements. choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A
  • B.Both A and R are true and R is not the correct explanation of A
  • C.A is true but R is false
  • D.A is false but R is true
Correct Answer: Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A

Action research, as described by Kurt Lewin, involves a comparative study of different forms of social action and research, leading to social action. It follows a spiral of steps, each of which involves planning, action, and fact-finding about the results of the action. The ultimate goal of action research is to create a simple, practical, and iterative process of learning, evaluation, and improvement, leading to better and more effective outcomes.

 

In essence, both Assertion A and Reason R align in emphasizing that research, particularly action research, aims to not only understand situations but also actively work towards improving them based on the research findings.

Question 26
Given below are two Statements, one is labelled as Assertion A and other is labelled as Reason R: (UGC NET 11 Nov 2020 Evening paper)Assertion A:In order to bridge the gap between theory and practice both fundamental and applied research formats have to be promoted.Reason R:Fundamental research focuses on theory making and applied research is directed at exploring the applicability of theory in varied practical situations.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.Both A and R are correct and R is the correct explanation of A
  • B.Both A and R are correct but R is NOT the correct explanation of A
  • C.A is correct but R is not correct
  • D.A is not correct but R is correct
Correct Answer: Both A and R are correct and R is the correct explanation of A

Fundamental research is focused on theory-making and aims to understand the underlying principles and mechanisms of how things work. It is driven by curiosity and the desire to expand knowledge in specific research areas. However, fundamental research may not have immediate practical applications.

On the other hand, applied research is directed at exploring the applicability of theories or knowledge gained from fundamental research in solving specific practical problems. The knowledge acquired from applied research is often used to develop products, procedures, or services with specific commercial objectives.

 

The explanation aligns with the assertion by highlighting the complementary roles of fundamental and applied research in connecting theoretical knowledge with practical applications. While fundamental research lays the groundwork for understanding the principles, applied research takes those principles and seeks to apply them in real-world contexts

Question 27
In which of the following methods of research, hypotheses are usually implied rather than being explicit? (UGC NET 11 Nov 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Descriptive survey method
  • B.Historical method
  • C.Experimental method
  • D.Ex-post facto method
Correct Answer: Historical method

Historical research involves the study of past events and phenomena based on available written records, documents, and other sources. In this method, the researcher evaluates historical evidence and seeks to understand the past through a careful examination of the available data.

 

While hypotheses are not always explicitly mentioned in historical research, they are often implied. The historian collects evidence and assesses its credibility and relevance to the research question. If the evidence aligns with the expected outcomes of a hypothesis, it is considered as supporting evidence. On the other hand, if the evidence contradicts the expected outcomes, the hypothesis is not confirmed

Question 28
In which of the following, there is a greater flexibility in both the methods and process of research? (UGC NET 11 Nov 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Ethnography and phenomenology
  • B.Descriptive survey and impact studies
  • C.Experimental and observation based studies
  • D.Ex-post facto and historical studies
Correct Answer: Ethnography and phenomenology

Phenomenology and ethnography are the options where there is greater flexibility in both the methods and process of research. Phenomenology is a philosophy that delves into the study of an individual's lived experiences within the world. Ethnography, on the other hand, is the study of culture, society, or community. Both of these approaches offer maximum flexibility in terms of the methods and process used in research, allowing researchers to deeply explore and understand the unique experiences and contexts of individuals and communities.

Question 29
In which method of research the independent variable is manipulated to observe and measure its effect on dependent variable? (UGC NET 09 Oct 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Ex-post facto method
  • B.Experimental method
  • C.Case study method
  • D.Historical method
Correct Answer: Experimental method

In experimental research, the researchers actively intervene by controlling and manipulating the independent variable to observe its impact on the dependent variable. This approach allows researchers to establish causal relationships and determine the cause-and-effect relationships between variables.

During an experiment, the independent variable is the factor that is intentionally changed or manipulated by the researchers to see how it affects the dependent variable. The dependent variable, on the other hand, is the outcome or response that is measured to assess the effect of the independent variable.

 

By conducting experiments, researchers can test hypotheses, draw conclusions, and make predictions based on the observed relationships between the variables. This method provides a rigorous and systematic approach to studying the cause-and-effect relationships between variables in a controlled environment.

Question 30
Statement I:Fundamental research is directed at exploring the applicability of truths and principles already established.Statement II:Action research aims at ameliorating the ongoing conditions and practices.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below: (UGC NET 05 Nov 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct
Correct Answer: Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct

Statement I is incorrect, as it describes Applied Research rather than Fundamental Research. Fundamental research is directed towards expanding scientific theories and improving the understanding and prediction of natural or other phenomena. It aims to advance fundamental knowledge about the world by creating or supporting theories that explain observed phenomena.

 

Statement II is correct. Action research is a type of research that aims to improve ongoing conditions and practices. It is a participatory research approach where the researcher and the participants work collaboratively to identify and address specific issues or problems in a real-world context. Action research involves a cyclical process of planning, acting, observing, and reflecting, with the goal of bringing about positive changes or amelioration in the situation being studied.

Question 31
What are the activities which take place during the stage of reconnaissance in action research? (UGC NET 04 Nov 2020 Morning paper)A. Identifying and classifying general ideaB. Describing the facts of the situationC. Explaining the facts of the situationD. Constructing a general planE. Developing the next action stepsChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.B and C only
  • B.A and B only
  • C.C and D only
  • D.D and E only
Correct Answer: B and C only

During the stage of reconnaissance in action research, the following activities take place:

a. Describing the facts of the situation: The researcher gathers preliminary information about the research problem and describes the current situation or context in which the study will take place.

 

b. Explaining the facts of the situation: The researcher seeks to gain a deeper understanding of the nature and context of the research problem. This may involve reflecting on personal beliefs, seeking insights from others, and exploring relevant literature.

Question 32
A teacher intends to establish the relationship between educational status of parents and the scholastic achievements of pupils. Which of the following method of research will be considered appropriate for this study? (UGC NET 04 Nov 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Philosophical method
  • B.Historical method
  • C.Ex-post facto method
  • D.Experimental method
Correct Answer: Ex-post facto method

Ex-post facto research is a type of research in which the researcher examines the possible causes behind an effect that has already occurred. It is particularly useful in social research when it is not feasible or ethical to manipulate certain variables. In this study, the teacher wants to investigate the scholastic achievements of pupils and considers the factor of their parents' educational status. Since the teacher cannot directly control or manipulate the parents' educational status, an ex-post facto research design allows them to explore the relationship between the variables without direct intervention.

Question 33
Which of the following methods is used in empirical researches? (UGC NET 05 Nov 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Inductive method
  • B.Deductive method
  • C.Initiative method
  • D.Scientific method
Correct Answer: Scientific method

Empirical research involves drawing conclusions from concrete and verifiable evidence. It relies on scientific experimentation and/or evidence to support its findings.

Empirical evidence is gathered using two main methods:

  • Quantitative research: This method involves gathering numerical data to quantify opinions, behaviors, or other defined variables. It follows a structured format and uses predetermined measures. Some commonly used methods in quantitative research include surveys, longitudinal studies, and polls.
  • Qualitative research: In this method, non-numerical data is collected to explore meanings, opinions, or underlying reasons from the subjects. Qualitative research methods are often unstructured or semi-structured, and the sample size is usually small. Focus groups, experiments, and interviews are some of the commonly used qualitative research methods.
Question 34
When the independent variable is explored rather than manipulated, to observe the effect on dependent variable, the method of research is called: (UGC NET 05 Nov 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Ex-post facto method
  • B.Experimental method
  • C.Case study method
  • D.Descriptive survey method
Correct Answer: Ex-post facto method

Ex-post facto research is a type of research where the researcher analyzes the possible causes behind an effect that has already occurred. Unlike experimental research, where the independent variable is manipulated, ex-post facto research involves exploring the independent variable as it naturally exists to observe its impact on the dependent variable. This method is particularly useful when true experimental designs are not practical or ethical to apply, making it a valuable alternative for studying cause-and-effect or correlational relationships in certain situations

Question 35
The research method which focuses on establishing causal relationships with controls among variables- independent, moderator and dependent, is called (UGC NET 01 Oct 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Ex post facto method
  • B.Survey method
  • C.Case study method
  • D.Experimental method
Correct Answer: Experimental method

In experimental research, investigators seek to establish causal relationships by carefully controlling and manipulating the conditions that determine the events they are interested in studying. The central aspect of an experiment involves introducing a change in the value of one variable, known as the independent variable, and then observing and measuring the effect of that change on another variable, known as the dependent variable. This setup allows researchers to investigate whether changes in the independent variable have a causal impact on the dependent variable.

 

Additionally, experimental research often takes into account the role of moderator variables, which can influence the strength or direction of the relationship between the independent and dependent variables. Moderator variables help researchers understand under which conditions or for which groups the causal relationship between the variables may vary.

Question 36
What is the usual sequence of steps in the scientific method? (UGC NET 01 Oct 2020 Morning paper)a. Hypothesis making by identifying the variablesb. Felt need which is creating the problemc. Identifying the difficulty and problem statement formulationd. Data analysis and interpretatione. Collection of data using appropriate research toolsChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, c, b, d, e
  • B.b, c, a e, d
  • C.c, d, e b, a
  • D.b, a, c, e, d
Correct Answer: b, c, a e, d

The usual sequence of steps in the scientific method is as follows:

a. Felt need which is creating the problem: The scientific method often starts with the recognition of a problem or a felt need. This could be a gap in knowledge, an unanswered question, or an issue that requires investigation.

 

b. Identifying the difficulty and problem statement formulation: Once the problem is recognized, it is essential to define and formulate it clearly. This involves identifying the key difficulties and issues that need to be addressed in the research.

 

c. Hypothesis making by identifying the variables: After formulating the problem, researchers develop hypotheses. Hypotheses are specific statements that propose a relationship between variables and serve as a basis for conducting the research.

 

d. Collection of data using appropriate research tools: With the hypotheses in place, researchers proceed to collect data using appropriate research tools and methods. This step involves gathering relevant information and evidence to test the hypotheses.

 

e. Data analysis and interpretation: Once the data is collected, it is analyzed using statistical or other relevant techniques to draw meaningful conclusions. The results are then interpreted to determine whether they support or refute the hypotheses.

Question 37
Which of the following research focuses on enhancing the corpus of knowledge in a given field? (UGC NET 04 Nov 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Action research
  • B.Applied research
  • C.Evaluative research
  • D.Fundamental research
Correct Answer: Fundamental research

Fundamental research, also known as pure research, aims to enhance the corpus of knowledge in a given field. It is a type of scientific research that focuses on improving scientific theories for a better understanding and prediction of natural or other phenomena. Fundamental research contributes to the advancement of fundamental knowledge about the world and plays a crucial role in creating, refining, or challenging theories that explain observed phenomena. This type of research is the source of new scientific ideas and innovative ways of thinking about the world. While fundamental research can take on various forms, explanatory research is the most common approach used to delve deeper into the underlying reasons and relationships behind observed phenomena

Question 38
Which of the following research method employs internal and external criticism for sifting as evidence and data? (UGC NET 04 Nov 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Ex post facto method
  • B.Experimental method
  • C.Historical method
  • D.Descriptive study method
Correct Answer: Historical method

The historical research method employs both internal and external criticism for evaluating and sifting evidence and data. Historical research is a systematic and objective approach that involves locating, evaluating, and synthesizing evidence to establish facts and draw conclusions about past events. In this method, the evaluation of historical data is conducted through historical criticism, which consists of two stages.

 

The first stage is external criticism, where the authenticity of the historical source is appraised. Researchers assess the credibility and reliability of the sources used in the study to ensure that they are accurate representations of the historical events being investigated.

The second stage is internal criticism, which involves evaluating the accuracy and worth of the data obtained from the historical sources. Researchers scrutinize the data to ensure its consistency, relevance, and reliability, and to determine if it can be used as evidence to support the conclusions drawn in the research.

By employing both internal and external criticism, historical research ensures that the data and evidence used in the study are credible, valid, and trustworthy, thereby enhancing the reliability and validity of the historical findings and conclusions.

Question 39
A college teacher intends to find out as to what extent students involvement in learning of boys and girls from rural/urban areas is attributable to the socio-economic status of the family from which they hail. What will be designated as an independent variable in this research project? (UGC NET 01 Oct 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Student involvement in learning
  • B.Socio-economic status of the family
  • C.Rural/urban areas
  • D.Gender (boys and girls)
Correct Answer: Socio-economic status of the family

In this research project, the independent variable is the socio-economic status of the family from which the students hail. The independent variable is the one that is manipulated or changed by the researcher to observe its effect on the dependent variable. In this case, the researcher intends to study the extent of students' involvement in learning, and to do so, they are looking at how this involvement varies based on the socio-economic status of the family.

 

On the other hand, the dependent variable is the one that is being observed or measured to see how it is affected by the independent variable. In this study, the dependent variable is the extent of students' involvement in learning, which is expected to be influenced by the socio-economic status of their families. Therefore, the socio-economic status of the family is the independent variable, and the students' involvement in learning is the dependent variable that is being studied in this research project.
