Question 43
In experimental research based studies, the observations derived from which of the following variables are considered for statistical analysis? (UGC NET 25 June 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.Independent variable
  • B.Dependent variable
  • C.Moderator variable
  • D.Control variable
Correct Answer: Dependent variable

In experimental research-based studies, the observations considered for statistical analysis are derived from the dependent variable. The independent variable is the one whose value is not influenced by any other variable, while the dependent variable's value is determined or derived from the value of the independent variable. The research aims to determine the value of the dependent variable, which changes based on the variations in the independent variable.

 

For instance, let's consider a study investigating the instances of cancer in people due to increasing air pollution. In this case, cancer would be the dependent variable, while the pollution levels would be the independent variable. The research aims to examine how changes in pollution levels (independent variable) impact the occurrences of cancer (dependent variable).

Quiz Attempt #119763

Total Questions: 22
Question 1
In grounded theory, researchers collect data using theoretical sampling until theoretical saturation is achieved. This process can be summarized in the following sequence. (UGC NET 05 Dec 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Sample theoretically decided → Collect data → Analyse data → Theoretical Saturation
  • B.General research question → Collect data → Sample theoretically decided → Analyse data → Theoretical Saturation
  • C.Sample theoretically decided → General research question → Collect data → Theoretical Saturation
  • D.General research question → Sample theoretically decided → Collect data → Analyse data → Theoretical Saturation
Correct Answer: General research question → Sample theoretically decided → Collect data → Analyse data → Theoretical Saturation

In grounded theory, researchers collect data using theoretical sampling until theoretical saturation is achieved. This process can be summarized in the following sequence:

(D) General research question → Sample theoretically decided → Collect data → Analyse data → Theoretical Saturation

 

Grounded theory, developed by sociologists Glaser and Strauss, is a qualitative research method aimed at generating theory inductively based on empirical data. Unlike traditional research approaches, grounded theory emphasizes simultaneous and iterative data collection and analysis. The process begins with a general research question that guides the study.

 

The first step involves purposefully selecting a small sample of participants who can provide rich and relevant data related to the research question. Data collection and analysis occur together and continuously. As the data is collected, it is analyzed and coded to identify patterns and themes.

 

The emerging theoretical ideas from the early analysis then guide the selection of the next set of participants for data collection. This iterative process continues, allowing researchers to build and refine their theories based on the collected data.

 

The key criterion for determining the sample size in qualitative research, including grounded theory, is Theoretical Saturation. Theoretical Saturation is reached when no new insights or information emerge from the data analysis. At this point, researchers consider that they have collected enough data to develop a comprehensive and meaningful theory.

Question 2
The time-frame in which a study explores a situation or problem is also called the: (UGC NET 26 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.reference period
  • B.age
  • C.longitudinal
  • D.retrospective time
Correct Answer: reference period

The reference period is a crucial aspect of survey design and research studies. It defines the specific time span for which respondents are asked to recall and report their activities, behaviors, experiences, or events of interest. It sets the boundaries within which the data will be collected and analyzed.

 

In many research studies and surveys, the reference period typically starts at a certain point in the past and ends at the time of the survey. For example, respondents may be asked to recall their activities over the past week, month, or year. This allows researchers to gather information about occurrences, frequencies, or changes in behaviors during that specific period.

 

Some surveys may have fixed reference periods, such as a calendar year or a calendar quarter, which is used consistently across all respondents. This standardizes the time-frame for data collection and enables easier comparisons and analysis of results.

 

The choice of the reference period depends on the research objectives, the nature of the study, and the type of data being collected. It is essential to carefully consider the appropriate reference period to ensure accurate and reliable data collection.

Question 3
Through which research method, the manipulation of an independent variable and its effect on dependent variable is examined with reference to a hypothesis under controlled conditions? (UGC NET 24 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Ex-post facto research
  • B.Descriptive research
  • C.Case study research
  • D.Experimental research
Correct Answer: Experimental research

The research method that examines the manipulation of an independent variable and its effect on a dependent variable under controlled conditions with reference to a hypothesis is known as Experimental research.

 

Experimental research strictly adheres to a scientific research design and involves the formulation of a hypothesis. In this type of research, an independent variable is manipulated by the researcher, and dependent variables are measured, calculated, and compared. The study is conducted in a controlled environment where all other variables are kept constant or controlled.

 

Question 4
In which of the following research studies interpretation and meaning get more attention than formulation of generalizations?(i) Historical studies(ii) Survey studies(iii) Philosophical studies(iv) Ethnographic studies(v) Hypothetical – deductive studies(vi) Ex-post facto studiesChoose your answer from the options given below: (UGC NET 24 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.(i), (ii) and (iii)
  • B.(iv), (v) and (vi)
  • C.(ii), (iv) and (v)
  • D.(i), (iii) and (iv)
Correct Answer: (i), (iii) and (iv)

In quantitative research, the formulation of generalizations through the testing of theories is a standard practice. However, in qualitative research, the primary focus is on providing a rich and contextualized understanding or interpretation of a specific aspect of human experience. Generalizing findings to a broader population is not the primary goal in qualitative research.

 

Historical studies involve an in-depth examination and interpretation of past events and contexts. Philosophical studies explore fundamental questions and ideas about existence, knowledge, values, reason, mind, and language. Ethnographic studies involve the intensive study of a particular culture or social group to gain insights into their beliefs, practices, and behaviors.

Question 5
In which of the following research paradigms the focus of concern is on interpreting reality in terms of participants perspective? (UGC NET 26 June 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Experimental Research
  • B.Ex-post facto Research
  • C.Ethnographic Research
  • D.Survey Research
Correct Answer: Ethnographic Research

Interpretive research methodology seeks to understand phenomena from the viewpoint of individuals, exploring interactions among them, as well as considering the historical and cultural contexts in which people exist. Those who follow the interpretive approach believe that quantitative research methods are insufficient to grasp complex social phenomena. Instead, they advocate for diverse qualitative techniques that allow for a deeper understanding of human experiences. These qualitative techniques often use human beings as the primary research instruments and encompass methodologies such as phenomenology, grounded theory, ethnography, case study, historical and documentary research, and ethno-methodology.

 

In ethnographic research, the researcher fully immerses themselves in the environment of the target participants to gain a comprehensive understanding of their goals, cultures, challenges, motivations, and emerging themes. Ethnography finds its roots in cultural anthropology, where researchers directly observe a culture, sometimes for extended periods, often engaging as a "participant observer." This method places importance on experiencing the environment firsthand rather than solely relying on interviews or surveys. By becoming a part of the social context being studied, researchers can gain rich insights into the lives and perspectives of the participants, allowing for a comprehensive.

Question 6
Which among the following is not the outcome of grounded theory research? (UGC NET 04 Dec 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Concepts
  • B.Narrative
  • C.Categories
  • D.Hypotheses
Correct Answer: Narrative

In grounded theory research, the outcome does not typically involve "Narrative" as one of its elements. The grounded theory approach involves collecting data, coding similar concepts, forming concepts into categories, generating theory, and verifying data in the field. The goal is to develop a theory that is grounded in the data collected from the research, and this is achieved by systematically analyzing and categorizing the data to identify underlying patterns and relationships among the concepts. The outcomes of grounded theory research usually include concepts, categories, and hypotheses that emerge from the data analysis and contribute to the development of a theoretical framework based on the empirical evidence.

 

 

Question 7
A university teacher plans to study the effect of level of aspiration of students in terms of their socio-economic background on their scholastic performance at the term end evaluation conducted by an external testing agency. What is the dependent variable in this study? (UGC NET 21 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Level of aspiration of students
  • B.Socio-economic background of students
  • C.Scholastic performance of
  • D.Term end evaluation
Correct Answer: Scholastic performance of

In experimental research, variables are factors or conditions that can exist in different amounts or types. There are three types of variables in an experiment: independent, dependent, and controlled variables.

 

The independent variable is the one that the researcher changes or manipulates in the study. It is the factor under investigation to observe its effect on other variables.

 

The dependent variable, on the other hand, is the variable that the researcher focuses on and measures to see how it responds to the change in the independent variable. It is the outcome or response variable that is expected to be influenced by the independent variable.

 

In this particular study, the university teacher plans to examine the effect of the level of aspiration of students (in terms of their socio-economic background) on their scholastic performance during the term end evaluation conducted by an external testing agency. Since the researcher is interested in observing how scholastic performance varies based on the level of aspiration, scholastic performance of students becomes the dependent variable.

Question 8
Participant observation is a part of: (UGC NET 21 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Philosophical research
  • B.Mentalist Theory of language
  • C.Mathematical research
  • D.Ethnographic research
Correct Answer: Ethnographic research

In Ethnographic research, the researcher immerses themselves in the environment of the participants to gain an in-depth understanding of their goals, cultures, challenges, motivations, and emerging themes. This research approach has its origins in cultural anthropology, where researchers directly observe a particular culture or community for an extended period, often for years. Instead of relying solely on interviews or surveys, the researcher becomes a "participant observer," meaning they actively engage in the everyday life and activities of the people within the chosen setting.

 

By being present in the natural context and interacting with the participants, the researcher can develop an "insider's view," experiencing and understanding what it is like to be a part of the group being studied. This approach allows for a comprehensive and holistic examination of the social phenomena and cultural practices within the community.

Question 9
Which of the following research formats focuses on hypothesis testing and generalizations’? (UGC NET 20 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Experimental and ex-post facto research
  • B.Intervention based action research
  • C.Phenomenological and narrative research
  • D.Case study research
Correct Answer: Experimental and ex-post facto research

Quantitative research is the research format that focuses on hypothesis testing and generalizations. Let's delve into the characteristics of quantitative research:

  • 1. Data is collected using structured and predetermined research instruments.
  • 2. Larger sample sizes are used to ensure representativeness of the population.
  • 3. The research study can be replicated or repeated, as it demonstrates high reliability.
  • 4. Researchers have well-defined research questions or hypotheses that can be tested to obtain answers.
  • 5. All aspects of the study are carefully designed before data collection.
  • 6. Data is presented in numerical form, often in tables, charts, figures, or other non-textual formats.
  • 7. The results can be generalized to broader concepts, predict future outcomes, or explore causal relationships.
  • 8. Researchers use tools like questionnaires or computer software to collect numerical data.
Question 10
Participation in which type of research has the great potential for ensuring the improvement of the professional as well as work situation? (UGC NET 21 June 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Fundamental research
  • B.Applied research
  • C.Evaluate research
  • D.Action research
Correct Answer: Action research

Action Research is a form of research that holds great potential for improving both the professional development of individuals and the work situations they are involved in. It is a disciplined process of inquiry conducted by and for those who are actively engaged in taking action. The main purpose of action research is to assist the participants in enhancing and refining their actions, leading to transformative change.

The concept of action research was introduced by Kurt Lewin, a professor at MIT, in 1944. It involves a simultaneous process of taking action and conducting research, which are connected through critical reflection. The ultimate goal is to bring about positive changes in the lives of the participants and their work environment.

Question 11
Which of the following action sets best represent an action research cycle? (UGC NET 20 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Reflect, act, plan and observe
  • B.Plan, act, observe and reflect
  • C.Observe, plan, reflect and act
  • D.Act, plan, observe and reflect
Correct Answer: Plan, act, observe and reflect

In an action research cycle, researchers follow a systematic process to bring about change and improvement in a particular context. The cycle typically involves the following steps:

  • 1. Plan: This is the initial stage where researchers carefully plan and design the actions they intend to take. They define the research questions, set clear objectives, and outline the strategies they will employ to achieve those objectives.
  • 2. Act: In this phase, the researchers put their planned actions into practice. They implement the strategies and interventions they designed during the planning stage. This step involves actively engaging with the situation or context they are studying.
  • 3. Observe: During the action phase, researchers keenly observe and collect data on the effects of their interventions and actions. They gather information about the outcomes, changes, and responses resulting from their implemented strategies.
  • 4. Reflect: After collecting the data, researchers enter the reflection phase. Here, they critically analyze and interpret the findings. They reflect on the outcomes of their actions and interventions, seeking deeper insights and understanding.

The significance of reflection lies in identifying what worked well, what didn't, and what unexpected outcomes occurred. This analysis informs the next cycle of planning and action, leading to continuous improvement and refinement of the interventions.

 

 

Question 12
Case studies are: (UGC NET 20 June 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Studies conducted in areas of genetics and microbiology.
  • B.In-depth examination of a subject and its related conditions.
  • C.A report on the existing sociopolitical condition.
  • D.Specialized research in the areas of health and sanitation.
Correct Answer: In-depth examination of a subject and its related conditions.

A case study refers to an intensive and systematic investigation or examination of a single individual, group, community, or any other distinct unit. During a case study, the researcher delves deeply into various aspects and data related to the specific subject of study. This approach involves analyzing multiple variables in the context of the subject under investigation. The main objective is to gain a comprehensive understanding of the complexities associated with the subject.

 

Case studies are conducted in a natural setting, allowing researchers to explore and comprehend intricate phenomena as they occur in real-life situations. By employing this method, researchers aim to enhance their understanding of the subject matter and draw insights that might not be easily obtained through other research approaches. Case studies are particularly valuable when seeking in-depth knowledge about a particular topic and when focusing on unique or exceptional cases.

Question 13
A college teacher does research with a view to depict the reality situations relating to home conditions of students and hostels provided for. Which of the following research format will be helpful to do so? (UGC NET 06 Dec 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Experimental research
  • B.Descriptive research
  • C.Participant observation-based research
  • D.Ethnographic research
Correct Answer: Participant observation-based research

Participant observation is a qualitative research method that involves the active engagement of the researcher with the research participants. In this approach, the college teacher would not only observe the students and their living conditions but also actively participate in their activities. By immersing themselves in the students' daily lives and experiences, the researcher gains firsthand insights into their home conditions and hostel situations.

 

This method allows the college teacher to closely observe and understand the behaviors, routines, and interactions of the students in their natural settings. By being present and involved, the researcher can capture nuanced details that might not be evident through other research methods. Participant observation is especially valuable when exploring complex social contexts and gaining an in-depth understanding of the participants' perspectives and experiences.

 

In contrast, the other research formats are less suitable for achieving the college teacher's specific objective:

  • a. Experimental research is not ideal for this situation because it typically involves controlled environments and the manipulation of variables, which may not be feasible or appropriate for studying home conditions and hostels.
  • b. Descriptive research, while focused on describing situations or phenomena, might not offer the same level of immersion and understanding as participant observation.
  • c. Ethnographic research, although involving the scientific description of human societies and cultures, might not fully capture the specific reality of home conditions and hostel experiences of the college students in the same participatory manner as participant observation.
Question 14
In an intervention-based action research process, which of the following is the usually recommended sequence? (UGC NET 06 Dec 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Plan, Act, Observe and Reflect
  • B.Observe, Plan, Act, and Reflect
  • C.Reflect, Plan, Act, and Observe
  • D.Observe, Act, Reflect and Plan
Correct Answer: Plan, Act, Observe and Reflect

To conduct action research, the researcher follows a systematic approach that involves several key steps:

  • 1. Plan: The first step is to develop a well-thought-out plan of action aimed at improving the existing situation or addressing a particular issue. During this phase, the researcher defines clear objectives, formulates research questions, and devises strategies for implementing the intended interventions.
  • 2. Act: With the plan in place, the researcher proceeds to put the proposed actions into practice. This involves implementing the strategies and interventions that were designed during the planning phase. The actions taken are typically targeted towards bringing about the desired changes or improvements.
  • 3. Observe: During the action phase, the researcher keenly observes and collects relevant data on the effects and outcomes of the implemented interventions. This observation is conducted within the natural context or setting where the actions are taking place. The data collected provides valuable insights into the actual impact of the interventions.
  • 4. Reflect: After gathering the necessary data, the researcher enters the reflection phase. In this stage, the data is carefully analyzed and interpreted. The researcher reflects on the observed effects and outcomes of the actions taken. This critical reflection serves as the basis for further planning, subsequent action, and iterative improvement through a series of cycles.

 

 

 

Question 15
Which of the following activities are performed by the researcher in an ethnographic research?(a) Conducts structured interview with the members of the community(b) Gets immersed in a social setting for an extended period of time(c) Listens to and engages in conversation(d) Tries to educate people about the harms of some evil practicesChoose the correct answer: (UGC NET 05 Dec 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.(a) and (b) only
  • B.(a) and (c) only
  • C.(b) and (d) only
  • D.(b) and (c) only
Correct Answer: (b) and (c) only

In ethnographic research, the researcher engages in specific activities to gain a deep understanding of the culture and lived experiences of the community under study. The correct activities performed by the researcher in an ethnographic research are as follows:

 

(a) Listens to and engages in conversation: Ethnographers actively listen to the members of the community and engage in conversations with them. This allows the researcher to gather valuable insights, narratives, and perspectives directly from the participants, enhancing the understanding of their culture and experiences.

 

(b) Gets immersed in a social setting for an extended period of time: Ethnographers immerse themselves fully in the social setting or community they are studying. They spend an extended period living and participating in the day-to-day lives of the people, which enables them to observe behaviors, rituals, customs, and interactions firsthand.

Question 16
A university teacher plans to improve the study habits of students in his/her class. Which type of research paradigm will be helpful in this regard? (UGC NET 04 Dec 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Evaluative research paradigm
  • B.Fundamental research paradigm
  • C.Applied research paradigm
  • D.Action research paradigm
Correct Answer: Action research paradigm

Action research has gained popularity in recent years and is considered an appropriate research paradigm for educational, professional, managerial, and organizational development. It involves collaborative, critical, and self-critical inquiry by practitioners, such as teachers or managers, into a significant problem or issue within their own practice or environment.

 

The key features of Action Research are as follows:

  • 1. Collaborative: Action research involves active collaboration between the researcher (in this case, the university teacher) and the participants (the students). The teacher works closely with the students to identify the study habits that need improvement and to develop strategies to achieve this goal.
  • 2. Critical and Self-critical Inquiry: Action research encourages a critical examination of the existing practices and seeks to find ways to enhance them. The teacher reflects on their own teaching methods and the students' learning behaviors, exploring areas for improvement.
  • 3. Problem-Oriented: The focus of action research is to address specific problems or concerns within the immediate context, in this case, improving study habits. The research is practical and directly applicable to the teacher's classroom and students.
  • 4. Practitioner-Driven: Action research is conducted by practitioners themselves, in this case, the university teacher. They take an active role in designing and implementing the research, making it relevant to their teaching practice.
Question 17
A university teacher intends to study the relationship between level of aspiration and achievement of rural children. Which design of research will be most appropriate in the context?(UGC NET 03 Dec 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Experimental research design
  • B.Ex Post Facto research design
  • C.Historical research design
  • D.Survey research design
Correct Answer: Ex Post Facto research design

Ex post facto study, also known as after-the-fact research, is a category of research design in which the investigation begins after the events or phenomena have occurred, without any interference or manipulation from the researcher. In social research, especially when it is not feasible or ethical to manipulate certain characteristics of human participants, ex post facto research designs are commonly employed.

 

This research design is particularly useful when studying variables that cannot be controlled or manipulated by the researcher. In the given scenario, the level of aspiration and achievement of rural children cannot be directly manipulated by the university teacher. Therefore, the teacher would opt for an ex post facto research design to examine the relationship between these variables as they naturally unfold in the real-world setting.

Ex post facto research is often utilized as an alternative to true experimental research, especially when testing hypotheses about cause-and-effect relationships. It allows researchers to explore associations and correlations between variables that have already occurred, even though the researcher did not have direct control over the variables during the study.

 

Question 18
Hypothesis testing is the main concept of which type of research? (UGC NET 03 Dec 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Experimental research
  • B.Historical research
  • C.Survey research
  • D.Exegetic research
Correct Answer: Experimental research

When conducting quantitative research, researchers aim to answer specific research questions or test hypotheses they have formulated. Hypothesis testing, also known as significance testing, is a crucial process within quantitative research methodologies.

The process of hypothesis testing involves several steps:

  • 1. Formulating a Research Hypothesis: The first step is to set a research hypothesis, which is a statement about the expected relationship between variables or the effect of an intervention. The hypothesis is based on the researcher's conceptualization of the research problem.
  • 2. Collecting Data: Researchers then collect data relevant to their research hypothesis through carefully designed experiments, observations, surveys, or other quantitative methods.
  • 3. Statistical Analysis: Once the data is collected, statistical analysis is performed to assess whether the results support or refute the research hypothesis. Various statistical tests, such as t-tests, ANOVA, chi-square tests, etc., are used to determine the significance of the findings.
  • 4. Drawing Conclusions: Based on the results of the statistical analysis, researchers draw conclusions about whether there is a significant relationship between variables or whether the intervention had a significant effect.

Experimental research is particularly well-suited for hypothesis testing because it involves manipulating one or more independent variables to observe their impact on a dependent variable. By conducting controlled experiments, researchers can make causal inferences and test the cause-and-effect relationships proposed in their hypotheses.

Question 19
In a research problem ‘studying the effect of Teaching Methods on the Scholastic Achievement of boys and girls in terms of their socio-economic background’. Which can be designated as independent variable? (UGC NET 02 Dec 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Scholastic achievement
  • B.Teaching methods
  • C.Gender
  • D.Socio-economic background
Correct Answer: Teaching methods

The independent variable is the factor that the researcher purposely manipulates or controls to observe its effect on the dependent variable. In this context, the independent variable is the Teaching methods, as the researcher can intentionally choose and implement different teaching approaches or methods for boys and girls based on their socio-economic backgrounds.

 

On the other hand, the dependent variable is the one that responds to the changes in the independent variable. In this case, the dependent variable is the Scholastic Achievement of boys and girls. The researcher aims to measure how the scholastic achievement of boys and girls varies based on the different teaching methods applied to them, considering their socio-economic backgrounds.

 

By analyzing the relationship between the independent variable (Teaching methods) and the dependent variable (Scholastic Achievement of boys and girls), the researcher can draw insights into how different teaching approaches impact the academic performance of students with various socio-economic backgrounds.

Question 20
A university department plans to undertake a study wherein attitudes, values and biases of teachers and students are to be probed with an eye on disclosing their patterns of adjustment. Which types of research methods will be considered appropriate in this context?(i) Experimental method(ii) Case study method(iii) Descriptive method(iv) Ethnographic method(v) Historical methodSelect the correct answer from the options given below: (UGC NET 02 Dec 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.(i) and (ii)
  • B.(ii) and (iii)
  • C.(iii) and (v)
  • D.(ii) and (iv)
Correct Answer: (ii) and (iv)

a. Case Study Method: The case study method involves in-depth observation and analysis of a single participant or a specific social group, such as a school class or a particular community. Researchers closely examine the case history or experiences of the individuals or groups to gain a comprehensive understanding of their attitudes, values, biases, and patterns of adjustment. Case studies allow for detailed investigations and offer insights into the complexities of the participants' behaviors and interactions.

 

b. Ethnographic Method: Ethnography is a qualitative research method in which researchers immerse themselves in the real-life environment of the study participants. They observe and interact with the individuals or groups in their natural settings to understand their social interactions, behaviors, and perceptions. By being participant observers, researchers can gain rich and contextual insights into the attitudes, values, and biases of teachers and students, as well as their patterns of adjustment within their respective social contexts.

 

The other research methods mentioned are as follows:

  • Experimental Method: This method involves manipulating an independent variable to observe its effect on a dependent variable, aiming to establish cause-and-effect relationships. However, experimental methods may not be suitable for investigating attitudes, values, and biases in a natural setting like the university department's study.
  • Descriptive Method: Descriptive research methods describe situations and events without making predictions or determining cause and effect. While they provide valuable information, they may not fully capture the complexities of attitudes, values, and biases and their patterns of adjustment.
  • Historical Method: Historical research delves into past events and influences that have shaped the present. While it offers insights into the historical context, it may not directly address the current attitudes, values, and biases of teachers and students in the university department.
Question 21
Which of the following sequences correctly reflects scientific investigation? (UGC NET 02 Dec 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Conceptualization, theorizing, deduced consequences, observation and testing
  • B.Testing, observation, conceptualizing, theorizing and deduced consequences
  • C.Theorizing, deducing consequences, testing, observing and conceptualizing
  • D.Observation, conceptualization, theorizing, deduced consequences and method to verify them
Correct Answer: Observation, conceptualization, theorizing, deduced consequences and method to verify them

Scientific investigation is a systematic approach used by scientists and researchers to answer questions about the world. It follows the scientific method, which involves a series of steps to formulate and test hypotheses. The correct sequence reflecting scientific investigation is as follows:

  • 1. Observation: The process begins with making observations about the phenomenon under study. Observations serve as the starting point for scientific inquiry.
  • 2. Conceptualization & Theorizing: Based on the observations, a hypothesis is formed—a testable explanation or proposition that seeks to explain the observed phenomenon.
  • 3. Deduced consequences: From the formulated hypothesis, predictions are made. These predictions are the expected outcomes if the hypothesis is true.
  • 4. Verification: The next step involves testing the predictions through experiments, observations, or other empirical methods. This testing aims to verify the accuracy and validity of the hypothesis.
  • 5. Iterate: The scientific process is often iterative. The results obtained from the verification step may lead to the formulation of new hypotheses or predictions, which will be subjected to further testing and refinement.
Question 22
There are two sets given below. Set - I specifies the types of research, while Set - II indicates their characteristics. Match the two and give your answer by selecting the appropriate code. (UGC NET Dec 2019)Set - I (Research types)(a) Fundamental research(b) Applied research(c) Action research(d) Evaluative researchSet - II (Characteristics)(i) Finding out the extent of perceived impact of an intervention(ii) Developing an effective explanation through theory building(iii) Improving an existing situation through use of interventions(iv) Exploring the possibility of a theory for use in various situations(v) Enriching technological resourcesCode:
  • A.a - (ii) b - (iv) c - (iii) d - (i)
  • B.a - (v) b - (iv) c - (iii) d - (ii)
  • C.a - (i) b - (ii) c - (iii) d - (iv)
  • D.a - (ii) b - (iii) c - (iv) d - (v)
Correct Answer: a - (ii) b - (iv) c - (iii) d - (i)

a. Fundamental research aims at advancing fundamental knowledge about the world and developing or contesting theories to explain observed phenomena. It involves developing effective explanations through theory building.

b. Applied research is the application of basic research fundamentals to solve specific, practical problems and aims at exploring the possibility of a theory for use in various situations.

c. Action research involves individuals or teams working together to improve the way they address issues and solve problems, leading to improvements in an existing situation through the use of interventions.

d. Evaluative research is a type of study conducted for evaluative purposes, aiming to find out the extent of perceived impact of an intervention.

Question 1
Which of the following sequences of research steps is nearer to scientific method? (UGC NET Jun 2018)
  • A.Suggested solution of the problem, Deducing the consequences of the solution, Perceiving the problem situation, Location of the difficulty and testing the solutions.
  • B.Perceiving the problem situation, Locating the actual problem and its definition, Hypothesizing, Deducing the consequences of the suggested solution and Testing the hypothesis in action.
  • C.Defining a problem, Identifying the causes of the problem, Defining a population, Drawing a sample, Collecting data and Analysing results.
  • D.Identifying the causal factors, Defining the problem, Developing a hypothesis, Selecting a sample, Collecting data and arriving at generalizations and Conclusions.
Correct Answer: Perceiving the problem situation, Locating the actual problem and its definition, Hypothesizing, Deducing the consequences of the suggested solution and Testing the hypothesis in action.

The scientific method is a systematic approach used in scientific inquiry to acquire knowledge and understanding of the natural world. It involves a series of steps that begin with the observation of a problem or phenomenon, followed by the formulation of a hypothesis to explain the observed phenomenon. The hypothesis is then tested through experimentation or data collection to gather evidence and draw conclusions.

 

The steps closely align with the scientific method:

  • 1. Perceiving the problem situation: This corresponds to the initial observation or recognition of a problem that needs to be investigated. 
  • 2. Locating the actual problem and its definition: This involves precisely defining the research problem to establish a clear focus for the study.
  • 3. Hypothesizing: Formulating a hypothesis is an essential part of the scientific method, where a potential explanation or solution to the problem is proposed.
  • 4. Deducing the consequences of the suggested solution: This step involves predicting the outcomes or consequences that would result if the proposed solution or hypothesis is correct.
  • 5. Testing the hypothesis in action: This step corresponds to the experimentation or data collection phase to gather evidence and validate or invalidate the hypothesis
Question 2

Question 4
In which of the following research methods the emphasis is laid on naturalistic settings and meaning-giving processes? (UGC NET 22 Dec 2018 Evening)
  • A.Case study method
  • B.Ex post facto method
  • C.Experimental method
  • D.Descriptive survey method
Correct Answer: Case study method

Naturalistic inquiry involves studying how people behave in genuine life experiences within their natural settings. In this approach, researchers aim to develop context-specific statements about the constructed realities of key participants. A case study is a research design used to gain in-depth, concrete, and contextual knowledge about a specific real-world subject, exploring its key characteristics, meanings, and implications.

Question 5
The characteristics of scientific method of research are: (UGC NET Dec 2018)(a) Empiricism(b) Objectivity(c) Systematic(d) Secretive(e) Security related(f) Predictive
  • A.(d), (e), (f) and (a)
  • B.(a), (b), (c) and (f)
  • C.(c), (d), (e) and (f)
  • D.(a), (b), (d) and (e)
Correct Answer: (a), (b), (c) and (f)

The scientific method of research is characterized by several key principles:

 

  • 1. Empiricism: The foundation of the scientific method is based on empirical evidence. All conclusions and claims are drawn from observable evidence or consequences that can be sensed or measured.
  • 2. Objectivity: Scientists strive to minimize bias and personal prejudices in their research. Objectivity is crucial to maintain impartiality and ensure that results are not influenced by the researcher's subjective views.
  • 3. Systematic: Scientific methodology involves a systematic approach to problem-solving. It follows a logical and organized process of observation, hypothesis formulation, testing, analysis, and interpretation of results. This systematic approach helps in refining knowledge and understanding. 
  • 4. Predictive: The scientific method aims to make predictions and test hypotheses. Through systematic observation and analysis, scientists develop predictions about the natural and social world, and then these predictions are tested to verify their accuracy.
Question 6
The research in which the independent variable is manipulated is termed as (UGC NET 19 Dec 2018 Morning)
  • A.Ethnographic research
  • B.Experimental hypothesis testing research
  • C.Non experimental hypothesis testing research
  • D.Hypothesis formulating research
Correct Answer: Experimental hypothesis testing research

Hypothesis-testing research aims to test a specific research hypothesis. This type of research can be conducted using either an experimental design or a non-experimental design. In the case of experimental hypothesis-testing research, the researcher deliberately manipulates the independent variable to observe its effect on the dependent variable. On the other hand, in non-experimental hypothesis-testing research, the independent variable is not manipulated, but its relationship with the dependent variable is still investigated.

 

It's worth noting that ethnographic research is a qualitative research method that involves researchers observing and/or interacting with study participants in their natural environment. Ethnography originated in anthropology but is now used across various social sciences. However, it is distinct from hypothesis-testing research, which focuses on testing specific hypotheses through experimental or non-experimental means.

Question 7
In which type of research, the steps of research have to be cyclic? (UGC NET 19 Dec 2018 Morning)
  • A.Action research
  • B.Experimental research
  • C.Grounded theory research
  • D.Case study research
Correct Answer: Action research

Coined by Kurt Lewin in 1944, Action Research is a unique approach that aims to bring about radical change by simultaneously taking action and conducting research in an interconnected manner. In this method, researchers actively engage in critical reflection on their own questions, beliefs, assumptions, and practices. The ultimate goal is to gain a deep understanding of the issues at hand and to develop and improve social practices.

 

According to Kurt Lewin, Action Research involves a spiral of steps, with each step composed of a circle of planning, action, and fact-finding about the results of that action. This cyclical or spiral nature of the research process allows for ongoing learning, adaptation, and refinement as the research progresses. It enables researchers to continually assess the impact of their actions and make necessary adjustments to achieve the desired outcomes. Action research cycle can be understood by the figure given below:

 

Question 8
For which type of research, the action words – ‘Control, manipulate and observe’ are most relevant? (UGC NET 19 Dec 2018 Morning)
  • A.Experimental research
  • B.Historical Research
  • C.Grounded theory approach-based research
  • D.Action research
Correct Answer: Experimental research

Experimental research aims to establish cause-and-effect relationships between two variables. In this type of research, one variable, known as the independent variable, is deliberately manipulated to observe its impact on another variable, known as the dependent variable. By controlling other variables that could potentially influence the outcome, researchers can isolate the effect of the independent variable on the dependent variable. Through careful observation and data analysis, experimental research seeks to draw conclusions about the causal relationship between the variables under study.

 

In contrast, historical research involves examining past events to gain insights and make predictions about the future. Grounded theory approach-based research focuses on developing theories and understanding social patterns through constant comparison and iterative data analysis. Action research, on the other hand, involves taking action to bring about radical change while simultaneously conducting research and reflecting critically on the process.

Question 9
Below are given a few key terms. Identify these which denote qualitative research paradigm. (UGC NET 19 Dec 2018 Morning)(a) Ex post facto method(b) Ethnography(c) Symbolic interaction(d) Descriptive survey(e) Narrative(f) Experimental method
  • A.(d), (e) and (f)
  • B.(a), (b) and (f)
  • C.(b), (c) and (e)
  • D.(a), (b) and (c)
Correct Answer: (b), (c) and (e)

Qualitative research is characterized by an inductive approach, where theories are developed based on the data collected. The methods used in qualitative research are flexible, and the focus is on understanding and interpreting the meanings and experiences of individuals or groups. Samples in qualitative research are typically small, and the researcher is considered as the research instrument. The data collected in qualitative research consists of words and narratives rather than numerical data.

 

  • 1. The term "Ethnography" refers to a qualitative research method where researchers observe and/or interact with participants in their natural environment to gain insights into their culture and behavior.
  • 2. "Symbolic interaction" is a perspective and method used in qualitative research that focuses on how individuals create and interpret symbols and meanings in their interactions with others.
  • 3. "Narrative" refers to the use of stories and personal accounts as a means of understanding human experiences and perspectives in qualitative research.
Question 10
In the two sets given below, Set - I specifies the methods of research while Set – Il describes the critical feature associated with a method of research. Match the two and select from the code to indicate your answer. (UGC NET 18 Dec 2018 Evening)Set -I (Research methods)(a) Experimental method(b) Ex post facto method(c) Historical method(d) Ethnographic methodSet – II (Critical features associated)(i) Generalizing to the population from a large sample(ii) Establishing the patterns of events which have happened, through primary and secondary sources(iii) Studying shared behaviour patterns(iv) Establishing cause and effect through control(v) Probing into the causal factors from the observed effectsCode:
  • A.a - (iv) b - (v) c - (ii) d - (iii)
  • B.a - (i) b - (ii) c - (iii) d - (iv)
  • C.a - (ii) b - (iii) c - (iv) d - (v)
  • D.a - (ii) b - (i) c - (iv) d - (iii)
Correct Answer: a - (iv) b - (v) c - (ii) d - (iii)

Here are the matches for the research methods and their critical features:

 

a. The experimental method is a systematic and scientific approach to research, involving the manipulation of one or more variables while controlling and measuring changes in other variables. Its primary objective is to establish cause-and-effect relationships through controlled experimentation. Researchers carefully design experiments to test hypotheses by altering the independent variable and observing its impact on the dependent variable. By controlling other variables, they ensure that any observed effects are a result of the manipulated variable, allowing them to draw meaningful conclusions about causal relationships.

 

b. Ex post facto research is employed when it is not feasible or ethical to manipulate variables as in true experimental research. In this type of research, the researcher investigates possible causes behind an effect that has already occurred. The critical feature associated with the ex post facto method is "Probing into the causal factors from the observed effects." Researchers analyze existing data and compare groups or conditions to identify potential causal relationships between variables after the effect has taken place. This method provides valuable insights into correlations between variables but does not establish causation due to the lack of experimental control.

 

c. Historical research involves a meticulous examination of written materials and oral documentation to understand past events and their implications. Researchers rely on available data such as written narrative records, diaries, letters, newspapers, and reports. The critical feature associated with the historical method is "Establishing the patterns of events which have happened through primary and secondary sources." By carefully analyzing primary and secondary sources, historians uncover patterns, gain insights, and construct narratives about past events. This method helps to illuminate historical contexts, cultural shifts, and social developments.

 

d. Ethnographic research is a qualitative method in which researchers immerse themselves in the real-life environment of study participants. The primary aim is to gain a deep understanding of participants' behaviors and experiences within their cultural context. The critical feature associated with the ethnographic method is "Studying shared behavior patterns." Through direct observation and interaction, researchers identify and analyze shared behavior patterns and cultural practices among participants. Ethnography allows researchers to capture rich data and unique insights into the social dynamics and lived experiences of individuals and communities

Question 11
The paradigm of research which focuses on the development of professional expertise of the researcher-practitioner is called: (UGC NET 18 Dec 2018 Evening)
  • A.Action research
  • B.Pure research
  • C.Qualitative research
  • D.Applied research
Correct Answer: Action research

Action Research, also referred to as practitioner-led or practitioner-based research, involves a self-reflective practice where the researcher carefully considers their actions. It is a collaborative process wherein researchers study themselves alongside other individuals engaged in similar activities. The main focus of action research is to enhance learning through action and reflection.

 

In action research, practitioners gather data, reflect on their actions, generate evidence from the data, and gradually draw conclusions based on various pieces of evidence. The process follows a cycle of planning, acting, observing, reflecting, and planning again.

 

  • Pure Research: Also known as basic research or fundamental research, it aims to improve scientific theories for a better understanding or prediction of natural phenomena. Basic research contributes to the advancement of fundamental knowledge about the world.
  • Qualitative Research: Primarily exploratory in nature, qualitative research seeks to gain insight into underlying reasons, opinions, and motivations. It helps in understanding problems, developing ideas, and formulating hypotheses for potential quantitative research. Qualitative research also uncovers trends in thoughts and opinions, delving deeper into the problem.
  • Applied Research: This methodology is used to solve specific, practical problems faced by individuals or groups. It finds applications in various fields like business, medicine, and education to develop solutions, cure diseases, solve scientific issues, or create technology.
Question 12
While presenting the research outcomes and sharing the same with others, in which of the following research type, the style has to be impersonal? (UGC NET 18 Dec 2018 Morning)
  • A.Narrative studies
  • B.Action research based studies
  • C.Ethnographic studies
  • D.Causal comparative based Ex post facto studies
Correct Answer: Ethnographic studies

When presenting research outcomes and sharing them with others, the research type that requires an impersonal writing style is Ethnographic studies (Option C). Ethnography is a qualitative research method where researchers observe and interact with study participants in their real-life environment over an extended period. In classical ethnography, the researcher maintains an objective and dispassionate approach, writing in an impersonal and impartial manner. The focus is on discovering the reality of the culture being studied, rather than imposing the researcher's perspective. This is achieved by neutralizing the researcher's presence and techniques of inquiry, adopting a stance of a 'native,' 'stranger,' or 'a fly on the wall.' The context is presented as existing independently of the methods used to study it.

 

Narrative studies involve gathering information through storytelling and writing a narrative of the experience. Action research based studies involve collaboration between the researcher and a client to diagnose and solve organizational problems. Causal comparative based Ex post facto studies aim to find relationships between variables after an event has occurred by comparing groups of individuals

Question 13
Which among the following provides the strongest evidence of cause-and-effect relationship between independent and dependent variables? (UGC NET 21 Dec 2018 Evening)
  • A.Descriptive statistics
  • B.Non-experimental approach
  • C.Co relational approach
  • D.Experimental approach
Correct Answer: Experimental approach

The experimental approach provides the strongest evidence of a cause-and-effect relationship between independent and dependent variables. In experimental research, a scientific approach is used, where one set of variables is manipulated and kept constant while the other set of variables is measured as the subject of the experiment. This controlled manipulation allows researchers to establish a clear cause-and-effect relationship, ensuring that observed effects are directly attributed to the manipulated cause.

Question 14
Participatory research is also described as: (UGC NET 21 Dec 2018 Morning)
  • A.Group-based
  • B.Individual-based
  • C.Community-based
  • D.Government-based
Correct Answer: Community-based

Participatory research is often described as community-based. It encompasses various methodological approaches and techniques aimed at empowering research participants, who are typically members of the community or community-based organizations. In this type of research, the participants have significant control over the research agenda, the process, and the actions taken. Importantly, the individuals involved in the research are actively engaged in analyzing and reflecting on the generated information, leading to the discovery of findings and conclusions derived from the research process.

Question 15
Which of the following is an incorrect statement? (UGC NET 21 Dec 2018 Morning)
  • A.Archival research uses data collected and sometimes coded by someone else.
  • B.Ex post facto research uses data that you collected before you came up with your hypothesis.
  • C.Using a scatterplot to graph your Correlational data will not tell you the direction of the relationship (positive or negative).
  • D.Observational methods are used in both Correlational and experimental research
Correct Answer: Using a scatterplot to graph your Correlational data will not tell you the direction of the relationship (positive or negative).

Statement C is incorrect because using a scatterplot to graph correlational data can indeed tell you the direction of the relationship (positive or negative). Scatterplots visually display the relationship between two variables, and the pattern of points on the plot can indicate the direction of the relationship. A positive relationship shows an upward trend, while a negative relationship shows a downward trend. The correlation coefficient also quantifies the direction and strength of the relationship, ranging from -1.00 to +1.00.

Question 16
Which of the sets of activities best indicate the cyclic nature of action research strategy? (UGC NET Jul 2018)
  • A.Reflect, Observe, Plan, Act
  • B.Observe, Act, Reflect, Plan
  • C.Act, Plan, Observe, Reflect
  • D.Plan, Act, Observe, Reflect
Correct Answer: Plan, Act, Observe, Reflect

According to Kurt Lewin, the process of action research involves a spiral of steps, where each step consists of a circle of planning, action, and fact-finding about the result of the action. This iterative process allows researchers to plan their actions, carry them out, observe the outcomes, and critically reflect on the consequences. The reflections then inform the next cycle of planning and action, creating a continuous and dynamic loop of learning and improvement in the pursuit of radical change and the enhancement of social practices.
