Question 17
A variable that measures the effect of a manipulated variable, is known as: (UGC NET 19 Dec 2018 Evening)
  • A.Independent variable
  • B.Confounding variable
  • C.Dependent variable
  • D.Controlled variable
Correct Answer: Dependent variable

In a research study, the dependent variable (DV) is the variable that is being measured or observed to determine the effect of the independent variable (IV). The independent variable is the variable that the researcher manipulates or controls to see how it influences the dependent variable. The relationship between the two variables is often studied to understand cause-and-effect relationships.

 

For example, if a researcher is investigating how different teaching methods affect students' test scores, the independent variable would be the teaching method (e.g., traditional lecture vs. interactive group discussions), and the dependent variable would be the students' test scores. The researcher manipulates the teaching method (IV) to see how it impacts the students' test scores (DV).

Question 18
A variable that is manipulated is known as: (UGC NET Dec 2018)
  • A.Dependent variable
  • B.Control variable
  • C.Independent variable
  • D.Confounding variable
Correct Answer: Independent variable

A variable that is manipulated or controlled by the researcher is known as the independent variable (IV). The independent variable is the causative or predictor variable that contributes to the changes in the dependent variable (DV), which is the variable being measured or observed to determine the effect of the independent variable. In a research study, the researcher manipulates the independent variable to study its influence on the dependent variable. The control variable is a factor held constant to test the relative impact of the independent variable. An antecedent variable explains a relationship between two variables based on its prior impact on them. An intervening variable helps explain an observed association between two variables and can affect the relationship between the dependent and independent variables.

Question 19
Which of the following research types focuses on ameliorating the prevailing situations? (UGC NET Nov 2017)
  • A.Fundamental Research
  • B.Applied Research
  • C.Action Research
  • D.Experimental Research
Correct Answer: Action Research

Action research is characterized by being either initiated to solve an immediate problem or conducted as a reflective process of progressive problem-solving. It is undertaken by individuals working with others in teams or as part of a "community of practice" with the aim of improving the way they address issues and solve problems. The essence of action research lies in actively participating in a change situation while simultaneously conducting research. It can be carried out by individuals within an existing organization or by larger organizations and institutions, often with the assistance or guidance of professional researchers, to enhance their strategies, practices, and knowledge of the environments within which they operate. The main goal of action research is to bring about positive and meaningful changes in real-life situations by combining practical action with rigorous research methods.

Question 20
A researcher attempts to evaluate the effect of method of feeding on anxiety - proneness of children. Which method of research would be appropriate for this? (UGC NET Nov 2017)
  • A.Case study method
  • B.Experimental method
  • C.Ex-post-facto method
  • D.Survey method
Correct Answer: Ex-post-facto method

The most suitable method of research for evaluating the effect of the method of feeding on anxiety-proneness of children would be the Ex-post-facto method.

 

a. A case study involves an in-depth examination of a specific subject of study and its contextual conditions. It may not be suitable for assessing the effects of a particular method on anxiety-proneness across a broader group.

 

b. Experimental research involves manipulating variables to establish cause-and-effect relationships. While it can be powerful, it may not be ethically feasible to manipulate feeding methods in a controlled setting for children.

 

c. The Ex-post-facto method is suitable when the researcher observes the effect (anxiety-proneness) after the cause (method of feeding) has already occurred. It is ideal for situations where the researcher cannot manipulate the variables directly. In this case, the researcher can compare different groups of children based on their method of feeding and assess their anxiety-proneness, making the Ex-post-facto method the most appropriate choice for this research scenario.

 

d. The survey method involves collecting data from individuals by asking them questions. While surveys are valuable for gathering opinions and behavioral information, they may not be as effective in evaluating the direct effect of a method of feeding on anxiety-proneness, especially without observing the cause and effect relationship over time.

Question 21
In doing action research what is the usual sequence of steps? (UGC NET Jan 2017)
  • A.Reflect, observe, plan, act
  • B.Plan, act, observe, reflect
  • C.Plan, reflect, observe, act
  • D.Act, observe, plan, reflect
Correct Answer: Plan, act, observe, reflect

 

Action Research, a term coined by Kurt Lewin in 1944, involves a process of seeking radical change by taking action and conducting research in a linked manner with critical reflection. The researchers start with planning, where they develop a plan to address a specific problem or improve a situation. After planning, they take action based on the developed plan.

 

Once the action is taken, they move on to the observation phase, where they closely monitor and observe the effects of the action on the situation. This step involves gathering data and information about the outcomes of the implemented actions.

 

Finally, the researchers engage in critical reflection. They analyze the consequences of their actions, reflect on the results, and evaluate the effectiveness of the changes made. This reflective process helps them gain insights and understanding, leading to further refinements or adjustments in the action plan.

 

Kurt Lewin described this process as a "spiral of steps," with each step comprising a circle of planning, action, and fact-finding about the results. This cyclic process allows for continuous improvement and learning throughout the action research journey. Action research cycle can be understood by the figure given below:

 

Question 22
Below are given two sets – research methods (Set-I) and data collection tools (Set-II). Match the two sets and indicate your answer by selecting the correct code: (UGC NET Jan 2017)Set – I (Research Methods)a. Experimental methodb. Ex post-facto methodc. Descriptive survey methodd. Historical methodSet – II (Data Collection Tools)i. Using primary and secondary sourcesii. Questionnaireiii. Standardized testsiv. Typical characteristic testsCodes:
  • A.a – iii, b – i, c – ii, d - iv
  • B.a – iii, b – iv, c – ii, d - i
  • C.a – ii, b – iii, c – I, d - iv
  • D.a – ii, b – iv, c – iii, d - i
Correct Answer: a – iii, b – iv, c – ii, d - i

The correct match between the research methods (Set-I) and data collection tools (Set-II) is as follows:

 

a. Experimental method: This research method involves manipulating one or more independent variables to observe their effects on dependent variables. It is a controlled and systematic approach to study cause-and-effect relationships.

 

b. Ex post-facto method: Ex-post-facto research is a type of empirical inquiry in which the researcher does not have direct control over the independent variables because they have already occurred or cannot be manipulated. It involves studying the effects of variables that are beyond the researcher's control.

 

c. Descriptive survey method: The survey method involves posing questions to individuals or groups to gather data about their opinions, attitudes, behaviors, or characteristics. Questionnaires and interviews are common data collection tools used in this method.

 

d. Historical method: The historical research method involves learning about the history of a subject or field before conducting an analysis. It provides insights into the past context, which can aid in a more accurate analysis of the subject under study.

Question 23
The principal of a school conducts an interview session of teachers and students with a view to explore the possibility of their enhanced participation in school programmes. This endeavour may be related to which type of research? (UGC NET Jan 2017)
  • A.Evaluation Research
  • B.Fundamental Research
  • C.Action Research
  • D.Applied Research
Correct Answer: Action Research

Action research is a research methodology that combines action and research to address specific questions or issues within a particular context. It involves active participation and collaboration of the researcher with the individuals or community being studied. The primary goal of action research is to improve practice and bring about positive changes by identifying practical solutions to immediate problems or challenges.

 

In this case, the principal is engaging in action research by actively seeking input from teachers and students to understand their perspectives and experiences related to school programs. By conducting interviews, the principal aims to gain insights into the factors that may enhance participation in the programs and subsequently make informed decisions to improve the school's practices.

 

Action research is particularly useful in educational settings as it allows educators and administrators to work together to identify and implement improvements that directly impact the learning environment and student outcomes. Through this collaborative and participatory approach, action research facilitates ongoing reflection and continuous improvement in educational practices.

Question 24
There are two sets given below, Set-I consists of methods of research and Set-II indicates their procedural characteristics. Match the two sets and choose your answer from the codes given below: (UGC NET Aug 2016)Set – I (Research method)a. Experimental methodb. Ex-post facto methodc. Descriptive methodd. Symbolic interactionisme. Action researchSet – II (Procedural Characteristics)i. Interventions to ameliorate a given situationii. Explaining patterns of behaviour in terms of meanings and their representations which people share.iii. Manipulating an independent variable in controlled conditions and measuring its effect on dependent variable.iv. Depending on primary and secondary sources of data.v. Obtaining information concerning the current status of phenomena.vi. Observing the effect on dependent variable and making probes into factors/variables which explain it.vii. Exegetic analysis.Codes:
  • A.a – iii, b – i, c – iv, d – v, e - vii
  • B.a – iii, b – iv, c – v, d – vi, e - vii
  • C.a – iii, b – i, c – ii, d – iv, e - v
  • D.a – iii, b – vi, c – v, d – ii, e - i
Correct Answer: a – iii, b – vi, c – v, d – ii, e - i

The correct match between the research methods (Set-I) and their procedural characteristics (Set-II) is as follows:

 

a. Experimental method involves manipulating an independent variable in controlled conditions to observe its effect on the dependent variable. It is a fundamental research approach that allows researchers to establish cause-and-effect relationships. By controlling variables, researchers can draw precise conclusions about the impact of specific interventions or treatments.

 

b. Ex-post facto method focuses on exploring the possible causes behind an effect that has already occurred. This method is ideal when researchers cannot manipulate variables due to ethical or practical constraints. It helps test hypotheses about causal relationships, although it does not establish definitive causality.

 

c. Descriptive research, as the name suggests, aims to describe situations, phenomena, or behaviors without making causal claims. It provides a detailed account of the current status or characteristics of the subject under study. Descriptive methods are valuable in understanding the prevalence of certain behaviors or attitudes within a population.

 

d. Symbolic interactionism, although not a research method per se, is a sociological theoretical perspective. It emphasizes the role of individual interactions and shared meanings in shaping society. Researchers adopting this perspective often use qualitative methods like interviews and observations to explore how people construct their social realities through interactions.

 

e. Action research is a unique research approach that seeks radical change by taking action and conducting research simultaneously. Researchers actively participate in solving real-life problems while critically reflecting on their actions and outcomes. This method is often used in education and social contexts to improve practices and strategies by actively involving stakeholders in the research process.

Question 25
A researcher intends to explore the effect of possible factors for the organization of effective mid-day meal interventions. Which research method will be most appropriate for this study? (UGC NET Jun 2016)
  • A.Historical method
  • B.Descriptive survey method
  • C.Experimental method
  • D.Ex-post-facto method
Correct Answer: Ex-post-facto method

For a researcher intending to explore the effect of possible factors for the organization of effective mid-day meal interventions, the most appropriate research method would be the Ex-post-facto method. This research method involves studying the possible causes behind an effect that has already occurred. It is particularly useful when the researcher cannot manipulate variables directly due to ethical or practical reasons.

  • Experimental research, on the other hand, is used when researchers intend to establish cause-and-effect relationships. It typically involves controlled observations in a laboratory setting, where variables are manipulated to study their effects.
  • Historical research involves studying the history of a subject or field to gain insights into its past context and culture. While it provides valuable historical perspective, it may not be the best fit for exploring the effectiveness of mid-day meal interventions.
  • Descriptive research methods focus on describing situations and phenomena without making causal claims. They are useful for providing a detailed account of current characteristics or prevalence of certain behaviors within a population.
Question 26
Jean Piaget gave a theory of cognitive development of humans on the basis of his: (UGC NET Jun 2015)
  • A.Fundamental Research
  • B.Applied Research
  • C.Action Research
  • D.Evaluation Research
Correct Answer: Fundamental Research

Jean Piaget's theory of cognitive development, which encompasses the nature and growth of human intelligence, is based on fundamental research. This theory delves into the process through which humans acquire, construct, and utilize knowledge. Jean Piaget's work focuses on the essence of knowledge itself, and his developmental stage theory is a result of extensive fundamental research conducted by him

Question 27
The conclusions/findings of which type of research cannot be generalized to other situations? (UGC NET Jun 2015)
  • A.Historical Research
  • B.Descriptive Research
  • C.Experimental Research
  • D.Causal Comparative Research
Correct Answer: Historical Research

Historical research involves studying, understanding, and interpreting past events to gain insights and conclusions about people or occurrences from the past. It goes beyond merely compiling factual information and involves interpretation of historical data such as documents and diaries. The main focus of historical research is to analyze and interpret historical records to shed light on specific individuals, social issues, and connections between the past and the present.

  • Descriptive Research is used to describe characteristics of a population or phenomenon being studied without answering questions about how, when, or why those characteristics occurred. It is concerned with the "what" question, seeking to identify and categorize the characteristics of the subject of study.
  • Experimental Research follows a scientific approach with controlled variables to establish cause-and-effect relationships between different sets of variables. It involves manipulating one set of variables while measuring the effects on another set, aiming to draw conclusions about the causal relationship between the variables.
  • Causal Comparative Research seeks to find relationships between independent and dependent variables after an action or event has already occurred. It involves comparing groups of individuals to determine whether the independent variable influenced the outcome, or dependent variable.
Question 28
Which of the following statements is not true in the context of participatory research? (UGC NET Dec 2015)
  • A.It recognizes knowledge as power.
  • B.It emphasises on people as experts.
  • C.It is a collective process of enquiry.
  • D.Its sole purpose is production of knowledge
Correct Answer: Its sole purpose is production of knowledge

Participatory research is an approach that goes beyond the traditional researcher-subject relationship and actively involves the community or participants in the research process. The other statements are true and characteristic features of participatory research:

 

(a) It recognizes knowledge as power: Participatory research acknowledges that individuals and communities possess valuable knowledge and expertise about their own experiences and contexts. It values the local knowledge and insights that participants bring to the research process.

 

(b) It emphasizes on people as experts: In participatory research, the community members are considered experts in their own lives and realities. They are active collaborators in the research process, sharing their perspectives and experiences, which contribute to a more comprehensive understanding of the research topic.

 

(c) It is a collective process of enquiry: Participatory research involves collective decision-making and problem-solving. It fosters a collaborative environment where researchers and participants work together to identify research questions, design methodologies, and interpret findings.

Question 29
When planning to do as social research, it is better to (UGC NET Dec 2014)
  • A.approach the topic with an open mind
  • B.do a pilot study before getting stuck into it
  • C.be familiar with literature on the topic
  • D.forget about theory because this is a very practical
Correct Answer: be familiar with literature on the topic

Social science research involves systematically understanding social facts or phenomena. It aims to gather information about the social world, interpret it, and make decisions based on the findings or develop new knowledge. The research attempts to explore cause-and-effect relationships related to social issues and provide answers or solutions to social problems. Like research in natural sciences, social research aims to discover new facts or validate existing social facts. Additionally, it seeks to develop new scientific tools, concepts, and theories that enhance the study of human behavior and social life. Being familiar with the existing literature on the topic is crucial as it provides a foundation for building on previous research, understanding gaps in knowledge, and designing a well-informed and meaningful study

Question 30
The research stream of immediate application is (UGC NET Jun 2014)
  • A.Conceptual research
  • B.Action research
  • C.Fundamental research
  • D.Empirical research
Correct Answer: Action research

Action research is an approach where the researcher collaborates with a client to diagnose a problem and develop a solution based on the diagnosis. It involves a close partnership between the researcher and the organization to solve real-world problems. Action research is characterized by its focus on practical applications and its involvement in the dynamic social world, recognizing that both the researcher and the research are part of the ongoing change process.

  • Conceptual research, on the other hand, involves the observation and analysis of existing information on a given topic without conducting practical experiments. It is a theoretical exploration of ideas and concepts.
  • Fundamental research, also known as basic research or pure research, aims to gather knowledge for the sake of knowledge. It seeks to make generalizations about phenomena and contributes to the pool of fundamental knowledge in a particular research area.
  • Empirical research relies on observed and measured phenomena to derive knowledge from actual experiences. It involves specific research questions, a defined population or behavior being studied, and a process that includes experimentation, direct or indirect observation, and experience.
Question 31
In which of the following methods of research the independent variable has to be selected rather than manipulated? (UGC NET Dec 2013)
  • A.Descriptive survey method
  • B.Ex post facto method
  • C.Experimental method
  • D.Exegetic research
Correct Answer: Ex post facto method

In Ex post facto research, the researcher examines possible causes behind an effect that has already occurred. This method is particularly useful in social research when it is not feasible or ethical to manipulate the characteristics of human participants. Ex post facto research serves as an alternative to true experimental research and allows researchers to test hypotheses related to cause-and-effect or correlational relationships without manipulating variables in a controlled experiment. It offers valuable insights into relationships between variables after the effect has taken place, without direct manipulation of the independent variable.

Question 32
The principles of fundamental research are used in (UGC NET Dec 2013)
  • A.action research
  • B.applied research
  • C.philosophical research
  • D.historical research
Correct Answer: applied research

Applied research takes the knowledge and insights gained from fundamental research and applies it to practical purposes. It aims to improve scientific knowledge and can lead to the discovery and development of new technologies or solutions to real-world problems.

 

Fundamental research, on the other hand, focuses on gaining knowledge for the sake of knowledge itself. It seeks to make generalizations about phenomena and aims to answer questions about why, what, or how things work. Fundamental research contributes to the pool of fundamental knowledge in a specific research area, laying the groundwork for further studies and advancements.

Question 33
The variable which impacts the relationship between an independent variable and a dependent variable is known as (UGC NET Sep 2013)
  • A.antecedent variable
  • B.dependent variable
  • C.predictor variable
  • D.control variable
Correct Answer: antecedent variable

The dependent variable is the one that researchers seek to explain or understand better. It represents the effect or outcome that is being studied.

 

On the other hand, the independent variable is the cause or factor that is believed to have an impact on the dependent variable. It is the variable that researchers manipulate or control to observe its effect on the dependent variable.

 

A control variable is a factor that researchers hold constant during the study to isolate the impact of the independent variable on the dependent variable.

 

In this case, the correct answer is "A" - antecedent variable. An antecedent variable is a specific type of intervening variable that explains or partially explains the relationship between two other variables (X and Y) based on its prior impact on these variables. It helps us understand how certain factors may influence the relationship between the independent and dependent variables

Question 34
The research that aims at immediate application is (UGC NET Jun 2012)
  • A.Action Research
  • B.Empirical Research
  • C.Conceptual Research
  • D.Fundamental Research
Correct Answer: Action Research

Action research is a type of research that is initiated to solve an immediate problem or to address real-world issues. It involves a reflective and progressive problem-solving process undertaken by individuals working collaboratively with others, often as part of a "community of practice." The primary objective of action research is to improve the way individuals or organizations address issues and solve problems in practical settings.

 

There are two main types of action research: participatory and practical. In participatory action research, individuals actively participate in bringing about change and improvement in their own context. They are both researchers and active participants in the change process. Practical action research can also be conducted by larger organizations or institutions, where professional researchers assist or guide the process to enhance their strategies, practices, and knowledge within their operating environments.

Question 35
The study in which the investigators attempt to trace an effect is known as : (UGC NET Jun 2007)
  • A.Survey Research
  • B.Ex-post Facto Research
  • C.Historical Research
  • D.Summative Research
Correct Answer: Ex-post Facto Research

Ex-post facto research is a type of systematic empirical inquiry in which the researcher aims to trace an effect. In this research approach, the investigator does not have direct control over the independent variables being studied because their manifestations have "already occurred" or are inherently not manipulated by the researcher.

 

In ex-post facto research, the investigator retrospectively examines the existing data or conditions to understand and analyze the effects or outcomes of the observed variables. It allows researchers to explore correlations or associations between variables and make inferences about cause-and-effect relationships based on the available data.

Question 36
Ex Post Facto research means (UGC NET Jun 2012)
  • A.The research is carried out after the incident
  • B.The research is carried out prior to the incident
  • C.The research is carried out along with the happening of an incident.
  • D.The research is carried out keeping in mind the possibilities of an incident.
Correct Answer: The research is carried out after the incident

Ex-post facto research is a type of non-experimental research design where the researcher investigates the possible causes or factors that led to an effect that has already taken place. Unlike experimental research, where the researcher manipulates variables and observes the outcomes, ex-post facto research relies on analyzing data from past events or situations to draw conclusions.

 

In this research approach, the researcher does not have control over the independent variable as it has already occurred naturally, and the study is based on observation and data collection after the fact. This method is often used in social research when it is not feasible or ethical to manipulate variables or conduct controlled experiments.

Question 37
Controlled group condition is applied in (UGC NET Dec 2011)
  • A.Survey Research
  • B.Historical Research
  • C.Experimental Research
  • D.Descriptive Research
Correct Answer: Experimental Research

Experimental research is a scientific approach used to investigate cause-and-effect relationships between variables. In an experimental study, the researcher manipulates one or more independent variables to observe their effects on a dependent variable while controlling other variables that could potentially influence the results. The key feature of experimental research is the use of controlled conditions, which allows researchers to isolate the impact of the independent variable on the dependent variable.

 

To achieve control, the researcher creates experimental and control groups. The experimental group is exposed to the manipulated independent variable, while the control group is not exposed to the variable and serves as a baseline for comparison. By comparing the outcomes between the two groups, researchers can determine whether the independent variable has a significant effect on the dependent variable.

 

Experimental research is often conducted in laboratory settings, where conditions can be carefully regulated and controlled. However, experimental studies can also be conducted in real-world settings, known as field experiments, where researchers still apply controlled group conditions.

In contrast, survey research involves posing questions to people to gather data about their opinions, behaviors, or characteristics. Historical research delves into the past to understand events, behaviors, or conditions in a specific historical context. Ex-post facto research aims to identify possible causes behind an effect that has already occurred, without direct manipulation of variables

Question 38
A doctor studies the relative effectiveness of two drugs of dengue fever. His research would be classified as (UGC NET Dec 2010)
  • A.Descriptive Survey
  • B.Experimental Research

Correct Answer: Experimental Research

Experimental research is a scientific approach to research where the researcher manipulates certain variables (in this case, the drugs being tested) while keeping other variables constant. The goal is to determine cause-and-effect relationships between the variables and to make comparisons between different groups or conditions. In the context of the study on dengue fever drugs, the doctor would administer the two drugs to different groups of patients and then measure their effectiveness in treating the disease.

Action research is a methodological approach where researchers actively participate in a change situation or problem-solving process while simultaneously conducting research. The main objective of action research is to bring about positive changes and improvements in a particular context or organization. It is often initiated to address practical issues and challenges faced by individuals, groups, or communities.

 

There are two main types of action research: participatory and practical. In participatory action research, individuals or communities actively collaborate with researchers to identify and implement solutions to their own problems. In practical action research, larger organizations or institutions undertake research to improve their strategies, practices, and knowledge within their specific environments.

Question 41
The process not needed in Experimental Researches is (UGC NET Dec 2009)
  • A.Observation
  • B.Manipulation
  • C.Controlling
  • D.Content Analysis
Correct Answer: Manipulation

In experimental research, an intervention is deliberately introduced to observe its effects. This intervention often involves the manipulation of variables to study their impact on the outcome. However, in the context of this question, the term "manipulation" does not refer to the manipulation of variables, but rather to "data manipulation" during the statistical analysis of the data collected through experimentation.

 

Data manipulation in this sense refers to actions taken to address issues like outliers, missing data, or non-normality that may affect the validity of the statistical analysis. It is essential to examine the data and address any real problems before conducting the statistical analysis.

While manipulation of variables is indeed a crucial aspect of experimental research, the question specifically refers to data manipulation, which is not needed or desirable in experimental research.

Question 42
If a researcher conducts a research on finding out which administrative style contributes more to institutional effectiveness? This will be an example of (UGC NET Dec 2009)
  • A.Basic Research
  • B.Action Research
  • C.Applied Research
  • D.None of the above
Correct Answer: Applied Research

If a researcher conducts research to find out which administrative style contributes more to institutional effectiveness, this would be an example of Applied Research because it aims to address a practical issue or problem.

 

a. Fundamental research, also known as basic research or pure research, is driven by curiosity and the desire to expand knowledge in a specific research area. It does not usually generate findings that have immediate practical applications.

 

b. Action research is a type of research that is either initiated to solve an immediate problem or undertaken as a reflective process of progressive problem-solving. It involves active participation in a change situation with the aim of improving practices and addressing issues.

 

c. Applied research, on the other hand, involves the application of basic research fundamentals to solve specific practical problems. It focuses on finding solutions to real-world issues and has direct applications in various fields such as business, medicine, and education.

 

In the given scenario, the researcher is seeking to understand which administrative style is more effective for institutional effectiveness.This objective is aligned with applied research, as the findings would have practical implications and could potentially be used to improve administrative practices in institutions.

Question 43
Fundamental research reflects the ability to: (UGC NET Jun 2007)
  • A.Synthesize new ideals
  • B.Expound new principles
  • C.Evaluate the existing material concerning research
  • D.Study the existing literature regarding various topics
Correct Answer: Expound new principles

Fundamental research, also known as pure research or basic research, is driven by the quest to increase understanding of fundamental principles. It is not primarily focused on immediate commercial benefits but is rather born out of curiosity and the pursuit of knowledge. Although fundamental research may not lead to immediate practical applications, it forms the basis for many applied research projects and eventual commercial products.

 

This type of research is typically conducted by universities and academic institutions, and it seeks to make generalizations and explore the underlying reasons behind phenomena. The philosophy of fundamental research is rooted in the pursuit of knowledge for knowledge's sake. It aims to answer fundamental questions such as "why," "what," or "how" about a specific subject or field, contributing to the pool of fundamental knowledge in that research area.

Quiz Attempt #119765

Total Questions: 38
Question 1
When a respondent is aware of being measured then its effect on his behaviour is identified as: (UGC NET 05 Jan Evening 2022)
  • A.Self — consciousness
  • B.Reactivity
  • C.Artificiality
  • D.Identity effect
Correct Answer: Reactivity

Reactivity refers to the phenomenon where individuals modify their behavior or responses when they are aware of being measured or observed. In the context of research, reactivity can occur when respondents alter their natural behavior due to the presence of researchers, awareness of being part of a study, or knowledge that their responses will be recorded or analyzed. This can lead to biased or inaccurate data if participants' responses are influenced by reactivity rather than reflecting their true behavior or attitudes. Researchers often try to minimize reactivity by using unobtrusive observation methods or by ensuring that participants feel comfortable and natural during data collection.

Question 2
A major limitation of the postal questionnaire survey is (UGC NET 14 Mar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Need for supplementary questions
  • B.Availability of extra data
  • C.Need for a covering letter
  • D.Higher rate of non-response
Correct Answer: Higher rate of non-response

In postal questionnaire surveys, researchers send questionnaires to potential participants via mail, and respondents are expected to complete and return them. One significant drawback of this method is that it often results in a higher rate of non-response. Non-response occurs when a substantial number of individuals who receive the questionnaire do not complete and return it. This can lead to incomplete data and potential biases in the survey results.

 

Several factors contribute to the higher rate of non-response in postal questionnaire surveys, including lack of motivation, time constraints, the complexity of the questionnaire, and respondents simply choosing not to participate. Researchers often need to employ various strategies to address non-response, such as follow-up reminders, incentives, or using alternative survey methods.

Question 3
During research, while recording observation if an observer rates an individual based on the rating given in another aspect of the interaction, this is termed as the: (UGC NET 24 June 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Evaluation effect
  • B.Error of central tendency
  • C.Halo effect
  • D.Categorical effect
Correct Answer: Halo effect

The Halo Effect is a cognitive bias that influences the way people make judgments and evaluations. It occurs when a person's overall impression or perception of someone is influenced by their feelings or judgments about specific characteristics or qualities of that person. In other words, if a person has a positive impression of one attribute of an individual, they are likely to extend that positive impression to other unrelated attributes of the same person.

 

For example, if an observer rates a person as being attractive, they may subconsciously assume that the same person is also intelligent, kind, or trustworthy, even though these characteristics have no direct connection to physical attractiveness. Similarly, if a person is perceived as having a negative quality, it may lead the observer to assume negative traits in other areas as well.

 

The Halo Effect can affect various situations, including social interactions, job interviews, and performance evaluations. It can lead to biased judgments and inaccurate assessments of individuals, as the observer's overall impression is skewed by a single characteristic.

 

Researchers and evaluators should be aware of the Halo Effect and take steps to minimize its impact on their assessments. One way to reduce the influence of the Halo Effect is to evaluate specific attributes or behaviors separately, rather than allowing one characteristic to unduly influence overall judgments. By recognizing and mitigating the Halo Effect, researchers can improve the accuracy and fairness of their evaluations.

Question 4
When a set of possible answers to select for a question is given to a respondent, it is called (UGC NET 28 Mar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Open-ended question
  • B.Classical question
  • C.Filtered question
  • D.Fixed choice question
Correct Answer: Fixed choice question

Four main types of questions used in surveys and questionnaires:

 

1.Open-Ended Questions: Open-ended questions are designed to elicit free-form responses from respondents. They do not provide predefined answer options and instead allow respondents to provide detailed, open-ended answers in their own words.

Use: Open-ended questions are valuable when researchers want to gather qualitative data, explore complex issues, or obtain in-depth insights. They are suitable for capturing diverse perspectives and uncovering new information.

Example: "Please describe your experience with our product or service."

 

2. Fixed Choice Questions (Closed-Ended Questions): Fixed choice questions provide respondents with a predefined set of answer options from which they choose the most appropriate response. These questions are structured and quantifiable.

Use: Fixed choice questions are ideal for collecting structured data that can be easily analyzed and summarized. They are commonly used in surveys to obtain specific information.

Examples: Multiple-choice questions ("Which of the following best describes your age group?"), Likert scale questions ("On a scale of 1 to 5, how satisfied are you with our customer service?"), and ranking questions ("Please rank the following factors in order of importance when choosing a product: price, quality, brand reputation, customer reviews").

 

3. Multiple-Response Questions: Multiple-response questions, also known as checkbox questions, allow respondents to select multiple answer options from a list. Unlike multiple-choice questions, they permit respondents to choose more than one answer.

Use: Multiple-response questions are suitable when multiple options may apply to respondents, such as selecting multiple interests or preferences.

Example: "Which of the following social media platforms do you use regularly? (Check all that apply: Facebook, Twitter, Instagram, LinkedIn)."

 

4. Ranking Questions: Ranking questions require respondents to order or rank a list of items or options in terms of preference, importance, or another criterion. Respondents assign a unique rank to each item.

Use: Ranking questions are useful when researchers want to understand the relative priority or preference of different items or when making choices based on a predefined order is relevant.

Example: "Please rank the following factors in order of importance when choosing a restaurant: food quality, price, location, ambiance."

Question 5
Identify the rules that you would follow while designing questions for a questionnaire. (UGC NET 24 Mar 2023 Morning)A. Avoid ambiguous terms in questions.B. Avoid long questions.C. Ask some leading questions.D. Avoid double-barrelled questions.E. Avoid very specific questions.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B and C only
  • B.B, C and D only
  • C.A, B and D only
  • D.B, C and E only
Correct Answer: A, B and D only

When designing questions for a questionnaire, you should follow these rules:

 

a. Avoid ambiguous terms in questions: This is a good rule to follow. Ambiguous terms can lead to confusion and different interpretations among respondents. Clear and unambiguous language is essential for questionnaire questions.

 

b. Avoid long questions: Long questions can be overwhelming and may lead to respondent fatigue or decreased response quality. It's generally a good practice to keep questions concise and to the point.

 

c. Avoid double-barreled questions: This is a valid rule to follow. Double-barreled questions combine two or more issues into a single question, making it difficult to determine which issue the respondent is addressing. Separating these issues into distinct questions is preferable.

Question 6
In a data set any extreme value, either very large or very small, compared to the rest of the data, is said to be: (UGC NET 21 Mar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Exceedance
  • B.Outlier
  • C.Extreme
  • D.Outsider
Correct Answer: Outlier

In a data set, any extreme value, either very large or very small, compared to the rest of the data, is said to be an Outlier. Outliers are data points that significantly differ from the majority of the data and can have a substantial impact on statistical analyses and interpretations.

This approach is often used in quantitative research to collect structured and standardized data from participants.

Question 11
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 14 Oct 2022 Morning)Statement I:While developing a 'consent form' an explanation of the purpose of the study, the reason for the selection of the participants should be explicit.Statement II:However, there is no need to give a description of any potential risks to the participants.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement (I) and Statement (II) are true.
  • B.Both Statement (I) and Statement (II) are false.
  • C.Statement (I) is true but Statement (II) is false.
  • D.Statement (I) is false but Statement (II) is true.
Correct Answer: Statement (I) is true but Statement (II) is false.

Statement I is true. Informed consent is an essential ethical requirement in research involving human participants. The consent form should provide a clear and explicit explanation of the purpose of the study and the reason for selecting specific participants. Participants need to have a clear understanding of what the study is about and why they have been chosen to participate.

 

Statement II is false. It is crucial to include a description of any potential risks or harms that participants may encounter during the study in the consent form. Participants have the right to be informed about any potential risks and make an informed decision about whether or not to participate in the research. Failing to disclose potential risks would be unethical and could lead to harm to the participants. Therefore, it is essential to provide a comprehensive explanation of both the purpose and the risks of the study in the consent form.

Question 12
Which one of the following is a research tool? (UGC NET Dec 2011)
  • A.Graph
  • B.Illustration
  • C.Questionnaire
  • D.Diagram
Correct Answer: Questionnaire

Research tools are instruments or techniques used to collect data for research purposes. They aid researchers in gathering information from participants to analyze and draw conclusions from the study. Questionnaires are one of the primary data-gathering tools used in research.

 

Questionnaires consist of a set of structured questions related to the research topic or objective. These questions can cover a wide range of subjects, such as opinions, attitudes, behaviors, preferences, demographics, and more. Researchers use questionnaires to collect quantitative and qualitative data, depending on the type of questions asked.

 

The questionnaire can be administered in various ways, such as through online surveys, paper-based forms, or face-to-face interviews. It allows researchers to collect data from a large number of respondents efficiently and analyze the responses to draw meaningful insights and conclusions.

 

While graphs, illustrations, and diagrams can be helpful in presenting and visualizing research findings, they are not research tools in themselves. They are used to represent data or information in a visual format and are derived from the data collected using research tools like questionnaires, interviews, or experiments.

Question 13
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 24 Dec Evening 2021)List Ia. Structured interviewb. Emailc. Censusd. Probability sampleList IIi. Embeddedii. Enumeration of an entire populationiii. Face-to-faceiv. Simple random sampleChoose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes

a. Structured interview - iii. Face-to-face

b. Email - i. Embedded

c. Census - ii. Enumeration of an entire population

A census is a method of data collection where information is collected from every individual in the entire population. It aims to gather data from all members of the target population, leaving no one excluded.

 

d. Probability sample - iv. Simple random sample

A probability sample is a type of sampling method where each member of the population has a known and non-zero chance of being selected in the sample. A simple random sample is a specific type of probability sample where every individual in the population has an equal chance of being chosen.

Question 16

  • A.Rating scale
  • B.Interview
  • C.Questionnaire
  • D.Schedule
Correct Answer: Questionnaire

Question 17
The easiest attitudinal scale which is a summated rating scale is the: (UGC NET 25 June 2020 Morning paper)
  • A.Guttman Scale
  • B.Likert Scale
  • C.Thurstone Scale
  • D.MLA Scale
Correct Answer: Likert Scale

Likert Scale is designed to measure people’s attitudes, opinions, or perceptions. Subjects choose from a range of possible responses to a specific question or statement; responses typically include “strongly agree,” “agree,” “neutral,” “disagree,” and “strongly disagree.” Often, the categories of response are coded numerically, in which case the numerical values must be defined for that specific study, such as 1 = strongly agree, 2 = agree, and so on. The Likert scale is named for American social scientist Rensis Likert, who devised the approach in 1932. This scale is also known as rating scale.

 

A Thurstone scale has a number of “agree” or “disagree” statements. It is a unidimensional scale to measure attitudes towards people. Developing the scale is time consuming and relatively complex compared to other scales.

 

A Guttman scale (also known as cumulative scaling or scalogram analysis) is an ordinal scale type where statements are arranged in a hierarchical order so that someone who agrees with one item will also agree with lower-order, easier, less extreme items.

Question 18
Mailed questionnaire, observation, interview and collective questionnaire are instances of: (UGC NET 24 June 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Secondary sources
  • B.Personal sources
  • C.Primary sources
  • D.Tertiary sources
Correct Answer: Primary sources

Sources of information or evidence are often categorized as primary, secondary, or tertiary material. These classifications are based on the originality of the material and the proximity of the source or origin. This tells us whether the author is reporting information that is first hand or is conveying the experiences and opinions of others which is considered second hand. All these sources are explained below:

 

Primary Sources: These sources are records of events or evidence as they are first described or actually happened without any interpretation or commentary. It is information that is shown for the first time or original materials on which other research is based.  Primary sources display original thinking, report on new discoveries, or share fresh information.

 

Examples of primary sources:

Theses, dissertations, scholarly journal articles (research based), some government reports, symposia and conference proceedings, original artwork, poems, photographs, speeches, letters, memos, personal narratives, diaries, interviews, autobiographies, observation, correspondence, newspaper articles and mailed questionnaires.

 

Secondary Sources: These sources offer an analysis or restatement of primary sources. They often try to describe or explain primary sources. They tend to be works which summarize, interpret, reorganize, or otherwise provide an added value to a primary source.

 

Examples of Secondary Sources:

Textbooks, edited works, books and articles that interpret or review research works, histories, biographies, literary criticism and interpretation, reviews of law and legislation, political analyses and commentaries.

 

Tertiary Sources: These are sources that index, abstract, organize, compile, or digest other sources (both primary and secondary). Some reference materials and textbooks are considered tertiary sources when their chief purpose is to list, summarize or simply repackage ideas or other information. Tertiary sources are usually not credited to a particular author.

 

Examples of Tertiary Sources:

Dictionaries/encyclopedias (may also be secondary), almanacs, fact books, Wikipedia, bibliographies (may also be secondary), directories, guidebooks, manuals, handbooks, and textbooks (may be secondary), indexing and abstracting sources.

Question 19
Tertiary source of data is: (UGC NET 20 June 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Films, hoardings and posters.
  • B.Government gazette, newspapers and magazines.
  • C.Information derived from both primary and secondary sources.
  • D.Data collected from policy papers.
Correct Answer: Information derived from both primary and secondary sources.

Sources of information or evidence are often categorized as primary, secondary, or tertiary material. These classifications are based on the originality of the material and the proximity of the source or origin. This tells us whether the author is reporting information that is first hand or is conveying the experiences and opinions of others which is considered second hand. All these sources are explained below:

 

Primary Sources: These sources are records of events or evidence as they are first described or actually happened without any interpretation or commentary. It is information that is shown for the first time or original materials on which other research is based. Primary sources display original thinking, report on new discoveries, or share fresh information.

Examples of primary sources:

Theses, dissertations, scholarly journal articles (research based), some government reports, symposia and conference proceedings, original artwork, poems, photographs, speeches, letters, memos, personal narratives, diaries, interviews, autobiographies, correspondence and newspaper articles.

 

Secondary Sources: These sources offer an analysis or restatement of primary sources. They often try to describe or explain primary sources. They tend to be works which summarize, interpret, reorganize, or otherwise provide an added value to a primary source.

Examples of Secondary Sources:

Textbooks, edited works, books and articles that interpret or review research works, histories, biographies, literary criticism and interpretation, reviews of law and legislation, political analyses and commentaries.

 

Tertiary Sources: These are sources that index, abstract, organize, compile, or digest other sources (both primary and secondary). Some reference materials and textbooks are considered tertiary sources when their chief purpose is to list, summarize or simply repackage ideas or other information. Tertiary sources are usually not credited to a particular author.

Examples of Tertiary Sources:

Dictionaries/encyclopedias (may also be secondary), almanacs, fact books, Wikipedia, bibliographies (may also be secondary), directories, guidebooks, manuals, handbooks, and textbooks (may be secondary), indexing and abstracting sources.

Question 20
Match List I with List II: (UGC NET 09 July 2022 Evening)List I (Data collection method)a. Field observationb. Focus groupc. Intensive interviewingd. Case studyList II(Characteristics)i. Collects information from many data sources.ii. Gathers detailed information from a small non-random sample.iii. Gathers preliminary information for a research project.iv. Studies a phenomenon in natural settings.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a- i, b- iii, c- ii, d- iv
  • B.a- ii, b- iv, c- iii, d- i
  • C.a- iii, b- iv, c- i, d- ii
  • D.a- iv, b- iii, c- ii, d- i
Correct Answer: a- iv, b- iii, c- ii, d- i

The correct match between List I (Data collection method) and List II (Characteristics) is:

 

a. Field observation: This method involves gathering data by directly observing and studying a phenomenon in its natural setting or environment. Researchers carefully observe and record events, behaviors, and interactions without directly intervening or influencing the subjects. Field observation is particularly useful when studying complex social behaviors, cultural practices, or natural occurrences.

 

b. Focus group: Focus groups are a qualitative data collection method that involves bringing together a small group of individuals to discuss a specific topic or issue. The participants are encouraged to share their thoughts, opinions, and experiences openly. The focus group setting allows researchers to explore different perspectives, uncover underlying beliefs, and gain valuable insights into the subject under investigation.

 

c. Intensive interviewing: This method involves conducting in-depth interviews with a small number of carefully selected participants. These interviews are structured and allow for open-ended questions, enabling participants to provide detailed and rich responses. Intensive interviewing is particularly suitable for gaining a deep understanding of individual experiences, beliefs, attitudes, and motivations.

 

d. Case study: Case study research focuses on the detailed examination of a specific individual, group, organization, or event. Researchers collect information from multiple data sources, such as interviews, observations, documents, and archival records, to gain a comprehensive understanding of the case under study. Case studies are valuable for exploring complex phenomena within their real-life context and can provide rich and contextualized data.

Question 23

b. Questions can be grouped, if the list of questions is long: This is a useful tip. Grouping similar questions together can make the interview more organized and easier for both the interviewer and the interviewee.

Question 24
The advantages of structured interview are: (UGC NET 04 Dec Evening)a. Provides limited choices that reduce the possibility of generalization.b. Standardises questions.c. Accuracy is possible to a large extent.d. Data processing is easy.e. Misinterpretation is possible due to strict standardisation.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.) a, b, c only
  • B.b, c, d only
  • C.c, d, e only
  • D.a, d, e only
Correct Answer: b, c, d only

The advantages of structured interviews are:

 

a. Standardizes questions: This statement is correct. One of the main advantages of structured interviews is that the questions are standardized, meaning that all participants are asked the same set of questions in the same way, which ensures consistency and comparability.

 

b. Accuracy is possible to a large extent: This statement is correct. Structured interviews allow for precise and accurate data collection since the questions are carefully designed and asked in a standardized manner.

 

c. Data processing is easy: This statement is correct. Structured interviews generate data that are easier to process and analyze because the responses are usually in a closed-ended format and can be easily coded for analysis.

Question 25
The advantages of secondary analysis in research are: (UGC NET 21 Dec 2018 Morning)(a) It is inexpensive.(b) There is no need to construct a measuring instrument.(c) Data archives are a valuable source.(d) Useful opportunity is provided to produce valuable knowledge.(e) Provides less time to understand data
  • A.(a), (b), (c) and (d)
  • B.(a), (c), (d) and (e)
  • C.(b), (c) and (e)
  • D.(d) and (e) only
Correct Answer: (a), (b), (c) and (d)

Secondary analysis refers to the process of using existing data that was collected for a different purpose or research project to answer new research questions or explore alternative perspectives. The advantages of using secondary analysis in research are as follows:

 

(a) Cost-Effectiveness: Conducting new primary data collection can be expensive and time-consuming. Secondary analysis allows researchers to utilize data that has already been collected, saving both time and resources.

 

(b) No Need for Constructing a Measuring Instrument: In primary research, researchers need to design and construct their measuring instruments, such as surveys or questionnaires. When using secondary data, this step is not necessary since the data already exist.

 

(c) Valuable Data Archives: Various organizations, government agencies, and research institutions maintain data archives containing valuable information collected over time. Researchers can access these archives to find relevant data for their research.

 

(d) Producing Valuable Knowledge: By reusing existing data for new research questions, researchers can add to the body of knowledge without duplicating efforts. Secondary analysis allows researchers to explore different aspects of the data, leading to valuable insights and discoveries.

Question 26
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 01 Dec Morning 2021)Statement I:Experimenter effects are errors introduced during the collection or analysis of experimental data due to the behaviour of the experimenter.Statement II:Due to the presence of certain cues in the experimental setting, the participants form an interpretation of the experiment's purpose and subconsciously change their behaviour to fit that interpretation.In light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect.
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.

Statement I is about experimenter effects, which refer to the unintended influence that the experimenter may have on the participants and the experimental results. This can happen due to various factors, such as the experimenter's behavior, expectations, or unintentional cues given to the participants.

 

Statement II is related to demand characteristics, which are cues or hints present in the experimental setting that lead participants to form an interpretation of the study's purpose. As a result, participants may change their behavior in response to these cues, affecting the validity of the experiment.

Question 27
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET09 July 2022 Evening)Statement I:Developing research questions means narrowing down and focusing directly on what you want to know.Statement II:A research question does not prompt a researcher to do literature survey.In the light of the above statements. choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Statement I is true but Statement II is false.

Statement I: Developing research questions involves the process of refining and narrowing down the focus of the study to clearly articulate what the researcher wants to investigate. Research questions play a crucial role in guiding the research process and providing a clear direction for the study.

 

Statement II: Research questions are formulated based on existing knowledge and literature on the topic. Before developing research questions, researchers typically conduct a literature survey or review to understand what has already been studied and what gaps exist in the current knowledge. This helps in formulating relevant and meaningful research questions that contribute to the existing body of knowledge. Therefore, research questions are often informed by the literature survey rather than being independent of it.

Question 28
Responses to open-ended questions are: (UGC NET08 Oct 2022 Morning)
  • A.Quantifiable
  • B.Realistic
  • C.Subjective
  • D.Imitative
Correct Answer: Subjective

Responses to open-ended questions are subjective because they allow respondents to provide detailed and personalized answers based on their own thoughts, opinions, and experiences. These responses are not pre-defined or constrained by fixed options, unlike closed-ended questions where respondents choose from a set of provided response choices. Open-ended questions offer more in-depth insights into the respondents' perspectives and allow for a richer understanding of their viewpoints. However, analyzing and interpreting open-ended responses can be more challenging compared to quantifying closed-ended responses.

Question 29
Given below are two statements, one is labelled as Assertion A and the other is labelled as Reason R: (UGC NET 25 Nov Morning 2021)Assertion ‘A’:A research question should have some connection with an existing theory or research.Reason ‘R’:The research question formulated should be either too broad or too narrow.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A.
  • B.Both A and R are true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A.
  • C.A is true but R is false.
  • D.A is false but R is true.
Correct Answer: A is true but R is false.

Assertion A is true because a research question should indeed have some connection with an existing theory or previous research. Formulating research questions that build on existing knowledge helps to contribute to the advancement of the field and ensures that the research is relevant and meaningful.

 

However, Reason R is not true. The research question should neither be too broad nor too narrow. Instead, it should be focused and specific enough to guide the research but not overly restrictive. A research question that is too broad may be difficult to address adequately within the scope of the study, while a question that is too narrow may limit the exploration of the topic. The ideal research question strikes a balance between being focused and comprehensive enough to allow for meaningful investigation and analysis.

Question 30
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET12 July 2022 Evening)Statement I:The research questions should be linked to each other.Statement II:The research questions should be either broad or narrow.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Statement I is true but Statement II is false.

Statement I is true because research questions should be linked to each other in a coherent and logical manner. A well-structured research project typically has a hierarchy of research questions, where broader questions lead to more specific ones, and each question contributes to addressing the overall research objective.

 

However, Statement II is false. Research questions should not be either broad or narrow. Instead, they should strike a balance between being focused enough to guide the research and broad enough to allow for meaningful investigation. Overly broad research questions may lack clarity and may be difficult to address comprehensively, while overly narrow questions may limit the scope of the study and miss important aspects of the topic. The ideal research question is specific and focused but not overly restrictive.

Question 31
Debriefing involves several activities following the collection of data: (UGC NET 29 Nov Evening)1. Explanation of any deception.2. Explaining the superiority of the present research.3. Description of the purpose of the study.4. Post‐study follow‐up medical or psychological attention.5. Publication of the finding of the research in a journal.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:

  • C.2,3,4 only

Debriefing involves several activities following the collection of data in research studies involving human participants. These activities are aimed at providing necessary information and support to the participants and ensuring their well-being. The correct activities are:

2. Description of the purpose of the study: Participants should be informed about the overall purpose and objectives of the study so that they understand the context of their involvement.

3. Post‐study follow‐up medical or psychological attention: If the research involves any potentially distressing or harmful procedures, participants should be provided with appropriate follow-up support, such as access to medical or psychological attention if needed.

Question 33
Which of the following sources of data is not based on primary data collection? (UGC NET Dec 2009)
  • A.Census of India
  • B.National Sample Survey
  • C.Statistical Abstracts of India
  • D.National Family Health Survey
Correct Answer: Statistical Abstracts of India

Primary Data Collection involves the process of gathering original data directly from the source for a specific research purpose. This data is collected through field surveys, interviews, observations, or experiments.

 

On the other hand, Secondary Data Collection involves using existing data that has been collected by someone else for a different purpose. It includes data from published sources, government reports, research papers, and other publicly available data.

 

In the context of the question, the Census of India, National Sample Survey, and National Family Health Survey all involve primary data collection methods. These surveys and census involve sending volunteers and employees to visit households, conduct interviews, and collect data directly from the respondents.

 

However, "Statistical Abstracts of India" is a publication that compiles and presents data from various sources, including primary data collected by different agencies and departments. It is a secondary data source that provides a comprehensive overview of statistical data from multiple sources but does not involve the direct collection of data from the field.

Question 34
If data has been recorded using technical media, which among the following is a necessary step on the way to its interpretation? (UGC NET 06 Dec 2019 Evening Paper)
  • A.Transcription
  • B.Structural Equation Modelling
  • C.Sequential Analysis

Data transcription is the process of converting speech or recorded information into written or electronic text documents. This step is essential when data has been captured through audio or video recordings. Transcription services are commonly used in various fields, such as business, legal, and medical, to convert spoken content into text format for further analysis and interpretation.

Question 35
Which of the following steps are required to design a questionnaire? (UGC NET Jun 2015)(a) Writing primary and secondary aims of the study.(b) Review of the current literature.(c) Prepare a draft of questionnaire.(d) Revision of the draft.Select the correct answer from the codes given below:
  • A.(a), (b) and (c)
  • B.(a), (c) and (d)
  • C.(b), (c) and (d)
  • D.(a), (b), (c) and (d)
Correct Answer: (a), (b), (c) and (d)

To design a questionnaire, the following steps are required:

 

a. Writing primary and secondary aims of the study: This step involves defining the main objectives and goals of the research. It helps in clarifying what information the questionnaire should gather to achieve those aims.

 

b. Review of the current literature: Conducting a literature review is essential to understand the existing knowledge and research related to the study topic. This step helps in identifying gaps in the current understanding and shaping the questionnaire accordingly.

 

c. Prepare a draft of the questionnaire: Based on the study objectives and literature review, a preliminary version of the questionnaire is created. This draft includes all the questions and items necessary to collect the required data.

 

d. Revision of the draft: The draft questionnaire is thoroughly reviewed and revised to ensure clarity, accuracy, and relevance. This step involves refining the wording of questions, checking for any potential biases, and making improvements based on feedback from experts or pilot testing.

Question 36
A questionnaire that offers no scope for any respondent’s own view is called: (UGC NET 25 June 2020 Evening paper)
  • A.closed-ended
  • B.schedule
  • C.open-ended
  • D.unstructured
Correct Answer: closed-ended

Closed-ended questions are designed in such a way that respondents are provided with predefined response options and are not given the opportunity to provide their own inputs or elaborate on their answers. These questions often require respondents to choose from options such as "Yes," "No," "Agree," "Disagree," or select a response from a list of multiple-choice options. The closed-ended format is commonly used to collect quantitative data as it allows for straightforward analysis and easy comparison of responses.

 

On the other hand, an open-ended questionnaire includes questions that do not limit respondents to specific choices. Instead, respondents are encouraged to provide detailed and free-text responses, expressing their thoughts and opinions in their own words. Open-ended questions allow for more in-depth insights and qualitative data, as respondents can elaborate on their perspectives.

 

A schedule, on the other hand, refers to a set of questions that are administered in person by an interviewer or observer. The questions remain consistent in wording and order, and while the interviewer may clarify any confusion, the respondent is still expected to choose from predetermined response options.

Question 37
A shift in attitude in respondents between two points during data collection is called: (UGC NET 26 June 2019 Morning Paper)
  • A.Reactive effect
  • B.Maturation effect
  • C.Regression effect
  • D.Conditioning effect
Correct Answer: Regression effect

The regression effect is a statistical phenomenon where extreme values on a variable tend to move closer to the mean when the variable is measured again at a later point in time. This effect occurs even without any intervention or treatment being applied. When a group of subjects with low values on a particular measurement is retested, their mean value is likely to increase, and similarly, when a group with high values is retested, their mean value is likely to decrease. This regression effect can be observed in various research contexts.

 

However, the misinterpretation of the regression effect can lead to what is known as the "regression fallacy." This fallacy occurs when the increase or decrease in values is incorrectly attributed to an intervention or treatment, when in fact, it is merely a result of the regression effect. Researchers and decision-makers need to be cautious and aware of this phenomenon to avoid drawing inaccurate conclusions from their data.

Question 38
From the list given below identify those questions which are called process rather than content- based questions? (UGC NET 26 June 2019 Morning Paper)(i) Convergent questions(ii) Divergent questions(iii) Fact based questions(iv) Concept based questions(v) Open questions(vi) Closed questionsChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.(i), (ii) and (iii)
  • B.(ii), (iii) and (iv)
  • C.(iv), (v) and (vi)
  • D.(ii), (iv) and (v)
Correct Answer: (ii), (iv) and (v)

Process-based questions focus on encouraging higher-order thinking, reasoning, and critical analysis skills in students. They require students to explore and generate multiple possibilities, solutions, or perspectives. On the other hand, content-based questions concentrate on factual information and often have a definitive answer.

Question 1
The approach of accepting knowledge because people have agreed upon, following a reasonable argument is known as (UGC NET 06thMar 2023 Morning)
  • A.Authoritarian
  • B.A -priori
  • C.Scientific
  • D.Experiential
Correct Answer: A -priori

A-priori knowledge is knowledge that is derived from reason and logical deduction rather than empirical observation or experience. It is often based on prior assumptions, principles, or arguments that are accepted as true or self-evident. This form of knowledge does not rely on direct sensory experience or experimentation, as in the case of empirical or experiential knowledge.

Question 5
Symbolic interactionism is a (UGC NET 06thMar 2023 Evening)
  • A.Theory
  • B.Hypothesis
  • C.Research question
  • D.Review
Correct Answer: Theory

Question 6
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET 05thMar 2023 Morning)Statement I:For open-ended questions, respondents can produce their own answers without any restriction of length.Statement II:The memory phenomenon of telescoping is not an issue in survey research.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:

  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect
  • C.Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.
  • D.Statement I is incorrect but Statement II is correct.
Correct Answer: Statement I is correct but Statement II is incorrect.

Statement I: This statement is correct. Open-ended questions in surveys allow respondents to provide their own answers in their own words, without predefined options or restrictions on the length of their responses.

 

Statement II: This statement is incorrect. Telescoping is a memory phenomenon in which respondents in a survey may inaccurately recall events as occurring more recently than they actually did. It can be an issue in survey research, especially when asking respondents to recall specific events or timelines.

Question 7

  • C.Content analysis
  • D.Narrative analysis
